Ambiguity in Manumitting One of Two Slaves: Ta'liq vs. Tanjiz
Dispute on modality and rulings of ambiguous manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on ambiguous manumission (ta'liq vs. tanjiz) and apply the rulings on employment and injuries to determine which view each supports.

Core Idea
When a master says 'one of you is free', the freedom is either suspended on choice (Abu Yusuf) or immediate in an unspecified slave (Muhammad).

The seemingly simple statement 'one of you is free' conceals a deep intra-Hanafi disagreement. Does it create any legal effect immediately, or does it only become operative after the master specifies which slave is intended? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lays out the two positions and tests them by examining practical scenarios—employment, injuries, and homicide—showing that each view has consistent implications. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how a legal principle (ta'liq vs. tanjiz) governs a chain of specific rulings.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish original from incidental ambiguity
Note that the text first separates 'original' ambiguity (from the start) from 'incidental' (arising later). The dispute concerns only the original type: a master says 'one of you is free' without naming either slave.
Original ambiguity is the focus; incidental ambiguity is not discussed here.
2
State the two positions and their evidence
Abu Yusuf (and reportedly Abu Hanifa) holds that the manumission is suspended (ta'liq) upon specification—no freedom occurs until the master chooses. Muhammad holds that the manumission is immediate (tanjiz) in an unspecified slave, and the choice merely clarifies which slave was already free. The evidence includes analogies to divorce and sale with option.
The text provides divorce examples and narrations from the Imams.
3
Examine the rulings on employment and injuries
The passage lists several practical rulings: the master may employ and profit from both slaves before choice (supports ta'liq); if the master cuts their hands, no liability (supports ta'liq); if he kills both with one blow, half diya of each is due to their heirs (supports tanjiz); if an outsider cuts their hands, slave compensation to master (supports ta'liq); if an outsider kills both together, half value to master and half diya to heirs (supports tanjiz).
These rulings show that each view is internally consistent.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if suspended, the master retains full control until specification; if immediate, the slaves are partially free from the outset, limiting the master's rights and affecting compensation for injuries.
The text does not give a final tarjih; both positions are applied in different contexts.

واختيار العتق في أحدهما بيان ونسب هذا القول لمحمد. ولم يكن منصوصاً عليه من أصحابنا لكنه مدلول عليه ومشار إليه ؛ أما الدلالة فلأنه ظهر الاختلاف بين أبي يوسف ومحمد في الطلاق فيمن قال لامرأتيه أحداكما طالق أن العدة تعتبر من وقت الاختيار في قول أبي يوسف والعدة إنما تجب من وقت وقوع الطلاق، فدل أن الطلاق لم يكن واقعاً. وفي قول محمد يعتبر من وقت الكلام السابق وهو يدل على أن الطلاق قد وقع من حين وجوده. وأما الإشارة فإنه روي عن أبي يوسف أنه قال : إذا أعتق أحد عبديه تعلق العتق بذمته ويقال له أعتق. وفيه إشارة إلى أنه غير نازل في المحل. ومعنى قوله «أعتق» اختر العتق لإجماعنا أنه لا يكلف بإنشاء العتق . وذكر محمد في الزيادات يقال له بين؛ وفيه إشارة إلى الوقوع في غير المعين. ثم القائلون بالبيان اختلفوا في كيفية البيان فمنهم قال إنه إظهار محض، وقيل إظهار من وجه إنشاء من وجه هذا غير سديد، لأن القول الواحد لا يكون إظهاراً وإنشاء. وأما الأحكام فنقول إن للمولى أن يستخدمهما ويستغلهما قبل الاختيار، وهذا يدل على أنه غير واقع ولو جنى عليهما قبل الاختيار فلا يخلو إما إن كانت من المولى أو من الأجنبي، وكل لا يخلو إما أن يكون على النفس أو على ما دون النفس، فإن كانت من المولى على ما دون النفس بأن قطع يدهما فلا شيء عليه وهو يدل على عدم نزول العتق، وسواء قطعهما معاً أو على التعاقب وإن كان على النفس بأن قتلهما؛ فإن كان على التعاقب فالأول عبد والثاني فتلزمه دية الثاني وتكون لورثته ولا يرث المولى منها شيئاً، وإن قتلهما معاً بضربة واحدة فعليه نصف دية كل واحد منهما وهذا يؤيد القول بنزول العتق في غير المعين. وإن كانت من أجنبي فيما دون النفس بأن قطع إنسان يدهما فعليه أرش العبيد للمولى وهو نصف قيمة كل واحد منهما، قطعهما معاً أو على التعاقب، وهو يدل على عدم نزوله. وإن كانت في النفس فلا يخلو إما أن يكون القاتل واحداً أو اثنين، فإن كان واحداً فإن قتلهما معاً فعلى القاتل نصف قيمة كل واحد منهما وتكون للمولى وعليه نصف دية كل واحد منهما لورثتهما، وهذا يدل على أن العتق نازل في غير العين، وإن قتلهما على التعاقب يجب على القاتل قيمة الأول للمولى ودية الثاني للورثة. ثم قال: وأما الحكم بعد موت المولى فسيأتي. قوله : (وأما الأحكام معطوف على قوله أما كيفيته وهذا هو الموضع الثاني. وقد جعله البدائع نوعين واقع لأنه لا سبيل إلى استخدام الحر من غير رضاه. وقوله ويستغلهما» أي يستكسبهما وتكون الغلة والكسب للمولى. قال في البدائع : وهذا أيضاً يدل على ما
Then know that the ambiguity of the manumitter is either original or incidental. If original, meaning the wording from the beginning is attributed to one of the mentioned but unspecified, then the competing person is either capable of being manumitted, i.e., such that his manumission is effective, like saying to his two slaves 'one of you is free'. The discussion on this is in two places: first, the modality of this disposition; second, its rulings. As for its modality, it is said that the manumission is suspended on specification and does not take effect before choice, except that here the condition enters upon the ruling, not the cause, like tadbir and sale with option, unlike suspension with other conditions. This is attributed to Abu Yusuf, and it is also said it is the statement of Abu Hanifa. Some said: it is immediate manumission in the unspecified for the present, and choosing manumission in one of them is specification. This is attributed to Muhammad. It is not explicitly narrated from our scholars, but it is indicated and alluded to. As for the indication: the difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad appeared in divorce, regarding one who says to his two wives 'one of you is divorced' - that the waiting period is reckoned from the time of choice according to Abu Yusuf, whereas the waiting period is only obligatory from the time of divorce occurrence, indicating that the divorce had not occurred. According to Muhammad, it is reckoned from the earlier statement, indicating that the divorce occurred from its existence. As for the allusion: it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he said: if a man manumits one of his two slaves, the manumission attaches to his liability and he is told 'manumit'. There is indication that it does not descend upon the slave. The meaning of 'manumit' is 'choose manumission', because it is agreed (ijma) that he is not obliged to initiate manumission. Muhammad said in al-Ziyadat: 'He is told: specify.' There is indication of occurrence in the unspecified. Then those who say it is by specification differed about the modality of specification: some said it is pure disclosure; some said disclosure in one respect and initiation in another - this is unsound because a single statement cannot be both disclosure and initiation. As for the rulings: we say that the master may employ them and profit from them before choice - this indicates it has not occurred. If he commits an offense against them before choice, it is either from the master or an outsider; each is either upon life or less than life. If from the master upon less than life, e.g., he cuts their hand, there is no liability - indicating the non-descent of manumission, whether he cuts them together or successively. If upon life, e.g., he kills them: if successively, the first is a slave, the second - the blood-money (diya) of the second is due and goes to his heirs; the master does not inherit any of it. If he kills both with one blow, half of the diya of each is due, supporting the view of descent in the unspecified (ghayr al-mu'ayyan). If from an outsider upon less than life, e.g., a person cuts their hand, he pays the 'arsh (damages) of slaves to the master, which is half the value of each, whether cut together or successively - indicating non-descent. If upon life: whether the killer is one or two. If one kills both together, the killer owes half the value of each to the master and half the diya of each to their heirs - indicating that the manumission has descended in the unspecified. If killed successively, the killer owes the value of the first to the master and the diya of the second to the heirs. Then he said: As for the ruling after the master's death, it will come. His statement: 'As for the rulings' is a conjunct to his statement 'As for the modality' - this is the second place. Al-Bada'i' divided it into two types: what pertains during the master's life and what pertains after his death. Then he said: 'As for the first, we say: the master...' The author should have done likewise because he will later say 'As for the ruling after the master's death'. His statement: 'This indicates it has not occurred because there is no way to employ a free person without his consent.' His statement: 'and profits from them' i.e., he may earn from them, and the produce and earning go to the master. Al-Bada'i' said: This also indicates what.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into the issue of original ambiguity in manumission, where a master says to his two slaves 'one of you is free'. The text first distinguishes between two types of ambiguity: original (from the start) and incidental. It then presents two key positions: (1) Abu Yusuf's view that the manumission is suspended (mu'allaq) upon specification, meaning no freedom actually occurs until the master chooses which slave is free, but the condition is on the ruling (hukm) not the cause (sabab), similar to a sale with option. (2) Muhammad's view that manumission is immediate (tanjiz) in an unspecified slave, and choosing one is merely a specification (bayan) of which slave already became free. The text provides evidence from divorce cases and narrations from the Imams. It then extensively discusses the legal effects during the master's lifetime, such as the master's right to employ the slaves, and the consequences of injuries or killing by the master or an outsider. These effects are used to infer which position is stronger, as they show whether the slaves are considered free or not before choice. The author notes that al-Bada'i' divided the discussion into two parts: during life and after death, with the latter to be addressed separately.

Key Terms
جهالة المعتق (jahalat al-mu'tiq): Ambiguity in the manumitter's statement, specifically when the identity of the freed slave is not specified.
بيان (bayan): Specification; the act of choosing which slave is intended, which according to some completes the manumission.
تنجيز (tanjiz): Immediate effect; the manumission is deemed to have occurred at the moment of utterance, with the slave freed in an unspecified sense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, what is the nature of the manumission when a master says to his two slaves 'one of you is free'?
A) The manumission is suspended until the master specifies.
B) The manumission is immediate but not effective until the master chooses.
C) The manumission is immediate in an unspecified slave, and specification is merely confirmatory.
D) The manumission is void until the master says the name.

Key Takeaway
The ambiguous expression 'one of you is free' generates immediate legal effects even before specification, but the nature differs between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, affecting the master's rights and liabilities.

Nature of Ambiguous Emancipation: Ta'jiz vs Ta'liq
Intra-Hanafi dispute analysis with rational evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on ambiguous emancipation and apply the divorce analogy (qiyas ala al-talaq) to distinguish between ta'liq and ta'jiz.

Core Idea
When a master says 'one of my slaves is free,' it is suspended until choice (Abu Yusuf), not immediate (Muhammad).

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks a classical intra-Hanafi dispute: is the declaration 'one of my two slaves is free’ an immediate emancipation (ta'jiz) of an unspecified slave, or a suspended emancipation (ta'liq) requiring the master's choice to take effect? The answer determines when freedom becomes actual and what rights the master retains in the interim. By studying the evidence from the divorce parallel and the practical rulings, you will gain precision in analyzing ambiguous legal declarations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Note that Abu Yusuf (and reportedly Abu Hanifa) hold the statement is ta'liq, while Muhammad holds it is ta'jiz. The passage explicitly attributes these views.
Muhammad's view is described as 'indicated' rather than explicitly transmitted from him.
2
Extract the divorce analogy evidence
The author cites the parallel case of a man saying to his two wives 'One of you is divorced.' Abu Yusuf computes the waiting period from the moment of choice, proving divorce is not immediate; Muhammad computes from the utterance, proving immediate effect.
This analogy (qiyas) is the primary rational evidence for the dispute.
3
Analyze the concept of bayān (declaration)
For Muhammad, the subsequent choice is a pure bayān – it merely discloses which slave was already freed at the moment of utterance. For Abu Yusuf, the choice itself creates the emancipation.
The passage criticizes the intermediate view that bayān is partly creation and partly disclosure.
4
Examine the practical ruling before choice
Both positions agree that the master may employ both slaves and take their earnings before choice. This practical consequence supports the ta'liq view, as a free person cannot be employed without consent.
This ruling is cited as evidence that emancipation is not yet actual.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The passage indicates that the majority view (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa) is the relied-upon position, as it aligns with the practical implications and is supported by the divorce analogy.
Al-Marghinani and later Hanafi authorities prefer the ta'liq view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العتق باب العبد يعتق بعضه
من الشروط، ونسب هذا القول إلى أبي يوسف. ويقال إنه قول أبي حنيفة أيضاً. وقال بعضهم : هو تنجيز العتق في غير المعين للحال واختيار العتق في أحدهما بيان ونسب هذا القول لمحمد. ولم يكن منصوصاً عليه من أصحابنا لكنه مدلول عليه ومشار إليه ؛ أما الدلالة فلأنه ظهر الاختلاف بين أبي يوسف ومحمد في الطلاق فيمن قال لامرأتيه أحداكما طالق أن العدة تعتبر من وقت الاختيار في قول أبي يوسف والعدة إنما تجب من وقت وقوع الطلاق، فدل أن الطلاق لم يكن واقعاً. وفي قول محمد يعتبر من وقت الكلام السابق وهو يدل على أن الطلاق قد وقع من حين وجوده. وأما الإشارة فإنه روي عن أبي يوسف أنه قال : إذا أعتق أحد عبديه تعلق العتق بذمته ويقال له أعتق. وفيه إشارة إلى أنه غير نازل في المحل. ومعنى قوله «أعتق» اختر العتق لإجماعنا أنه لا يكلف بإنشاء العتق . وذكر محمد في الزيادات يقال له بين؛ وفيه إشارة إلى الوقوع في غير المعين. ثم القائلون بالبيان اختلفوا في كيفية البيان فمنهم قال إنه إظهار محض، وقيل إظهار من وجه إنشاء من وجه هذا غير سديد، لأن القول الواحد لا يكون إظهاراً وإنشاء. وأما الأحكام فنقول إن للمولى أن يستخدمهما ويستغلهما قبل الاختيار، وهذا يدل على أنه غير واقع.

في
قوله : (وأما الأحكام معطوف على قوله أما كيفيته وهذا هو الموضع الثاني. وقد جعله البدائع نوعين : نوع يتعلق به في حال حياة المولى ونوع يتعلق به بعد وفاته ثم قال: أما الأول
فنقول للمولى الخ. وكان ينبغي للمؤلف أن يفعل كذلك لأنه سيأتي يقول، وأما الحكم بعد موت المولى قوله : (وهذا يدل على أنه غير واقع لأنه لا سبيل إلى استخدام الحر من غير رضاه. وقوله ويستغلهما» أي يستكسبهما وتكون الغلة والكسب للمولى. قال في البدائع : وهذا أيضاً يدل على ما
Book of Emancipation, Chapter on the Slave Who Is Partially Emancipated. Among the conditions, and this statement is attributed to Abu Yusuf. It is said that it is also the statement of Abu Hanifa. Some said: It is immediate emancipation in an unspecified [slave] currently, and the choice of emancipation in one of them is a declaration (bayan). This statement is attributed to Muhammad. It was not explicitly stated by our companions, but it is indicated and referred to. As for the indication, it is because the difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad appeared in divorce regarding someone who said to his two wives 'One of you is divorced' that the waiting period is calculated from the time of choice according to Abu Yusuf, and the waiting period is only required from the time of divorce occurrence, so it indicates that the divorce had not occurred. According to Muhammad, it is calculated from the time of the earlier speech, indicating that the divorce had occurred from its existence. As for the allusion, it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he said: When he emancipates one of his two slaves, emancipation attaches to his liability and he is told 'Emancipate.' There is an allusion that it does not descend upon the actual person. The meaning of his saying 'Emancipate' is 'choose emancipation' because of our consensus that he is not obligated to initiate emancipation. Muhammad mentioned in al-Ziyadat that he is told 'Declare'; and in that is an allusion to occurrence in the unspecified. Then those who say it is a declaration differed concerning the modality of the declaration: some said it is pure disclosure, and some said it is disclosure from one aspect and creation from another. This is unsound because a single statement cannot be both disclosure and creation. As for the rulings, we say: The master may employ them and benefit from them before the choice, and this indicates that it is not actual. Comment by the author: His saying 'As for the rulings' is conjoined to his saying 'As for its modality,' and this is the second topic. Al-Bada'i' has made it two types: a type pertaining to during the life of the master and a type pertaining to after his death. Then he said: As for the first, we say to the master, etc. It would have been appropriate for the author to do likewise because he will later say: 'As for the ruling after the death of the master.' His saying: 'This indicates that it is not actual' because a free person cannot be employed without his consent. His saying 'and benefit from them' meaning he may make them earn, and the earnings are for the master. Al-Bada'i' said: This also indicates what [follows].
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the ruling regarding a master who says 'one of my slaves is free' without specifying which. The commentary opens by identifying the different positions within the Hanafi school: Abu Yusuf (and reportedly Abu Hanifa) hold that the statement is a suspended emancipation (ta'liq) that descends upon an unspecified slave at the moment of choice, while Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that it is an immediate emancipation (ta'jiz) in an unspecified slave, with the subsequent choice being merely a declaration (bayan) of which slave was freed from the beginning. The commentator then provides evidence from the parallel case of divorce (talaq) to illustrate the difference: if a man says to his two wives 'one of you is divorced,' Abu Yusuf calculates the waiting period from the time of choice, indicating divorce is not immediate, while Muhammad calculates from the initial statement, indicating immediate divorce. An additional narration from Abu Yusuf uses the phrase 'it attaches to his liability' suggesting the emancipation is not yet fixed in a specific slave. The commentator criticizes the view that the choice is partly disclosure and partly creation, saying a single utterance cannot be both. He then states the first practical ruling: before choice, the master may still employ both slaves and take their earnings, which supports the view that freedom is not yet actual (i.e., the ta'liq position). The passage concludes with the sharh's own structural analysis of the matn, referencing al-Bada'i' and noting that the same point about using the slaves indicates the non-occurrence of emancipation.

Key Terms
تنجيز (tanzīz): Immediate effect of emancipation at the moment of utterance, without waiting for choice.
تعليق (taʿlīq): Suspended emancipation that takes effect only upon a future condition, here the master's choice.
بيان (bayān): Declaration or specification; in this context, the act of choosing which slave was meant from the start.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the practical consequence of the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the statement 'one of my two slaves is free'?
A) The master may not use the slaves before choice in either view.
B) The master may use both slaves and take their earnings before choice.
C) The slaves are immediately free and the master has no rights.
D) The master must pay compensation for using them.

Key Takeaway
In ambiguous emancipation, the mufta bihi Hanafi position is that freedom is not actual until the master chooses, allowing the master to use the slaves in the interim.

Compensation for Injuries and Death Before Choice in Ambiguous Emancipation
Rulings for injuries by one or two killers, and compensation distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ta'liq view to determine compensation when one or two killers injure or kill slaves whose emancipation is pending choice.

Core Idea
The suspended cause of emancipation affects liability for injuries, treating the slaves as partially free.

When a master ambiguously promises to free one of two slaves, their status is suspended until choice. This suspension has concrete effects on third-party liabilities. In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq works through scenarios where one or two killers injure or kill the slaves before the master chooses, showing how compensation is calculated for the master and heirs. The key is that the cause (sabab) of emancipation is already effective, analogous to a mother-slave (umm walad).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The first scenario: two killers kill both slaves together. The ruling: each killer pays half the value to the heirs and half to the master. Note the full diyah is not due.
Focus on the reason given: uncertainty about from whom diyah is due.
2
Locate the dalil
The author does not cite a direct text but uses analogy: the cause of emancipation is established, so the slaves are like partially free; accordingly, the liability is split.
This is a qiyas based on the ta'liq view.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The cause (sabab) is like istilad, which transmits freedom. Therefore, the master's right to compensation for injury to the 'quasi-free' portion is reduced.
The slaves are not yet free, but the cause affects ownership rights.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The ta'jiz view (Imam Muhammad) would see the emancipation as immediate, so the slaves are fully free and compensation goes entirely to heirs. The ta'liq view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) gives partial compensation to master.
The passage explicitly states 'on the ta'liq view'.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi is the ta'liq view, so these differential compensation rules are operative in Hanafi fatwa.
This is supported by the author's repeated confirmation.

وإن كان القاتل اثنين فإن كانا معاً فعلى كل واحد منهما القيمة نصفها للورثة ونصفها للمولى، وإنما لم تجب دية لأن من تجب عليه الدية منهما مجهول بخلاف ما إذا كان واحداً. وإن كان على التعاقب فعلى الأول القيمة للمولى وعلى الثاني الدية للورثة، ولو كانا أمتين فولدت كل واحدة ولداً أو إحداهما فاختار المولى عتق إحداهما عتقت هي وعتق ولدها، سواء كان للأخرى ولد أو لم يكن أما على قول التنجيز فظاهر، وهكذا على قول التعليق لانعقاد السبب فيسري كالاستيلاد ولو ماتا معاً قبل الاختيار وقد ولدت كل ولداً خير المولى فيختار عتق أي الوالدين شاء كما كان مخيراً فيهما، ولو قتل الأمتين رجل خير المولى في الولدين فأيهما اختار عتقه لا يرث من أرش أمه شيئاً لأنه إنما عتق بالاختيار وهو بعد موت الأم فلا يرث منها بل يكون الكل للمولى، وهذا نص مذهب التعليق . ولو وطئتا بشبهة قبل الاختيار يجب عقرهما للمولى كالأرش وهو يؤيد قول التعليق، ولو باعهما صفقة واحدة فسد البيع على المذهبين لانعقاد السبب على قول التعليق كما لو جمع بين قن ومدبر في البيع ولم يبين حصة كل واحد منهما من الثمن، ولو قبضهما المشتري وملك أحدهما وأعتقهما المشتري أمر البائع باختيار العتق، وأيهما اختار عتقه عتق الآخر على المشتري، فإن مات البائع قبل البيان قام الوارث مقامه، فإن لم يعتق المشتري حتى مات البائع لم ينقسم العتق بينهما حتى يفسخ القاضي البيع، فإذا فسخه انقسم وعتق من كل نصفه . ولو وهبهما قبل الاختيار أو تصدق بهما أو تزوج عليهما تخير فيختار العتق في أيهما شاء وتجوز الصدقة والهبة والإمهار في الآخر لأن حرية أحدهما لا يوجب بطلان هذه التصرفات لأنه لو جمع في الهبة بين حر وعبد فإنه يصح في العبد، وإن مات المولى قبل أن يبين العتق في أحدهما بطلت الهبة والصدقة فيهما وبطل إمهاره لشيوع العتق بموته ولو أسرهما أهل الحرب كان للمولى أن يختار العتق ويكون الآخر لأهل الحرب، فإن لم يختر حتى مات بطل ملك أهل الحرب لشيوع الحرية
And if the killer is two, then if they kill together, upon each of them is half the value [of each slave] for the heirs and half for the master; the full blood-money (diyah) is not due because from which of them the blood-money is due is unknown, unlike when there is one killer. If they kill consecutively, upon the first is the value for the master and upon the second is the blood-money for the heirs. And if they were two female slaves and each gave birth to a child, or one of them gave birth, then the master chooses emancipation of one of them; she becomes free and her child becomes free, whether the other has a child or not. On the view of immediate emancipation (tajiz) it is obvious; likewise on the view of suspension (ta'liq) because the cause is established, so it is transmitted like istilad. And if both die before choice and each had a child, the master is given the choice of emancipation of either parent; he may choose to free whichever he wishes, just as he had choice over them. And if a man killed both female slaves, the master chooses between the two children; whichever he chooses to free, that child does not inherit anything from the compensation for his mother, because he becomes free only by choice after the mother's death, so he does not inherit from her; rather, all goes to the master. This is the explicit text of the school of suspension. And if they are both penetrated under a doubtful contract before choice, the offspring belong to the master like compensation (arsh), and this supports the view of suspension. And if he sells them in one transaction, the sale is void according to both schools because the cause is established on the view of suspension, as if he combined a qinn and a mudabbar in a sale without specifying the share of each in the price. And if the buyer takes possession of them and owns one of them and emancipates them, the seller is ordered to choose the emancipation; whichever he chooses becomes free, and the other becomes free [as well] upon the buyer. If the seller dies before declaration, his heir stands in his place. If the buyer does not emancipate until the seller dies, the emancipation does not split between them until the judge rescinds the sale; when he rescinds it, it splits and half of each becomes free. And if he gives them as a gift (hiba) before choice, or gives them as charity, or gives them as dower (mahr), he may choose; he chooses emancipation in whichever he wishes, and the charity, gift, and dower are valid for the other, because the freedom of one does not necessitate invalidation of these transactions, just as if he combined a free person and a slave in a gift, it is valid for the slave. And if the master dies before declaring the emancipation in one of them, the gift and charity become void for both, and the dower becomes void because of the prevalence of freedom at his death. And if they are captured by warring polytheists, the master may choose emancipation; the other belongs to the polytheists. If he does not choose until he dies, the ownership of the polytheists becomes void due to the prevalence of freedom.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the practical legal consequences when two slaves are subject to an ambiguous emancipation statement and various events occur before the master makes his choice. The commentary extends the earlier dispute between ta'jiz and ta'liq into concrete scenarios. For instance, if a third party kills both slaves, the compensation distribution differs depending on whether the killing is simultaneous or consecutive, and whether the killer is one or two. The author explains that on the ta'liq view, the emancipation is suspended, so certain results follow, like the slave children becoming free with their mother when chosen, and the master retaining rights to offspring from doubtful intercourse. Sales, gifts, and other transactions made before choice are analyzed: a single sale of both slaves is void because the unspecified emancipation cloud is present. If the master dies before choosing, the choice passes to his heir; if no choice is made by the time of death, a legal fiction (like court rescission of sale) is used to effect a partial emancipation of each. The passage repeatedly shows that the ta'liq view (suspension) is the basis for these rulings, as it aligns with the practical need to preserve the master's options until choice while protecting the rights of all parties.

Key Terms
الاستيلاد (al-istīlād): The state of a female slave becoming umm walad by bearing her master's child, which partially frees her and affects transfer.
سبب (sabab): The cause or legal basis that triggers the eventual emancipation; here the master's statement is the sabab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the compensation from a killer if the two slaves are killed consecutively by two different people?
A) Both killers pay value to the master.
B) Both killers pay diyah to the heirs.
C) First killer pays value to master; second killer pays diyah to heirs.
D) First killer pays diyah; second pays value.

Key Takeaway
The suspended cause of emancipation from an ambiguous statement changes the legal consequences of injuries, splitting compensation between master and heirs.

Validity of Transactions and Effects of Master's Death in Ambiguous Emancipation
Rulings on sale, gift, charity, dower, and death before choice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the validity of sales, gifts, and other transactions involving slaves subject to ambiguous emancipation, and apply the rule that the choice passes to the heir upon the master's death.

Core Idea
A sale combining slaves with a pending emancipation cause is void; gifts and dower may be valid for the unchosen slave.

Once the master has made an ambiguous emancipation statement, his freedom to transact with those slaves is limited. Selling both together in one transaction is void because the cause of emancipation clouds the ownership. However, gifts and dower are permissible for the slave not later chosen. If the master dies before choosing, the choice passes to his heir. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details these rules, emphasizing that the cause of emancipation (sabab) is already effective, so that upon the master's death, freedom spreads to both, voiding any unfinished transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction and its ruling
First scenario: master sells both slaves in one lot. The ruling: the sale is void (fasid).
Reason: the cause of emancipation is established, making ownership uncertain.
2
Locate the dalil
The author draws an analogy: combining a qinn (fully owned slave) and a mudabbar (slave freed upon master's death) in a sale without specifying price shares is void.
Here, both slaves are like mudabbar because the cause is in effect.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The cause (sabab) of emancipation is like istilad, which gives a partial free status, making the ownership non-transferable in a single price.
The analogy works because in both cases, one of the slaves has a claim to freedom.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may consider the sale valid if the master can later specify, because emancipation is not yet effective.
Hanafis reject this because the cause is already in effect.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In Hanafi practice, the buyer must wait for the master to choose; the sale is void and must be rescinded by the court. Other schools might enforce the sale and let the master choose later.
The later part of the passage discusses the court's role.

المدبّر (al-mudabbar): A slave who is to be freed upon the master's death.

Compensation for Killing a Partially Free Slave by Two Persons
Ruling and commentary on compensation for killing a partially free slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the compensation owed by each killer when two persons kill a partially free slave, distinguishing joint from successive killing, and explain the underlying qiyas (analogical reasoning).

Core Idea
When two kill a partially free slave, each owes full value if joint; if successive, first owes value, second owes blood money.

The Hanafi school provides detailed rulings for scenarios where a slave with partial freedom is killed by two persons. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the rule, distinguishing between joint and successive killing, and explains the reasoning based on certainty versus doubt. It also reveals an internal Hanafi dispute about whether partial emancipation takes effect immediately or is suspended until the master's death. Understanding this ruling sharpens your ability to apply qiyas in complex liability cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the slave is partially free (e.g., half-free, half-slave) and the killers are two persons. Note the distinction between joint killing (both act together) and successive killing (one kills after the other).
The slave's status changes after the first killing if the emancipation takes effect.
2
Apply the joint-killing rule
If both kill together, each owes the full value (qimah) of the slave. Half of this goes to the master (for the slave portion) and half to the heirs (for the free portion). Blood money (diyah) is not imposed because the actual killer is unknown.
Certainty of value (qimah) overrides doubt about which killer caused death.
3
Apply the successive-killing rule
If they kill one after the other, the first killer owes value to the master (slave still partially enslaved), and the second killer owes blood money to the heirs (slave becomes fully free after first killing).
This depends on the view that emancipation takes effect immediately (tajiz).
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some Hanafi scholars hold that emancipation is suspended until the master's death (ta'liq). Under that view, the first killing does not fully free the slave, leading to different obligations in sub-cases (like gifts, sales, etc.).
The commentary explains how each view affects the division of compensation.
5
Trace the qiyas (reasoning)
The ruling is derived by analogy: killing a slave requires value; killing a free person requires blood money. Partial freedom creates partial obligations. When doubt exists about the killer's identity, value (certain) is preferred over blood money (uncertain).
This is an example of applying qiyas with certainty (qat'iy) over doubt (shakk).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان القاتل اثنين فإن كانا معاً فعلى كل واحد منهما القيمة نصفها للورثة ونصفها للمولى، وإنما لم تجب دية لأن من تجب عليه الدية منهما مجهول بخلاف ما إذا كان واحداً. وإن كان على التعاقب فعلى الأول القيمة للمولى وعلى الثاني الدية للورثة، ولو كانا أمتين فولدت كل واحدة ولداً أو إحداهما فاختار المولى عتق إحداهما عتقت هي وعتق ولدها، سواء كان للأخرى ولد أو لم يكن أما على قول التنجيز فظاهر، وهكذا على قول التعليق لانعقاد السبب فيسري كالاستيلاد ولو ماتا معاً قبل الاختيار وقد ولدت كل ولداً خير المولى فيختار عتق أي الوالدين شاء كما كان مخيراً فيهما، ولو قتل الأمتين رجل خير المولى في الولدين فأيهما اختار عتقه لا يرث من أرش أمه شيئاً لأنه إنما عتق بالاختيار وهو بعد موت الأم فلا يرث منها بل يكون الكل للمولى، وهذا نص مذهب التعليق . ولو وطئتا بشبهة قبل الاختيار يجب عقرهما للمولى كالأرش وهو يؤيد قول التعليق، ولو باعهما صفقة واحدة فسد البيع على المذهبين لانعقاد السبب على قول التعليق كما لو جمع بين قن ومدبر في البيع ولم يبين حصة كل واحد منهما من الثمن، ولو قبضهما المشتري وملك أحدهما وأعتقهما المشتري أمر البائع باختيار العتق، وأيهما اختار عتقه عتق الآخر على المشتري، فإن مات البائع قبل البيان قام الوارث مقامه، فإن لم يعتق المشتري حتى مات البائع لم ينقسم العتق بينهما حتى يفسخ القاضي البيع، فإذا فسخه انقسم وعتق من كل نصفه . ولو وهبهما قبل الاختيار أو تصدق بهما أو تزوج عليهما تخير فيختار العتق في أيهما شاء وتجوز الصدقة والهبة والإمهار في الآخر لأن حرية أحدهما لا يوجب بطلان هذه التصرفات لأنه لو جمع في الهبة بين حر وعبد فإنه يصح في العبد، وإن مات المولى قبل أن يبين العتق في أحدهما بطلت الهبة والصدقة فيهما وبطل إمهاره لشيوع العتق بموته ولو أسرهما أهل الحرب كان للمولى أن يختار العتق ويكون الآخر لأهل الحرب، فإن لم يختر حتى مات بطل ملك أهل الحرب لشيوع الحرية
قلنا قوله : (وإنما لم تجب دية الخ) قال في البدائع وإيجاب القيمتين دون قيمة ودية على قول من يقول إن العتق غير نازل ظاهر لأن كل واحد منهما قتل عبداً خطأ وأنه يوجب القيمة، وأما على قول من يقول بنزول العتق فإنما لم تجب الدية لأن من تجب الدية عليه متهماً مجهول إذ لا يعلم من الذي تجب عليه منهما فلا يمكن إيجاب الدية الشك والقيمة متيقنة فنجب بخلاف ما إذا كان القاتل مع واحداً لأن هناك من عليه معلوم إنما الجهالة فيمن له وأما انقسام القيمتين لأن المستحق لأحد البدلين هو المولى والمستحق للبدل الآخر هو الوارث وكل واحد منهما يستحق في حال ولا يستحق، فوجوب أحد القيمتين حجة أحد القولين وانقسامهما حجة القول الآخر قوله : (وعلى الثاني الدية للورثة قال في البدائع : لأن قتل الأول أوجب تعين الثاني للحرية والأول للرق قوله : (الشيوع العتق بموته قال في البدائع : فيعتق من كل واحد منهما نصفه ومعتق البعض لا يحتمل التمليك من الغير
If the killer is two, if they both killed together, then each one owes the value, half of it to the heirs and half to the master. And the blood money is not obligatory because the one upon whom the blood money is due is unknown, unlike when it is one person. If they killed successively, then the first owes the value to the master and the second owes the blood money to the heirs. If they were two slave women and each gave birth to a child, or one of them, and the master chose to free one of them, she becomes free and her child becomes free, whether the other had a child or not. On the view of immediate effect, it is apparent. Likewise on the view of suspension, because the cause is established so it spreads, like istilad (giving birth to a master's child). If both died before choice and each had given birth to a child, the master chooses to free whichever parent he wishes, just as he was given choice in the mothers. If a man killed the two slave women, the master has choice regarding the two children; whichever he chooses to free does not inherit from the value of his mother's blood money because he only becomes free by choice, and that is after the mother's death, so he does not inherit from her. Instead, all goes to the master. This is the explicit doctrine of the suspension view. If they were sexually violated under shubha before choice, their 'uqr (compensation) is obligatory for the master, like the blood money, and this supports the suspension view. If he sold them as a single lot, the sale is invalid according to both views, because the cause is established on the suspension view, just as if he combined a regular slave and a mudabbar in a sale without specifying each's share of the price. If the buyer took possession of both and owned one of them and then the buyer emancipated them, the seller is ordered to choose emancipation. Whichever he chooses to free, the other becomes free upon the buyer. If the seller dies before statement, the heir takes his place. If the buyer does not free until the seller dies, the emancipation is not divided between them until the judge rescinds the sale. When he rescinds it, it is divided and half of each is freed. If he gifted both before choice, or gave charity with them, or gave them as dower, he has choice; he chooses emancipation in whichever he wishes, and the charity, gift, and dower are valid in the other, because the freedom of one does not necessitate the invalidity of these dispositions, since if he combined a free person and a slave in a gift, it is valid for the slave. If the master dies before specifying emancipation in one of them, the gift and charity become void in both, and the dower becomes void due to the spread of emancipation by his death. If the people of war capture both, the master may choose emancipation and the other goes to the people of war. If he does not choose until he dies, the ownership of the people of war becomes void due to the spread of freedom. We say: His statement: (And the blood money is not obligatory, etc.) He said in al-Bada'i: The imposition of both values without value and blood money, according to the one who says that emancipation does not descend, is apparent because each one killed a slave by mistake, and that necessitates value. As for the one who says that emancipation does descend, the blood money is not obligatory because the one upon whom the blood money is due is suspected and unknown, since it is not known which of them the blood money is due from, so it is not possible to impose the blood money due to doubt, while the value is certain, so it is imposed. Unlike when the killer is one, because there the one upon whom it is due is known; the ignorance is only in the one to whom it is owed. As for the division of the two values, because the one entitled to one of the replacements is the master, and the one entitled to the other replacement is the heir, and each one is entitled in one case and not entitled. So the obligation of one of the two values is a proof for one of the two views, and their division is a proof for the other view. His statement: (And on the second, the blood money to the heirs). He said in al-Bada'i: Because the killing of the first necessitated the determination of the second for freedom and the first for slavery. His statement: (The spread of emancipation by his death). He said in al-Bada'i: So half of each of them is freed, and a partially freed slave cannot be owned by anyone.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, presents the ruling when two persons kill a slave who is partially free. The matn (base text) states that if two persons jointly kill such a slave, each owes the full value (not blood money), with half to the master and half to the heirs (since the slave was half-free, half-slave). The reason is that the identity of the one who actually caused death is unknown, so blood money (diyah) cannot be imposed; value (qimah) is certain and thus imposed. If the two kill successively, the first owes value to the master (as the slave was still partly enslaved at that time), and the second owes blood money to the heirs (because after the first killing, the slave became fully free, so killing a free person incurs diyah). The commentary from Bada'i' al-Sana'i' explains the reasoning behind the two views within the Hanafi school: the view that emancipation does not descend (tajiz) and the view that it does descend (ta'liq). All further sub-cases follow from these principles.

Key Terms
قيمة (qimah): Value, the compensation due for killing a slave (as opposed to diyah which is for a free person).
دية (diyah): Blood money payable for killing a free person.
عتق (itq): Emancipation, freeing of a slave.
قول التنجيز (qawl al-tajiz): The view that emancipation takes effect immediately upon the utterance.
قول التعليق (qawl al-ta'liq): The view that emancipation takes effect only upon the master's death (suspended).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When two persons jointly kill a half-free slave, what compensation do they owe?
A) Each owes half a blood money.
B) Each owes full value (qimah), half to master, half to heirs.
C) Each owes full blood money.
D) Only the first killer owes compensation.

Key Takeaway
In joint killing of a partially free slave, each killer owes full value; in successive killing, first owes value, second owes blood money.

Choice in Partial Emancipation: Master's Rights with Captives from Ahl al-Harb
Ruling on master's choice when slaves are bought from ahl al-harb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a merchant buys two partially free slaves from enemy territory and identify the master's right to choose which slave to free and the consequences of that choice.

Core Idea
The master retains the right to free one slave and take the other with its price, overriding the merchant's purchase.

This lesson examines the master's right to choose which of his partially free slaves to emancipate when a merchant buys them from ahl al-harb. The Hanafi ruling balances the master's ownership rights with the validity of the merchant's purchase, ensuring the master's original commitment to free his slaves is not undermined.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the scenario involves a merchant buying two partially free slaves from enemy territory (ahl al-harb). The slaves were previously partially owned by a master who had begun the process of emancipation.
Partial freedom means the slave is half-free or has some share of freedom.
2
State the master's options
The master can choose to free whichever of the two slaves he wishes and take the other slave by paying the merchant his share of the price.
3
Effect if master frees the bought slave
If the merchant bought only one of the two slaves, and the master chooses to free that specific slave, the slave becomes free and the purchase becomes void because the merchant's ownership was invalid due to the partial freedom.
4
Effect if master takes the bought slave by paying
If the master takes the slave from the merchant by reimbursing the price, then the other slave (the one not taken) becomes free immediately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيهما. ولو اشتراهما من أهل الحرب تاجر فللمولى أن يختار عتق أيهما شاء ويأخذ الآخر بحصته من الثمن، فإن اشترى التاجر أحدهما فاختار المولى عتقه عتق وبطل الشراء، فإن أخذه المولى من الذي اشتراء بالثمن عتق الآخر. ولو أعتق أحد عبديه في صحته ثم بين في المرض فإنه يعتق من جميع المال وإن كانت قيمته أكثر من الثلث وهذا يدل على أن إضافة العتق إلى المجهول إيقاع وتنجيز إذا لو كان تعليقاً لاعتبر من الثلث كالإنشاء في المرض، وسيأتي بيان ما يكون بياناً وما لا يكون بياناً. ولو قال أحد عبيدي حر ثلاث مرات وله ثلاثة عتقوا جميعاً، ولو قال أحدكم حر وكرره ثلاثاً لم يعتق إلا واحد لأن أحدهم عتق باللفظ الأول، ثم الثاني جمع بين حر وعبدين فقال أحدكم فلم يصح، ثم باللفظ الثالث جمع بين عبد وحرين فلم يصح ذلك أيضاً. ولو قال لعبده أنت حر أو مدبر يؤمر بالبيان، فإن قال عنيت به الحرية عتق، وإن قال عنيت التدبير صار مدبراً، فإن مات قبل البيان والقول في الصحة عتق نصفه بالإعتاق البات ونصفه بالتدبير لشيوع العتقين فيه إلا أن نصفه يعتق مجاناً من جميع المال، ونصفه يعتق من الثلث سواء كان التدبير في المرض أو في الصحة، إن خرج من الثلث عتق كل النصف، وإن لم يكن له مال غيره عتق ثلث النصف ويسعى في النصف وهو ثلث الكل . ثلثي وأما الحكم بعد موت المولى من غير بيان فإنه يعتق من كل واحد منهما نصفه والخيار لا يورث لشيوع العتق ويسعى في نصفه. وهذا كله إذا كان المزاحم له محتملاً للعتق وهو أحاداً ألا ترى قوله : (الشيوع الحرية فيهما قال في البدائع: لأنه لما مات المولى شاعت الحرية وعتق من كل واحد منهما نصفه فتعذر التملك وفيه : ولو أسر أهل الحرب أحدهما لم يملكوه لأن أحدهما حر وثبت له حق الحرية بخلاف ما إذا باع أحدهما لأن بيعه إياه اختيار منه للملك فقد باع ملكه باختياره فصح قوله : (عتق الآخر) قال في البدائع : لأن أخذه إياه إعادة له إلى قديم ملكه فيتعين الآخر قوله : (وله ثلاثة عتقوا قال في البدائع : كما لو قال ابتداء أحد عبيدي حر وليس له إلا عبد واحد لأن لفظة «أحد» لا تقتضي أن الله تعالى موصوف أنه أحد ولا مثل له ولا شريك قوله : (ثم باللفظ الثالث جمع بين عبد وحرين هكذا رأيته في البدائع قوله : ( وإن لم يكن له مال غيره الخ) لم يذكر مقابل وقوله والقول في الصحة وفي البدائع : هذا كله إذا كان القول في الصحة فإن كان في ذلك المرض يعتبر من الثلث قوله : (وأما الحكم بعد موت المولى هذا هو النوع الثاني من نوعي الأحكام المذكورين في البدائع كما نبهنا عليه سابقاً قوله : (والخيار لا يورث) أي فلا يقوم الوارث مقامه . قال في البدائع : ثم فرقا بين هذا الخيار وبين خيار التعيين في باب البيع فإن الوارث هناك يقوم مقام المورث في البيان أن هناك ملك المشتري أحد العبدين مجهولاً فمتى جرى الإرث يثبت ولاية التعيين أما ها هنا فأحدهما أو استحق الحرية وذلك يمنع جريان الإرث في أحدهما قوله : حر
In them both. If a merchant buys them from the people of war, then the master may choose to free whichever he wishes and take the other with his share of the price. If the merchant bought one of them, and the master chooses to free him, he becomes free and the purchase is void. If the master takes him from the one who bought him with the price, the other becomes free. If he emancipates one of his two slaves in health, then specifies in illness, he becomes free from all the wealth even if his value exceeds one-third. This indicates that attaching emancipation to the unknown is an immediate act (tajiz), because if it were suspended (ta'liq), it would be considered from one-third, like initiating in illness. The explanation of what counts as specification and what does not will come later. If he says 'One of my slaves is free' three times and he has three, they all become free. If he says 'One of you is free' and repeats it three times, only one becomes free, because the first utterance freed one; then the second utterance combined a free person with two slaves so it is invalid; then the third utterance combined a slave with two free persons, so that is also invalid. If he says to his slave 'You are free or mudabbar,' he is ordered to specify. If he says 'I meant freedom,' he becomes free; if he says 'I meant tadbir,' he becomes mudabbar. If he dies before specification, and the statement was in health, half of him is freed by definitive emancipation and half by tadbir due to the spread of the two emancipations in him, except that half is freed gratis from all the wealth, and half is freed from one-third, whether the tadbir was in illness or health. If it comes out of one-third, the whole half is freed; if he has no other wealth, one-third of that half is freed and he works to earn the half, which is one-third of the whole. And as for the ruling after the master's death without specification, half of each of them is freed, and the option is not inheritable due to the spread of emancipation, and he works to earn half of his value. All this is when the competitor is capable of emancipation. He said: (The spread of freedom in them) He said in al-Bada'i: Because when the master died, freedom spread and half of each of them was freed, so ownership became impossible. And in it: If the people of war captured one of them, they do not own him because one of them is free and the right of freedom is established for him, unlike if he sold one of them, because his sale of him is a choice for ownership, so he sold his property by choice, so it is valid. His statement: (The other is freed) He said in al-Bada'i: Because his taking him is a return to his old ownership, so the other becomes determined. His statement: (And he has three, they are all freed) He said in al-Bada'i: As if he initially said 'One of my slaves is free' and he only has one slave, because the word 'one' does not imply that Allah is described as 'One' without like or partner. His statement: (Then with the third utterance he combined a slave and two free persons) This is how I saw it in al-Bada'i. His statement: (And if he has no other wealth, etc.) He did not mention the opposite and his statement that the statement was in health. In al-Bada'i: All this is if the statement was in health; if it was in that illness, it is considered from one-third. His statement: (And as for the ruling after the master's death) This is the second type of the two types of rulings mentioned in al-Bada'i as we pointed out earlier. His statement: (And the option is not inheritable) i.e., the heir does not take his place. He said in al-Bada'i: Then he distinguished between this option and the option of specification in the chapter of sale, because there the heir takes the place of the testator in specification because there the buyer owns one of the two slaves ambiguously, so when inheritance occurs, the authority of specification is established. But here, one of them has deserved freedom, and that prevents the occurrence of inheritance in one of them. His statement: Free.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq continues with several rulings related to partial emancipation. First, if a merchant buys two partially free slaves from enemy territory, the master retains the choice to free one and take the other with its price. If the master frees the one the merchant bought, the purchase is void, and if the master takes that slave by paying the price, the other becomes free. Second, if a master emancipates one of his two slaves in health (i.e., before his final illness) and then specifies which one in his will during illness, that slave is freed from the entire estate even if his value exceeds one-third, because the emancipation was immediate (tajiz) rather than suspended. If it were suspended, it would be limited to one-third. Third, if someone says 'One of my slaves is free' three times and he has three slaves, all three become free because each utterance is interpreted as referring to a different slave. But if he says 'One of you is free' to a group and repeats it three times, only one slave is freed because the first utterance already freed one, and subsequent utterances are invalid when they combine free and slave. Fourth, if someone says to his slave 'You are free or mudabbar,' he must specify his intention. If he dies without specifying, half is freed as a definitive emancipation and half as tadbir; the definitive half is free from all wealth, while the tadbir half is free from one-third. Fifth, after the master's death without any specification, half of each partially free slave is freed, and the option (to choose) is not transferred to heirs because freedom has already spread. The commentary from Bada'i' explains the reasoning behind these rulings.

Key Terms
أهل الحرب (ahl al-harb): Non-Muslims who are in a state of war with Muslims.
اختيار (ikhtiyar): Choice or option given to the master to select which slave to free.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A merchant buys two partially free slaves from ahl al-harb. The master chooses to free one. What is the ruling on the other slave?
A) The other slave remains enslaved with the merchant.
B) The other slave becomes free automatically.
C) The master must pay the merchant's share of the price for the other slave to become free.
D) The other slave is returned to the master without payment.

Key Takeaway
The master retains the right to choose which partially free slave to free when purchased from enemy territory, but must compensate the merchant for the other slave's share.

Immediate vs. Suspended Emancipation: Health and Illness Specification
Ruling on emancipation in health with specification in illness, showing it is immediate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between immediate (tajiz) and suspended (ta'liq) emancipation and apply the Hanafi ruling when a master frees a slave in health and specifies in illness.

Core Idea
Emancipation attached to an unknown slave is immediate, so it takes effect from the entire estate, not limited to one-third.

This lesson examines the distinction between immediate and suspended emancipation in the context of partial emancipation. The key ruling states that if a master frees one of his two slaves while in good health and later specifies which one during his final illness, that slave is freed from the entire estate, even if his value exceeds one-third. This indicates that the emancipation was immediate, not suspended, unlike a bequest made during illness which is limited to one-third.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The master says 'One of my slaves is free' while in good health (before terminal illness). Later, during his terminal illness, he specifies which slave he meant.
The master is healthy at the time of the first statement.
2
Determine the ruling
The slave becomes free from the entire estate, even if his value exceeds one-third of the estate.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning
The ruling demonstrates that attaching emancipation to an unknown slave is an immediate act (tajiz), not a suspended one (ta'liq). If it were suspended, it would be treated like a bequest made during illness and limited to one-third.
The proof is the contrast: if it were ta'liq, the rule would be from one-third.
4
Note the implication
The distinction between immediate and suspended affects whether the emancipation is limited by the one-third rule applicable to bequests.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

All this is when the competitor is capable of emancipation. He said: (The spread of freedom in them) He said in al-Bada'i: Because when the master died, freedom spread and half of each of them was freed, so ownership became impossible. And in it: If the people of war captured one of them, they do not own him because one of them is free and the right of freedom is established for him, unlike if he sold one of them, because his sale of him is a choice for ownership, so he sold his property by choice, so it is valid. His statement: (The other is freed) He said in al-Bada'i: Because his taking him is a return to his old ownership, so the other becomes determined. His statement: (And he has three, they are all freed) He said in al-Bada'i: As if he initially said 'One of my slaves is free' and he only has one slave, because the word 'one' does not imply that Allah is described as 'One' without like or partner. His statement: (Then with the third utterance he combined a slave and two free persons) This is how I saw it in al-Bada'i. His statement: (And if he has no other wealth, etc.) He did not mention the opposite and his statement that the statement was in health. In al-Bada'i: All this is if the statement was in health; if it was in that illness, it is considered from one-third. His statement: (And as for the ruling after the master's death) This is the second type of the two types of rulings mentioned in al-Bada'i as we pointed out earlier. His statement: (And the option is not inheritable) i.e., the heir does not take his place. He said in al-Bada'i: Then he distinguished between this option and the option of specification in the chapter of sale, because there the heir takes the place of the testator in specification because there the buyer owns one of the two slaves ambiguously, so when inheritance occurs, the authority of specification is established. But here, one of them has deserved freedom, and that prevents the occurrence of inheritance in one of them. His statement: Free.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq continues with several rulings related to partial emancipation. First, if a merchant buys two partially free slaves from enemy territory, the master retains the choice to free one and take the other with its price. If the master frees the one the merchant bought, the purchase is void, and if the master takes that slave by paying the price, the other becomes free. Second, if a master emancipates one of his two slaves in health (i.e., before his final illness) and then specifies which one in his will during illness, that slave is freed from the entire estate even if his value exceeds one-third, because the emancipation was immediate (tajiz) rather than suspended. If it were suspended, it would be limited to one-third. Third, if someone says 'One of my slaves is free' three times and he has three slaves, all three become free because each utterance is interpreted as referring to a different slave. But if he says 'One of you is free' to a group and repeats it three times, only one slave is freed because the first utterance already freed one, and subsequent utterances are invalid when they combine free and slave. Fourth, if someone says to his slave 'You are free or mudabbar,' he must specify his intention. If he dies without specifying, half is freed as a definitive emancipation and half as tadbir; the definitive half is free from all wealth, while the tadbir half is free from one-third. Fifth, after the master's death without any specification, half of each partially free slave is freed, and the option (to choose) is not transferred to heirs because freedom has already spread. The commentary from Bada'i' explains the reasoning behind these rulings.

Key Terms
إيقاع (iqa'): Immediate effect; the act takes effect at the time of utterance.
تنجيز (tajiz): Making something immediate; synonymous with iqa'.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension; the act takes effect upon fulfillment of a condition (e.g., death).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A master in good health says 'One of my slaves is free.' He later specifies in his final illness. What is the ruling?
A) The slave is freed from one-third of the estate.
B) The slave is freed from the entire estate.
C) The slave is not freed because specification must be in health.
D) The slave is freed only if the heirs consent.

Key Takeaway
Emancipation attached to an unknown slave while healthy is immediate and not subject to the one-third limitation for bequests.

Ambiguous Language in Emancipation: Repetition and Specification
Rulings on ambiguous emancipation language, including repetition and alternative expressions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling when ambiguous emancipation language is used, including repeated statements and 'free or mudabbar' scenarios, and determine the outcome.

Core Idea
Repeated ambiguous emancipation statements can free multiple slaves; if the master expresses doubt, he must specify his intent, and death without specification leads to partial freedom.

This lesson covers two important scenarios involving ambiguous language in emancipation: (1) repeating 'One of my slaves is free' three times when owning three slaves, and (2) saying 'You are free or mudabbar' without specification. The Hanafi rulings clarify how each word is interpreted and what happens when the master dies without clarifying his intent.

Guided Path
1
First scenario: repeated 'One of my slaves is free'
If a master says 'One of my slaves is free' three times and he has three slaves, all three become free because each utterance is interpreted as referring to a different slave.
This is based on qiyas: like saying it to a single slave initially.
2
Second scenario: 'One of you is free' repeated
If the master says 'One of you is free' to a group and repeats it three times, only one becomes free because after the first utterance, the group includes a free person, invalidating subsequent utterances.
3
Third scenario: 'You are free or mudabbar'
The master must specify his intent. If he says 'I meant freedom,' the slave is free; if 'I meant tadbir,' he becomes mudabbar. If the master dies before specifying, the slave becomes half-free by immediate emancipation and half by tadbir.
Half from all wealth, half from one-third.
4
Ruling after death without specification
If the master dies without specifying, half of each of two partially free slaves is freed, and the option to choose is not inheritable because freedom has already spread.

In them both. If a merchant buys them from the people of war, then the master may choose to free whichever he wishes and take the other with his share of the price. If the merchant bought one of them, and the master chooses to free him, he becomes free and the purchase is void. If the master takes him from the one who bought him with the price, the other becomes free. If he emancipates one of his two slaves in health, then specifies in illness, he becomes free from all the wealth even if his value exceeds one-third. This indicates that attaching emancipation to the unknown is an immediate act (tajiz), because if it were suspended (ta'liq), it would be considered from one-third, like initiating in illness. The explanation of what counts as specification and what does not will come later. If he says 'One of my slaves is free' three times and he has three, they all become free. If he says 'One of you is free' and repeats it three times, only one becomes free, because the first utterance freed one; then the second utterance combined a free person with two slaves so it is invalid; then the third utterance combined a slave with two free persons, so that is also invalid. Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq continues with several rulings related to partial emancipation. First, if a merchant buys two partially free slaves from enemy territory, the master retains the choice to free one and take the other with its price. If the master frees the one the merchant bought, the purchase is void, and if the master takes that slave by paying the price, the other becomes free. Second, if a master emancipates one of his two slaves in health (i.e., before his final illness) and then specifies which one in his will during illness, that slave is freed from the entire estate even if his value exceeds one-third, because the emancipation was immediate (tajiz) rather than suspended. If it were suspended, it would be limited to one-third. Third, if someone says 'One of my slaves is free' three times and he has three slaves, all three become free because each utterance is interpreted as referring to a different slave. But if he says 'One of you is free' to a group and repeats it three times, only one slave is freed because the first utterance already freed one, and subsequent utterances are invalid when they combine free and slave. Fourth, if someone says to his slave 'You are free or mudabbar,' he must specify his intention. If he dies without specifying, half is freed as a definitive emancipation and half as tadbir; the definitive half is free from all wealth, while the tadbir half is free from one-third. Fifth, after the master's death without any specification, half of each partially free slave is freed, and the option (to choose) is not transferred to heirs because freedom has already spread. The commentary from Bada'i' explains the reasoning behind these rulings.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A type of emancipation where the master declares that his slave will be free after his death.
بيان (bayan): Specification or clarification of which slave is intended for emancipation.
شيوع (shuyu'): Spread or diffusion; here, the spread of freedom over both slaves after the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A master says 'You are free or mudabbar' to his slave and dies without specifying. The statement was made in health. What is the ruling?
A) The slave is free from all the wealth.
B) The slave is mudabbar from one-third.
C) Half is free from all wealth, half is mudabbar from one-third.
D) The slave is not freed until the heirs specify.

Key Takeaway
Ambiguous emancipation language can lead to multiple slaves being freed or a split ruling; specification is required to avoid partial freedom.
