The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Conditional Manumission with Twins
Intra-Hanafi dispute over composite condition ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on conditional manumission with unknown twin order and explain why the position of al-Jami' al-Saghir is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
When a condition has two parts, certainty about one part demands consideration of states, not outright rejection.

This lesson delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute where a master’s conditional manumission involves twins of unknown birth order. The core question is whether the condition is unitary or composite, leading to different rulings from Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to handle partial certainty in legal conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the two conditions
The master says: 'If the first child is a boy, you are free; if a girl, she is free.' Twins are born, order unknown. The condition has two parts: birth of a boy/girl and being first.
The condition is not simple; it is composite (murakkab).
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah position (Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf)
According to al-Jami' al-Saghir: the girl is free (in either scenario), the boy is a slave, and half of the mother is freed. This is based on considering the possible states.
Half the mother is freed because she is fully free if boy first, slave if girl first.
3
State Muhammad's opposing position and his proof
Imam Muhammad (later view in al-Kaysaniyyat) rules that none are freed because the condition as a whole is not certainly fulfilled; manumission cannot be based on doubt.
He treats the condition as a single unit.
4
Apply the tarjih principle to determine mufta bihi
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq supports the position of al-Jami' al-Saghir because: (1) it is textually established (nasṣ), (2) the condition is composite, and (3) i'tibar al-ahwal is necessary when part of the condition is certain.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العتق باب العبد يعتق بعضه
في الجامع الصغير من غير خلاف فيه. والمذكور لمحمد في الكيسانيات في هذه المسألة أنه لا يحكم بعتق واحد منهم لأنا لم نتيقن بعتق واعتبار الأحوال بعد التيقن بالحرية، ولا يجوز إيقاع العتق بالشك فعن هذا حكم الطحاوي بأن محمداً كان أولاً مع أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ثم رجع. وفي النهاية عن المبسوط أن هذا الجواب ليس جواب هذا الفصل بل في هذا الفصل لا يحكم بعتق واحد ولكن يحلف المولى بالله ما يعلم أنها ولدت الجارية أولاً، فإن نكل فنكوله كإقراره، وإن حلف فكلهم أرقاء وأما جواب هذا الفصل إنما هو فيما إذا قال إن كان أول ولد تلدينه غلاماً فأنت حرة، وإن كانت جارية فهي حرة، فولدتهما ولا يدري الأول فالغلام رقيق والأنثى حرة ويعتق نصف الأم، ولا شك أن هذا ليس جواب الكتاب لأن في هذه الصورة يعتق جميع الجارية على كل حال لأنها إن ولدت الجارية أولاً عتقت بالشرط، وإن ولدت الغلام أولاً عتقت تبعاً للأم وأما انتصاف عتق الأم فلأنها تعتق في ولادة الغلام أولاً وترق في الجارية، وجواب الكتاب عتق نصفها مع نصف الأم. وصحح في النهاية ما في الكيسانيات لأن الشرط الذي لم يتيقن وجوده إذا كان في طرف واحد كان القول قول من أنكر وجوده كما إذا قال إن دخلت الدار غداً فأنت حر فمضى الغد ولا يدري أدخل الدار أم لا للشك في شرط العتق فكذا وقع الشك في شرط العتق وهو ولادة الغلام أولاً. وأما إذا كان الشرط مذكوراً في طرفي الوجود والعدم كان أحدهما موجوداً لا محالة فحينئذ يحتاج إلى اعتبار الأحوال فإن قلت : المفروض في مسألة الكتاب تصادقهم على عدم علم المتقدم والمتأخر، فكيف يحلف ولا دعوى ولا منازع؟ قلت: هو محمول على دعوى من خارج حسبة عتق الأمة أو بنتها لوجود الشرط، وقد عرف أن الأمة لو أنكرت العتق وشهد به يقبل فعلى هذا جاز أن يدعي رجل حسبة إذا لم تكن بينة ليحلف لرجاء نكوله، هذا ولكن المذكور في المبسوط في تعليله صرح بأن الأم تدعي العتق والمولى ينكر والقول للمنكر مع يمينه، فأفاد أن ذلك في صورة دعوى الأم وهي غير هذه الصورة التي في الكتاب. واعلم أن ما ذكر في النهاية من ترجيح ما في الكيسانيات حقيقته إبطال قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف مع أنه لم يرو عنهما رواية شاذة تخالف ذلك في الجواب، واستدلاله بأن الشرط الكائن في طرف واحد إلى آخر قد ينظر فيه بأن ذلك في الشرط الظاهر لا الخفي، ولذا قيد في المبسوط حيث قال : إذا قال إن فعلت كذا فأنت حر وذلك من الأمور الظاهرة كالصوم والصلاة ودخول الدار فقال العبد فعلت لا يصدق إلا ببينة بخلاف قوله إن كنت تحبيني إلى طلاق المعينة رجعياً فكذلك، وإن كان بائناً كان بياناً لما علم من أن البائن لا يلحق البائن قوله: (ما يعلم أنها ولدت الجارية أو لا كذا في عامة النسخ وهكذا رأيته في الفتح وفي بعض النسخ مصلحاً بإبدال الجارية بالغلام وهو ظاهر.

كتاب العتق باب العبد يعتق بعضه
آخره. فيمكن أن تكون الولادة من الأمور التي ليست ظاهرة فيوجب الشك فيها اعتبار الأحوال فيعتق نصف الأم كما في الجامع والله أعلم؛ كذا في فتح القدير وفيه نظر، لأن جعل الولادة من الأمور الخفية كمحبة القلب لا يصح لأن المراد بالأمور الظاهرة ما يمكن اطلاع الغير عليها والمراد بالخفية ما لا يمكن اطلاع الغير عليه ولا شك أن الولادة مما يمكن الاطلاع عليها ولذا اتفقوا أنه لا يقبل قول المرأة في الولادة ولو كانت كالمحبة لقبل قولها، وإنما اختلفوا هل يكتفي بشهادة المرأة أو لا بد من شهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين كما قدمناه. فالحق أن المسألة مشكلة لأنها لا توافق الأصول ولا يمكن الحكم بإبطال هذا الجواب كما في النهاية لأن جوابها نص الجامع الصغير، ولولا ذلك لتعين القول بما في النهاية، وقد ظهر للعبد الضعيف أن مشايخنا يعتبرون الأحوال عند تعدد الشرط وعند التعليق بشرط واحد له جزآن كمسألتنا.
قوله : (فإن العتق معلق على شرطه له جزآن إحداهما ولادة الغلام، وثانيهما كونه أول، ففي كل منهما إذا تحقق وجود البعض ووقع التردد في تعيينه فحينئذ تعتبر الأحوال، فإن في مسألتنا تحقق ولادة الغلام لكن لم يدر أنه أول بخلاف التعليق بدخول الدار ونحوه فإن الشرط شيء واحد ولم يتحقق وجوده فلا تعتبر الأحوال. فالحاصل أن الشرط إذا كان مركباً من جزئين فهو كالتعليق بشرطين. وبهذا التقدير يصح ما في الجامع الصغير وتتوافق الفروع مع الأصول كما لا يخفى والمراد بعدم علم الأول تصادقهم على عدم معرفة الأول، وقيد به لأنهم لو اتفقوا على أن ولادة الغلام أولاً أو اتفقوا على أن ولادة الجارية أولاً فلا يعتق أحد في الثاني ويعتق كل الأم والجارية في الأول فهي ثلاثة، والرابعة لو اختلفا فادعت الأم ولادة الغلام أولاً وأنكر المولى والجارية صغيرة فالقول قول المولى لأنه ينكر شرط العتق ويحلف على العلم لأنه فعل الغير ؛ فإن حلف لم يعتق واحد منهما إلا تقيم البينة بعد ذلك، وإن نكل عتقت الأم والبنت لأن دعوى الأم حرية الصغير معتبرة لأنها نفع محض ولها عليها ولاية لا سيما إذا لم يعرف لها أب. الخامسة أن تدعي الأم بأن الغلام هو الأول ولم تدع البنت وهي كبيرة فإنه يحلف المولى، فإن حلف لم يعتق واحد منهم، وإن نكل عتقت الأم دون البنت لأن النكول حجة ضرورية فلا تتعدى ولا ضرورة أن.
قوله: (ولا شك أن الولادة مما يمكن الإطلاع عليها قال في النهر : لا يخفى أنه ليس المراد بالولادة مطلقها بل التي الكلام فيها وهو كون الغلام أولاً وهذا مع ولادتهما في حمل واحد مما يخفى غالباً قوله : ( فالحاصل أن الشرط إذا كان مركباً الخ) تتوقف صحة هذا التعميم على صحة هذا الحكم في قوله لعبده إن دخلت الدار قبل زيد فأنت حر ووجد الدخول ولم تدر القبلية فإن مقتضى ما ذكره اعتبار الأحوال مع أن الرق ثابت بيقين ووقع الشك في زواله لعدم العلم بوقوع الجزء الآخر تأمل.
Chapter of Manumission: Section on a slave who is partially freed. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, there is no disagreement about it. What is mentioned by Muhammad in al-Kaysaniyyat regarding this issue is that he does not rule that any of them is freed, because we are not certain of manumission, and consideration of states (i'tibar al-ahwal) is after certainty of freedom, and it is not permissible to effect manumission with doubt. Based on this, al-Tahawi ruled that Muhammad was initially with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, then retracted. In al-Nihaya from al-Mabsut: This answer is not the answer for this chapter; rather, in this chapter, no one is ruled to be freed, but the master takes an oath by Allah that he does not know whether she gave birth to the girl first. If he refuses, his refusal is like his confession; if he swears, all are slaves. The answer for this chapter is only in the case where he says: 'If the first child you give birth to is a boy, you are free; if it is a girl, she is free,' and she gives birth to both and it is not known which was first: the boy is a slave, the female is free, and half of the mother is freed. There is no doubt that this is not the answer of the book because in this scenario the entire girl is freed in any case because if she gave birth to the girl first, she is freed by the condition; if she gave birth to the boy first, she is freed as a consequence of the mother. As for half of the mother being freed, it is because she is freed in the case of the boy being born first and remains a slave in the case of the girl. The answer of the book is that half of her is freed along with half of the mother. Al-Nihaya corrected what is in al-Kaysaniyyat because the condition whose existence is not certain, if it is on one side, the word is of the one who denies its existence, as when he says 'If you enter the house tomorrow, you are free,' then tomorrow passes and he does not know whether he entered the house or not, due to doubt in the condition of manumission. So similarly, doubt occurred in the condition of manumission, which is the birth of the boy first. When the condition is mentioned on both sides of existence and non-existence, then one of them must exist inevitably; then consideration of states is needed. If you say: The scenario in the book is that they agree on not knowing which was earlier and later, so how can he take an oath when there is no claim or dispute? I say: It is interpreted as a claim from an outsider (hissba) for the sake of freeing the slave woman or her daughter due to the existence of the condition. It is known that if the slave woman denies the manumission and testimony is given, it is accepted. Based on this, it is permissible for a man to make a claim for hisba if there is no evidence, so that he may take an oath hoping for his refusal. But what is mentioned in al-Mabsut in its reasoning states clearly that the mother claims manumission and the master denies, and the word is of the denier with his oath. So this indicates that it is in the case of the mother's claim, which is different from the case in the book. Know that what is mentioned in al-Nihaya preferring what is in al-Kaysaniyyat is essentially nullifying the statement of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, even though no odd transmission contrary to that in the answer has been narrated from them. His argument that the condition being on one side... may be considered that it is in the apparent condition, not the hidden one. Hence al-Mabsut conditioned where he said: If he says 'If you do such and such, you are free,' and that is among apparent matters like fasting, prayer, and entering the house, and the slave says 'I did it,' he is not believed except with evidence, contrary to his saying 'If you love me' up to the divorce of a specific woman revocably, then likewise; if it is irrevocable, it is an explanation of what is known that the irrevocable does not join the irrevocable. His statement: 'He does not know whether she gave birth to the girl or not' is found in most copies, and thus I saw it in al-Fath. In some copies it is corrected by replacing 'al-jariya' with 'al-ghulam', which is apparent. ... So it is possible that birth is among matters that are not apparent, so doubt about it necessitates consideration of states, so half of the mother is freed as in al-Jami'. Allah knows best. Thus in Fath al-Qadir, but there is a view: because making birth like hidden matters like love of the heart is not correct, because what is meant by apparent matters is what others can have knowledge of, and what is meant by hidden is what others cannot have knowledge of. There is no doubt that birth is something that can be known, hence they agreed that the woman's statement regarding birth is not accepted, whereas if it were like love, her statement would be accepted. They only disagreed whether the testimony of a woman is sufficient or whether the testimony of two men or one man and two women is necessary, as we have presented. The truth is that the issue is problematic because it does not conform to the principles, and it is not possible to rule invalidating this answer as in al-Nihaya because its answer is the text of al-Jami' al-Saghir. Were it not for that, the statement according to al-Nihaya would be determined. And it has become apparent to this weak servant that our shuyukh consider the states (ahwal) when there are multiple conditions and when the ta'liq is with a single condition that has two parts, like our issue. His statement: 'The manumission is suspended on its condition. It has two parts: one is the birth of the boy, and the second is his being first. So in each of them, if the existence of some is verified and hesitation occurs in its determination, then the states are considered. In our issue, the birth of the boy is verified but it is not known if he was first, contrary to the ta'liq on entering the house and the like, because the condition is one thing and its existence is not verified, so the states are not considered. The conclusion is that if the condition is composed of two parts, it is like ta'liq with two conditions. With this estimation, what is in al-Jami' al-Saghir becomes correct and the branches align with the principles, as is not hidden. What is meant by not knowing the first is their agreement on not knowing the first. It is restricted because if they agree that the birth of the boy was first or agree that the birth of the girl was first, then no one is freed in the second and the entire mother and girl are freed in the first. So there are three cases. The fourth: if they differ, the mother claims the boy was born first and the master denies and the girl is young, then the word is of the master because he denies the condition of manumission and he takes an oath based on knowledge because it is an act of another. If he swears, neither of them is freed unless evidence is established after that. If he refuses, the mother and the daughter are freed because the mother's claim of freedom for the young child is considered because it is pure benefit and she has guardianship over her, especially if no father is known. The fifth: the mother claims that the boy is the first and the daughter (who is adult) does not claim; then the master takes an oath. If he swears, none of them is freed; if he refuses, the mother is freed but not the daughter, because the refusal (nukul) is a necessary proof and does not extend beyond necessity. His statement: 'There is no doubt that birth is something that can be known.' In al-Nahr: It is not hidden that what is meant by birth here is not absolute birth but the one under discussion, which is the boy being first, and this, together with their being born in one pregnancy, is often hidden. His statement: 'The conclusion is that if the condition is composed, etc.' The correctness of this generalization depends on the correctness of this ruling in his saying to his slave: 'If you enter the house before Zaid, you are free' and entry occurs but it is not known whether it was before; then the implication of what he mentioned is consideration of states, even though slavery is established with certainty and doubt occurred in its removal due to lack of knowledge of the occurrence of the other part. (Consider carefully.)
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding a case of conditional manumission where twins are born and it is unknown which child was born first. The case: A master says to his pregnant slave woman, 'If the first child you give birth to is a boy, you are free; if it is a girl, she is free.' She gives birth to a boy and a girl, but it is unknown which came first. The Hanafi school has three positions: The position recorded in al-Jami' al-Saghir (attributed to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that the girl is freed entirely, the boy remains a slave, and half of the mother is freed. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani initially agreed but later retracted, as reported in al-Kaysaniyyat, ruling that none of them are freed because certainty of manumission is required and doubt prevents it. Al-Nihaya attempts to reconcile by stating that the master should take an oath, and if he refuses, all are freed; if he swears, all remain slaves. However, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq critically refines these views. He explains that the condition here is composite (murakkab): it has two parts—birth of a boy and the boy being first. Since the birth of a boy is certain but the 'firstness' is uncertain, this is different from a simple condition like 'enter the house,' where the entire condition is uncertain. Therefore, consideration of states (i'tibar al-ahwal) is necessary, which supports the ruling from al-Jami' al-Saghir. The author also addresses whether birth is an apparent or hidden matter, concluding that the specific fact of which twin was first is often hidden, justifying the consideration of states. He then enumerates five possible scenarios based on agreement or disagreement among the parties. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of al-Jami' al-Saghir, because it aligns with usul and is textually established. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of reconciling textual sources (manqul) with juristic reasoning (ma'qul).

Key Terms
الشرط (al-shart): The condition upon which manumission is suspended. In this passage, it has two parts: birth of a boy and being first.
اعتبار الأحوال (i'tibar al-ahwal): The legal method of considering the different possible states or scenarios when there is uncertainty about a condition, and assigning the ruling that applies to each state proportionally.
النكول (al-nukul): Refusal of the defendant to take an oath after being required to do so. In this context, it is treated as an admission (iqrar) against the defendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (al-Jami' al-Saghir), what is the ruling for the mother when twins are born with unknown order?
A) She is fully free.
B) She is fully a slave.
C) She is half-free.
D) Her status depends on an oath.

Key Takeaway
When a condition has two parts and one part is certain, i'tibar al-ahwal (consideration of states) is applied, not outright rejection based on doubt.

7 min
I'tibar al-Ahwal: The Principle of Considering States in Composite Conditions
Analytical principle (i'tibar al-ahwal) from qiyas on composite conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a composite condition and apply the principle of i'tibar al-ahwal to derive the ruling.

Core Idea
A condition with two certain parts requires proportional consideration, not blanket uncertainty.

This lesson focuses on the methodological principle that resolves the intra-Hanafi dispute: i'tibar al-ahwal (consideration of states). By analyzing the qiyas (analogy) between simple and composite conditions, you will learn how to derive rulings when partial certainty exists. This is a core tool in Hanafi usul that ensures rulings align with both textual authority and rational consistency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the simple condition (asl) and its ruling
The asl is the case where a master says 'If you enter the house tomorrow, you are free' and the day passes without knowledge. The ruling: the slave is not freed because the condition is entirely uncertain.
This is a single condition (dakhul al-dar).
2
Compare with the composite condition (far') in our case
The far' is the twin case: 'If the first child is a boy, you are free; if a girl, she is free.' Here, the condition has two parts: birth of a boy (certain) and being first (uncertain). This is not a single condition; it is composite.
The existence of a boy is verified; only the order is unknown.
3
Extract the illa (effective cause) for the different ruling
In the asl, the entire condition is uncertain. In the far', one part is certain. The illa is: when part of a condition is certain, we cannot treat it as wholly uncertain; we must consider the possible states (i'tibar al-ahwal).
The illa is extracted via tahqiq al-manat: the fact that certainty about one part changes the legal reasoning.
4
Apply i'tibar al-ahwal to derive the ruling for the mother
Consider two states: State 1 (boy first): mother free, girl free as tābi'. State 2 (girl first): mother slave, girl free. Since both states are possible, the mother is half-free (proportional), and the girl is free in both states. The boy is a slave because his conditional freedom requires being first, which is uncertain.
This yields the ruling in al-Jami' al-Saghir: girl free, boy slave, mother half-free.

كتاب العتق باب العبد يعتق بعضه
في الجامع الصغير من غير خلاف فيه. والمذكور لمحمد في الكيسانيات في هذه المسألة أنه لا يحكم بعتق واحد منهم لأنا لم نتيقن بعتق واعتبار الأحوال بعد التيقن بالحرية، ولا يجوز إيقاع العتق بالشك فعن هذا حكم الطحاوي بأن محمداً كان أولاً مع أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ثم رجع. وفي النهاية عن المبسوط أن هذا الجواب ليس جواب هذا الفصل بل في هذا الفصل لا يحكم بعتق واحد ولكن يحلف المولى بالله ما يعلم أنها ولدت الجارية أولاً، فإن نكل فنكوله كإقراره، وإن حلف فكلهم أرقاء وأما جواب هذا الفصل إنما هو فيما إذا قال إن كان أول ولد تلدينه غلاماً فأنت حرة، وإن كانت جارية فهي حرة، فولدتهما ولا يدري الأول فالغلام رقيق والأنثى حرة ويعتق نصف الأم، ولا شك أن هذا ليس جواب الكتاب لأن في هذه الصورة يعتق جميع الجارية على كل حال لأنها إن ولدت الجارية أولاً عتقت بالشرط، وإن ولدت الغلام أولاً عتقت تبعاً للأم وأما انتصاف عتق الأم فلأنها تعتق في ولادة الغلام أولاً وترق في الجارية، وجواب الكتاب عتق نصفها مع نصف الأم. وصحح في النهاية ما في الكيسانيات لأن الشرط الذي لم يتيقن وجوده إذا كان في طرف واحد كان القول قول من أنكر وجوده كما إذا قال إن دخلت الدار غداً فأنت حر فمضى الغد ولا يدري أدخل الدار أم لا للشك في شرط العتق فكذا وقع الشك في شرط العتق وهو ولادة الغلام أولاً. وأما إذا كان الشرط مذكوراً في طرفي الوجود والعدم كان أحدهما موجوداً لا محالة فحينئذ يحتاج إلى اعتبار الأحوال فإن قلت : المفروض في مسألة الكتاب تصادقهم على عدم علم المتقدم والمتأخر، فكيف يحلف ولا دعوى ولا منازع؟ قلت: هو محمول على دعوى من خارج حسبة عتق الأمة أو بنتها لوجود الشرط، وقد عرف أن الأمة لو أنكرت العتق وشهد به يقبل فعلى هذا جاز أن يدعي رجل حسبة إذا لم تكن بينة ليحلف لرجاء نكوله، هذا ولكن المذكور في المبسوط في تعليله صرح بأن الأم تدعي العتق والمولى ينكر والقول للمنكر مع يمينه، فأفاد أن ذلك في صورة دعوى الأم وهي غير هذه الصورة التي في الكتاب. واعلم أن ما ذكر في النهاية من ترجيح ما في الكيسانيات حقيقته إبطال قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف مع أنه لم يرو عنهما رواية شاذة تخالف ذلك في الجواب، واستدلاله بأن الشرط الكائن في طرف واحد إلى آخر قد ينظر فيه بأن ذلك في الشرط الظاهر لا الخفي، ولذا قيد في المبسوط حيث قال : إذا قال إن فعلت كذا فأنت حر وذلك من الأمور الظاهرة كالصوم والصلاة ودخول الدار فقال العبد فعلت لا يصدق إلا ببينة بخلاف قوله إن كنت تحبيني إلى طلاق المعينة رجعياً فكذلك، وإن كان بائناً كان بياناً لما علم من أن البائن لا يلحق البائن قوله: (ما يعلم أنها ولدت الجارية أو لا كذا في عامة النسخ وهكذا رأيته في الفتح وفي بعض النسخ مصلحاً بإبدال الجارية بالغلام وهو ظاهر.

كتاب العتق باب العبد يعتق بعضه
آخره. فيمكن أن تكون الولادة من الأمور التي ليست ظاهرة فيوجب الشك فيها اعتبار الأحوال فيعتق نصف الأم كما في الجامع والله أعلم؛ كذا في فتح القدير وفيه نظر، لأن جعل الولادة من الأمور الخفية كمحبة القلب لا يصح لأن المراد بالأمور الظاهرة ما يمكن اطلاع الغير عليها والمراد بالخفية ما لا يمكن اطلاع الغير عليه ولا شك أن الولادة مما يمكن الاطلاع عليها ولذا اتفقوا أنه لا يقبل قول المرأة في الولادة ولو كانت كالمحبة لقبل قولها، وإنما اختلفوا هل يكتفي بشهادة المرأة أو لا بد من شهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين كما قدمناه. فالحق أن المسألة مشكلة لأنها لا توافق الأصول ولا يمكن الحكم بإبطال هذا الجواب كما في النهاية لأن جوابها نص الجامع الصغير، ولولا ذلك لتعين القول بما في النهاية، وقد ظهر للعبد الضعيف أن مشايخنا يعتبرون الأحوال عند تعدد الشرط وعند التعليق بشرط واحد له جزآن كمسألتنا.
قوله : (فإن العتق معلق على شرطه له جزآن إحداهما ولادة الغلام، وثانيهما كونه أول، ففي كل منهما إذا تحقق وجود البعض ووقع التردد في تعيينه فحينئذ تعتبر الأحوال، فإن في مسألتنا تحقق ولادة الغلام لكن لم يدر أنه أول بخلاف التعليق بدخول الدار ونحوه فإن الشرط شيء واحد ولم يتحقق وجوده فلا تعتبر الأحوال. فالحاصل أن الشرط إذا كان مركباً من جزئين فهو كالتعليق بشرطين. وبهذا التقدير يصح ما في الجامع الصغير وتتوافق الفروع مع الأصول كما لا يخفى والمراد بعدم علم الأول تصادقهم على عدم معرفة الأول، وقيد به لأنهم لو اتفقوا على أن ولادة الغلام أولاً أو اتفقوا على أن ولادة الجارية أولاً فلا يعتق أحد في الثاني ويعتق كل الأم والجارية في الأول فهي ثلاثة، والرابعة لو اختلفا فادعت الأم ولادة الغلام أولاً وأنكر المولى والجارية صغيرة فالقول قول المولى لأنه ينكر شرط العتق ويحلف على العلم لأنه فعل الغير ؛ فإن حلف لم يعتق واحد منهما إلا تقيم البينة بعد ذلك، وإن نكل عتقت الأم والبنت لأن دعوى الأم حرية الصغير معتبرة لأنها نفع محض ولها عليها ولاية لا سيما إذا لم يعرف لها أب. الخامسة أن تدعي الأم بأن الغلام هو الأول ولم تدع البنت وهي كبيرة فإنه يحلف المولى، فإن حلف لم يعتق واحد منهم، وإن نكل عتقت الأم دون البنت لأن النكول حجة ضرورية فلا تتعدى ولا ضرورة أن.
قوله: (ولا شك أن الولادة مما يمكن الإطلاع عليها قال في النهر : لا يخفى أنه ليس المراد بالولادة مطلقها بل التي الكلام فيها وهو كون الغلام أولاً وهذا مع ولادتهما في حمل واحد مما يخفى غالباً قوله : ( فالحاصل أن الشرط إذا كان مركباً الخ) تتوقف صحة هذا التعميم على صحة هذا الحكم في قوله لعبده إن دخلت الدار قبل زيد فأنت حر ووجد الدخول ولم تدر القبلية فإن مقتضى ما ذكره اعتبار الأحوال مع أن الرق ثابت بيقين ووقع الشك في زواله لعدم العلم بوقوع الجزء الآخر تأمل.
Chapter of Manumission: Section on a slave who is partially freed. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, there is no disagreement about it. What is mentioned by Muhammad in al-Kaysaniyyat regarding this issue is that he does not rule that any of them is freed, because we are not certain of manumission, and consideration of states (i'tibar al-ahwal) is after certainty of freedom, and it is not permissible to effect manumission with doubt. Based on this, al-Tahawi ruled that Muhammad was initially with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, then retracted. In al-Nihaya from al-Mabsut: This answer is not the answer for this chapter; rather, in this chapter, no one is ruled to be freed, but the master takes an oath by Allah that he does not know whether she gave birth to the girl first. If he refuses, his refusal is like his confession; if he swears, all are slaves. The answer for this chapter is only in the case where he says: 'If the first child you give birth to is a boy, you are free; if it is a girl, she is free,' and she gives birth to both and it is not known which was first: the boy is a slave, the female is free, and half of the mother is freed. There is no doubt that this is not the answer of the book because in this scenario the entire girl is freed in any case because if she gave birth to the girl first, she is freed by the condition; if she gave birth to the boy first, she is freed as a consequence of the mother. As for half of the mother being freed, it is because she is freed in the case of the boy being born first and remains a slave in the case of the girl. The answer of the book is that half of her is freed along with half of the mother. Al-Nihaya corrected what is in al-Kaysaniyyat because the condition whose existence is not certain, if it is on one side, the word is of the one who denies its existence, as when he says 'If you enter the house tomorrow, you are free,' then tomorrow passes and he does not know whether he entered the house or not, due to doubt in the condition of manumission. So similarly, doubt occurred in the condition of manumission, which is the birth of the boy first. When the condition is mentioned on both sides of existence and non-existence, then one of them must exist inevitably; then consideration of states is needed. If you say: The scenario in the book is that they agree on not knowing which was earlier and later, so how can he take an oath when there is no claim or dispute? I say: It is interpreted as a claim from an outsider (hissba) for the sake of freeing the slave woman or her daughter due to the existence of the condition. It is known that if the slave woman denies the manumission and testimony is given, it is accepted. Based on this, it is permissible for a man to make a claim for hisba if there is no evidence, so that he may take an oath hoping for his refusal. But what is mentioned in al-Mabsut in its reasoning states clearly that the mother claims manumission and the master denies, and the word is of the denier with his oath. So this indicates that it is in the case of the mother's claim, which is different from the case in the book. Know that what is mentioned in al-Nihaya preferring what is in al-Kaysaniyyat is essentially nullifying the statement of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, even though no odd transmission contrary to that in the answer has been narrated from them. His argument that the condition being on one side... may be considered that it is in the apparent condition, not the hidden one. Hence al-Mabsut conditioned where he said: If he says 'If you do such and such, you are free,' and that is among apparent matters like fasting, prayer, and entering the house, and the slave says 'I did it,' he is not believed except with evidence, contrary to his saying 'If you love me' up to the divorce of a specific woman revocably, then likewise; if it is irrevocable, it is an explanation of what is known that the irrevocable does not join the irrevocable. His statement: 'He does not know whether she gave birth to the girl or not' is found in most copies, and thus I saw it in al-Fath. In some copies it is corrected by replacing 'al-jariya' with 'al-ghulam', which is apparent. ... So it is possible that birth is among matters that are not apparent, so doubt about it necessitates consideration of states, so half of the mother is freed as in al-Jami'. Allah knows best. Thus in Fath al-Qadir, but there is a view: because making birth like hidden matters like love of the heart is not correct, because what is meant by apparent matters is what others can have knowledge of, and what is meant by hidden is what others cannot have knowledge of. There is no doubt that birth is something that can be known, hence they agreed that the woman's statement regarding birth is not accepted, whereas if it were like love, her statement would be accepted. They only disagreed whether the testimony of a woman is sufficient or whether the testimony of two men or one man and two women is necessary, as we have presented. The truth is that the issue is problematic because it does not conform to the principles, and it is not possible to rule invalidating this answer as in al-Nihaya because its answer is the text of al-Jami' al-Saghir. Were it not for that, the statement according to al-Nihaya would be determined. And it has become apparent to this weak servant that our shuyukh consider the states (ahwal) when there are multiple conditions and when the ta'liq is with a single condition that has two parts, like our issue. His statement: 'The manumission is suspended on its condition. It has two parts: one is the birth of the boy, and the second is his being first. So in each of them, if the existence of some is verified and hesitation occurs in its determination, then the states are considered. In our issue, the birth of the boy is verified but it is not known if he was first, contrary to the ta'liq on entering the house and the like, because the condition is one thing and its existence is not verified, so the states are not considered. The conclusion is that if the condition is composed of two parts, it is like ta'liq with two conditions. With this estimation, what is in al-Jami' al-Saghir becomes correct and the branches align with the principles, as is not hidden. What is meant by not knowing the first is their agreement on not knowing the first. It is restricted because if they agree that the birth of the boy was first or agree that the birth of the girl was first, then no one is freed in the second and the entire mother and girl are freed in the first. So there are three cases. The fourth: if they differ, the mother claims the boy was born first and the master denies and the girl is young, then the word is of the master because he denies the condition of manumission and he takes an oath based on knowledge because it is an act of another. If he swears, neither of them is freed unless evidence is established after that. If he refuses, the mother and the daughter are freed because the mother's claim of freedom for the young child is considered because it is pure benefit and she has guardianship over her, especially if no father is known. The fifth: the mother claims that the boy is the first and the daughter (who is adult) does not claim; then the master takes an oath. If he swears, none of them is freed; if he refuses, the mother is freed but not the daughter, because the refusal (nukul) is a necessary proof and does not extend beyond necessity. His statement: 'There is no doubt that birth is something that can be known.' In al-Nahr: It is not hidden that what is meant by birth here is not absolute birth but the one under discussion, which is the boy being first, and this, together with their being born in one pregnancy, is often hidden. His statement: 'The conclusion is that if the condition is composed, etc.' The correctness of this generalization depends on the correctness of this ruling in his saying to his slave: 'If you enter the house before Zaid, you are free' and entry occurs but it is not known whether it was before; then the implication of what he mentioned is consideration of states, even though slavery is established with certainty and doubt occurred in its removal due to lack of knowledge of the occurrence of the other part. (Consider carefully.)
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding a case of conditional manumission where twins are born and it is unknown which child was born first. The case: A master says to his pregnant slave woman, 'If the first child you give birth to is a boy, you are free; if it is a girl, she is free.' She gives birth to a boy and a girl, but it is unknown which came first. The Hanafi school has three positions: The position recorded in al-Jami' al-Saghir (attributed to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that the girl is freed entirely, the boy remains a slave, and half of the mother is freed. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani initially agreed but later retracted, as reported in al-Kaysaniyyat, ruling that none of them are freed because certainty of manumission is required and doubt prevents it. Al-Nihaya attempts to reconcile by stating that the master should take an oath, and if he refuses, all are freed; if he swears, all remain slaves. However, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq critically refines these views. He explains that the condition here is composite (murakkab): it has two parts—birth of a boy and the boy being first. Since the birth of a boy is certain but the 'firstness' is uncertain, this is different from a simple condition like 'enter the house,' where the entire condition is uncertain. Therefore, consideration of states (i'tibar al-ahwal) is necessary, which supports the ruling from al-Jami' al-Saghir. The author also addresses whether birth is an apparent or hidden matter, concluding that the specific fact of which twin was first is often hidden, justifying the consideration of states. He then enumerates five possible scenarios based on agreement or disagreement among the parties. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of al-Jami' al-Saghir, because it aligns with usul and is textually established. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of reconciling textual sources (manqul) with juristic reasoning (ma'qul).

Key Terms
الشرط (al-shart): The condition upon which manumission is suspended. Here, composite with two parts.
اعتبار الأحوال (i'tibar al-ahwal): Legal method of considering possible states proportionally when partial certainty exists.
العلة (al-illa): The effective cause in qiyas: partial certainty of one condition part.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What triggers i'tibar al-ahwal according to the passage?
A) Any uncertainty in a condition.
B) When the condition is composite and one part is certain.
C) When the master refuses to take an oath.
D) When the mother claims freedom.

Key Takeaway
I'tibar al-ahwal (consideration of states) is the Hanafi principle that resolves partial certainty in composite conditions by proportionally assigning rulings based on equally possible scenarios.

Conditional Emancipation and Compound Conditions
Expansion of conditional emancipation with compound condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of i'tibar al-ahwal to determine emancipation when a compound condition's parts are partially verified.

Core Idea
A compound condition acts as two separate conditions; consider circumstances when one part is known and the other is hidden.

When a master suspends emancipation on a condition with two parts, like giving birth to a boy AND him being first, the law treats each part independently. If one part is verified but the order of birth remains unknown, the jurists look to the circumstances—who claims what—to resolve the matter. This lesson unpacks the reasoning from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and shows how it applies to several scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the compound condition
The condition 'first-born boy' has two components: birth of a boy and being first. Recognize that in Hanafi law, this is equivalent to two separate conditions.
Compare with a simple condition like 'enter the house,' which is one unit.
2
Understand i'tibar al-ahwal
When facts are unknown, the law considers the circumstances—such as who claims and who denies emancipation—to reach a ruling.
This principle is applied here because the order of birth in a single pregnancy is often hidden.
3
Apply to the basic scenario
In the case of twins (boy and girl) with unknown order: the boy remains a slave (condition not fully met), the girl is free (since she could be first), and the mother is half-emancipated.
If they agree on order, the ruling changes accordingly.
4
Examine the six detailed cases
The text outlines scenarios where the mother, master, or children differ in claims. Determine who speaks and how oaths affect the outcome.
The master's word is taken when he denies the condition; refusal to swear leads to emancipation.
5
Generalize to multiple conditions
When the condition is multiple (e.g., separate if-boy-if-girl clauses), the same principles apply, leading to fractional emancipations when order is unknown.
Examples with two boys and two girls show the pattern of dividing shares.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن العتق معلق على شرطه له جزآن إحداهما ولادة الغلام، وثانيهما كونه أول، ففي كل منهما إذا تحقق وجود البعض ووقع التردد في تعيينه فحينئذ تعتبر الأحوال، فإن في مسألتنا تحقق ولادة الغلام لكن لم يدر أنه أول بخلاف التعليق بدخول الدار ونحوه فإن الشرط شيء واحد ولم يتحقق وجوده فلا تعتبر الأحوال. فالحاصل أن الشرط إذا كان مركباً من جزئين فهو كالتعليق بشرطين. وبهذا التقدير يصح ما في الجامع الصغير وتتوافق الفروع مع الأصول كما لا يخفى والمراد بعدم علم الأول تصادقهم على عدم معرفة الأول، وقيد به لأنهم لو اتفقوا على أن ولادة الغلام أولاً أو اتفقوا على أن ولادة الجارية أولاً فلا يعتق أحد في الثاني ويعتق كل الأم والجارية في الأول فهي ثلاثة، والرابعة لو اختلفا فادعت الأم ولادة الغلام أولاً وأنكر المولى والجارية صغيرة فالقول قول المولى لأنه ينكر شرط العتق ويحلف على العلم لأنه فعل الغير ؛ فإن حلف لم يعتق واحد منهما إلا تقيم البينة بعد ذلك، وإن نكل عتقت الأم والبنت لأن دعوى الأم حرية الصغير معتبرة لأنها نفع محض ولها عليها ولاية لا سيما إذا لم يعرف لها أب. الخامسة أن تدعي الأم بأن الغلام هو الأول ولم تدع البنت وهي كبيرة فإنه يحلف المولى، فإن حلف لم يعتق واحد منهم، وإن نكل عتقت الأم دون البنت لأن النكول حجة ضرورية فلا تتعدى ولا ضرورة. قوله: (ولا شك أن الولادة مما يمكن الإطلاع عليها قال في النهر : لا يخفى أنه ليس المراد بالولادة مطلقها بل التي الكلام فيها وهو كون الغلام أولاً وهذا مع ولادتهما في حمل واحد مما يخفى غالباً قوله : ( فالحاصل أن الشرط إذا كان مركباً الخ) تتوقف صحة هذا التعميم على صحة هذا الحكم في قوله لعبده إن دخلت الدار قبل زيد فأنت حر ووجد الدخول ولم تدر القبلية فإن مقتضى ما ذكره اعتبار الأحوال مع أن الرق ثابت بيقين ووقع الشك في زواله لعدم العلم بوقوع الجزء الآخر تأمل. السادسة أن تدعي البنت وهي كبيرة أن الغلام هو الأول ولم تدع الأم فتعتق البنت إذا نكل دون الأم لما ذكرنا . وقيد بكون الشرط واحداً لأنه لو كان متعدداً فهو على وجوه الأول لو قال إن كان أول ولد تلدينه غلاماً فأنت حرة، وإن كان جارية فهي حرة فولدتهما، فإن علم أنه أولاً عتق الأم والجارية لا غير وإن علم أن الجارية هي الأولى عتقت لا غير، وإن لم يعلم فالجارية حرة على كل حال والغلام عبد على كل حال ويعتق نصف الأم وتسعى في نصف قيمتها، وإن اختلفا فالقول قول المولى. الثاني لو قال إن كان أول ولد تلدينه غلاماً فهو حر، وإن كانت جارية فأنت حرة فولدتهما، فإن علم أنه الأول عتق هو لا غير، وإن علم أنها أولاً عتقت الأم والغلام لا غير، وإن لم يعلم فالغلام حر على كل والجارية رقيقة على كل حال ويعتق نصف الأم الثالث أن تلد غلامين وجاريتين والمسألة بحالها، فإن علم أن الأول ذكر عتق هو لا غير، وإن علم أنه جارية فهي رقيقة ومن سواها أحرار، وإن لم يعلم الأول يعتق من الغلامين من كل واحد منهما ثلاثة أرباعه ويسعى في ربع قيمته ويعتق من الأم نصفها ويعتق من البنتين من كل واحدة ربعها. الرابع لو قال إذا جارية فأنت حرة، وإن ولدت جارية ثم غلاماً فالغلام حر فولدتهما، فإن كان الغلام أولاً عتقت الأم والغلام والجارية رقيقان وإن كانت الجارية أولاً عتق الغلام والأم والجارية رقيقان، وإن لم يعلم الأول باتفاقهما فالجارية رقيقة، وأما الغلام والأم فإنه يعتق من كل واحد منهما نصفه وإن اختلفا فالقول قول المولى مع يمينه. الخامس لو ولدت غلامين وجاريتين والمسألة بحالها، فإن ولدت غلامين ثم جاريتين عتقت الأم وعتقت الجارية الثانية بعتقها وبقي الغلامان والجارية الأولى رقيقاً، وإن ولدت غلاماً ثم جاريتين ثم غلاماً عتقت الأم والجارية الثانية والغلام الثاني بعتق الأم، وإن ولدت جاريتين ثم غلامين عتق الغلام الأول وبقي من سواه رقيقاً، وكذا إذا ولدت جارية ثم غلامين ثم جارية عتق الغلام الأول لا غير وكذا إذا ولدت جارية ثم غلاماً ثم جارية ثم غلاماً الغلام الأول، وإن لم يعلم باتفاقهم يعتق من الأولاد من كل واحد ربعه ويعتق من الأم نصفها، وإن اختلفوا فالقول قول المولى مع يمينه؛ كذا في البدائع بحذف التعليل.
He said: (Emancipation is suspended on its condition having two parts: one is the birth of a boy, and the second is his being first. So in each of them, when partial existence is verified and there is hesitation in specifying it, then consideration of circumstances applies. In our case, the birth of a boy is verified but it is not known whether he is first, unlike suspension on entering the house etc., for the condition is one thing and its existence is not verified, so circumstances are not considered. The upshot: if the condition is composed of two parts, it is like suspension on two conditions. With this estimation, what is in al-Jami' al-Saghir is correct and the branches align with the principles. What is meant by not knowing the first is their agreement on not knowing the first. It is restricted because if they agree that the boy's birth was first or that the girl's birth was first, then no one is emancipated in the second, and the mother and girl are both emancipated in the first. So these are three. The fourth: if they differ: the mother claims the boy's birth was first, the master denies, and the girl is minor, then the master's word is accepted because he denies the condition of emancipation and takes an oath on knowledge because it is the act of another. If he swears, neither is emancipated unless they later establish evidence. If he refuses, the mother and daughter are emancipated because the mother's claim of freedom for the minor is considered as it is pure benefit and she has guardianship over her, especially if she has no known father. The fifth: the mother claims the boy is first and the daughter (being adult) does not claim, then the master takes an oath. If he swears, none are emancipated. If he refuses, the mother is emancipated without the daughter because refusal is a necessary proof and does not extend beyond necessity. He also said: (There is no doubt that birth is something that can be known). He said in al-Nahr: It is not hidden that what is meant is not absolute birth but the one under discussion, i.e. the boy being first, and this with their birth in one pregnancy is often hidden. He said: (The upshot: if the condition is composed etc.) The validity of this generalization depends on the validity of this ruling in his statement to his slave: 'If you enter the house before Zayd, you are free' and he entered but it is not known whether he entered before; then what he mentioned necessitates consideration of circumstances, while slavery is firmly established and doubt arises about its removal due to lack of knowledge of the occurrence of the other part. Consider. The sixth: the adult daughter claims the boy is first and the mother does not claim, then the daughter is emancipated if the master refuses, without the mother, for reasons mentioned. The condition being one is restricted because if it is multiple, then it has forms: First: if he said: 'If the first child you bear is a boy, you are free, and if it is a girl, she is free,' and she bore twins, then if it is known he is first, the mother and girl are emancipated, no other. If it is known the girl is first, she alone is emancipated. If not known, the girl is free in any case, the boy is a slave in any case, and half of the mother is emancipated and she works for half her value. If they differ, the master's word is accepted. Second: if he said: 'If the first child you bear is a boy, he is free, and if it is a girl, you are free,' and she bore twins, then if it is known he is first, he alone is emancipated. If it is known she is first, the mother and boy are emancipated, no other. If not known, the boy is free in any case, the girl is a slave in any case, and half of the mother is emancipated. Third: she bears two boys and two girls, and the case is as before. If it is known the first is male, he alone is emancipated. If it is known it is female, she is a slave and all others are free. If the first is not known, from each of the two boys three-quarters are emancipated and he works for a quarter of his value, half of the mother is emancipated, and from each of the two girls a quarter is emancipated. Fourth: if he said: 'If it is a girl, you are free, and if you bear a girl then a boy, the boy is free,' and she bore twins, then if the boy is first, the mother and boy are emancipated and the girl is a slave. If the girl is first, the boy and mother are emancipated and the girl is a slave. If the first is not known by their agreement, the girl is a slave. As for the boy and mother, half of each is emancipated. If they differ, the master's word is accepted with his oath. Fifth: if she bears two boys and two girls, and the case is as before, then if she bears two boys then two girls, the mother is emancipated and the second girl is emancipated by her emancipation, and the two boys and first girl remain slaves. If she bears a boy then two girls then a boy, the mother, second girl, and second boy are emancipated by the mother's emancipation. If she bears two girls then two boys, the first boy is emancipated and all others remain slaves. Likewise if she bears a girl then two boys then a girl, only the first boy is emancipated. Likewise if she bears a girl then a boy then a girl then a boy, only the first boy. And if not known by their agreement, from each child a quarter is emancipated and from the mother half. If they differ, the master's word is accepted with his oath. So in al-Bada'i' with omission of reasoning.
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding the ruling on conditional emancipation when a slave woman gives birth to twins and the order of birth is unknown. The passage type is 'ruling with proof,' where the author defends the principle of i'tibar al-ahwal (consideration of circumstances) as applied in Al-Jami' al-Saghir. The core reasoning: when a condition has two components (e.g., giving birth to a male AND being first), each component is like a separate condition. If part of the condition is verified but the other part cannot be known, circumstances (like who claims what) are considered to determine the outcome. The author addresses an objection that birth is not a hidden matter, noting that the specific issue here is knowing which child was first, which is often hidden in a single pregnancy. The passage then provides six detailed scenarios (from 'al-rabi'ah' to 'al-sadisah') and further cases when the condition is multiple (e.g., separate conditions for boy and girl). The overall ruling level is per Hanafi fiqh: such conditional emancipation statements are valid, and the principle of considering circumstances applies when the condition is compound. The authority weight is from the zahir al-riwayah as found in Al-Jami' al-Saghir and Al-Bada'i'.

Key Terms
إعتبار الأحوال (i'tibar al-ahwal): Consideration of circumstances, such as who makes the claim and who denies, to determine legal outcome when facts are unknown.
شرط مركب (shart murakkab): A condition composed of two independent parts, like giving birth to a male AND being the firstborn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master says to his slave woman: 'If you give birth to a boy first, you are free,' and she gives birth to twins (a boy and a girl) but it is unknown which was born first, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The boy is free, the mother remains a slave.
B) The girl is free, the mother remains a slave.
C) Half of the mother is emancipated and she works for half her value.
D) Nothing happens, the condition is void.

Key Takeaway
A compound condition is treated as two separate conditions; when one part is verified and the other is hidden, i'tibar al-ahwal determines the outcome.

Oath of Manumission Covers Future Slaves
Ruling on oath covering future slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that an oath of manumission (al-ḥalif bi al-‘itq) applies to slaves acquired after the oath but before the condition is fulfilled, and identify the authoritative support for this ruling.

Core Idea
An oath freeing slaves on a future day covers slaves acquired later but before that day.

This passage from Bahr al-Rāʼiq establishes a key ruling: if a person swears that all slaves he owns on a specific day are free, and later acquires new slaves before that day arrives, the new slaves are also freed. We will unpack the reasoning behind this ruling and see why later Hanafi authorities upheld it against objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath and its condition
Note the wording: 'If I enter, then every slave I own on that day is free.' The condition is entering, and the subject is all slaves owned on that day.
The day refers to the day the condition is fulfilled, not the day of the oath.
2
Determine the scope of ownership
Consider whether 'on that day' includes only slaves owned at the time of the oath or also those acquired later. The passage explicitly states that slaves owned afterward (ba‘dahu) are included.
The phrase 'عَقَّ مَا يَمْلِكُهُ بَعْدَهُ' indicates the oath applies to future acquisitions.
3
Recognize the authority behind the ruling
The passage cites Fakhr al-Islam and the author of al-Kāfī (a Hanafi text) as validating this ruling, and notes that the commentators approved it. This gives the ruling a strong position in the Hanafi school.
This is the muftā bihī (operative opinion) in the school.
4
Apply the ruling to a concrete case
Suppose a man says, 'If I enter the house, every slave I own on that day is free.' He then buys a new slave the next day, and enters the house a week later. The new slave becomes free upon entry.
The condition (entry) triggers the manumission for all slaves owned at that moment, including the recently acquired one.
5
Note the counter-argument and its refutation
The passage mentions that some claimed this ruling is invalid, but the authorities rejected that claim. The correct position is that the ruling is sound.
This is an example of legitimate ikhtilāf within the Hanafi tradition.

Interpretation of 'Yawma'idhin' in Suspended Emancipation Oaths
Explanation of the phrase 'يومئذ' in suspended emancipation oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the interpretation of 'yawma'idhin' in suspended emancipation oaths and apply it to determine which slaves are emancipated.

Core Idea
In suspended emancipation, 'that day' means the time the condition occurs, not when the oath is spoken.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into a subtle point of Hanafi fiqh: the temporal reference of 'yawma'idhin' in oaths of suspended emancipation. Understanding this is crucial for correctly applying the oath to the appropriate slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and condition
The act is suspended emancipation (ta'liq al-'itq) on a condition like entry. The phrase 'yawma'idhin' determines the time of emancipation.
2
Analyze the phrase 'yawma'idhin'
The tanwin on 'yawm' substitutes for the deleted clause 'idh' meaning 'when'. Thus 'that day' refers to the time of the condition, not the time of the oath.
Linguistic analysis: 'idh' is not semantically considered; it's a placeholder.
3
Derive the ruling
Slaves owned at the moment the condition occurs are emancipated. This includes slaves acquired after the oath but before the condition, but excludes slaves owned before but not at the condition.
The slave must be in the owner's possession at the exact time of the condition.
4
Support with Quranic analogy
The Quranic verse 'wa yawma'idhin yafrahu al-mu'minun' uses the same construction; 'idh' does not add temporal meaning.
5
Distinguish the contrary case
If one says about another's slave 'If you enter, my slave is free' and then buys that slave, the emancipation does not occur because the oath was not annexed to ownership at the time of entry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العتق باب الحلف بالعتق العتق جزاء على الحلف بأن يعلق العتق بشيء وهو شروع في بيان التعليق بعد ما ذكر مسائل التنجيز. وإنما ذكر مسألة التعليق بالولادة في باب عتق البعض لبيان أنه يعتق منه البعض عند عدم العلم. والحلف بفتح الحاء سكون اللام وكسرها مصدر قولهم حلف بالله يحلف مع حلفاً وحلفاً القسم، وبكسر الحاء مع سكون اللام العهد قوله : (ومن قال إن دخلت فكل مملوك لي يومئذ حر عتق ما يملكه بعده به أي بعد هذا القول بالدخول لأن التنوين في يومئذ عوض عن الجملة المضاف إليها لفظ إذ تقديره إذا دخلت . ولفظ «يوم)) ظرف للمملوك فكان التقدير كل من يكون في ملكي وقت الدخول حر. وهذا في الحقيقة إضافة عتق المملوك يوم الدخول إلى الدخول، والمملوك لا يكون إلا بملك فصار كأنه قال إن ملكت مملوكاً وقت يوم الدخول فهو حر وهو يصدق بملك قبل الدخول يقارن بقاءه الدخول فكأنه إضافة العتق إلى الملك الموجود عند الدخول بخلاف قوله لعبد غيره إن دخلت الدار فعبدي حر فاشتراه فدخل لا يعتق لأنه لم يضف العتق إلى ملكه لا صريحاً ولا معنى والمراد باليوم هنا مطلق الوقت حتى لو دخل ليلاً عتق ما في ملكه لأنه أضيف إلى فعل لا يمتد وهو الدخول وإن كان في اللفظ إنما أضيف إلى لفظ (إذ المضافة للدخول لكن معنى إذ غير ملاحظ وإلا كان المراد يوم وقت الدخول، وهو وإن كان يمكن على معنى يوم الوقت الذي فيه الدخول تقييداً لليوم به لكن إذا أريد به مطلق الوقت يصير المعنى وقت وقت الدخول ونحن نعلم مثله كثيراً في الاستعمال الفصيح كنحو ويومئذ يفرح المؤمنون بنصر الله ولا يلاحظ فيه شيء من ذلك فإنه لا يلاحظ في هذه الآية وقت يغلبون يفرح المؤمنون، ولا يوم وقت يغلبون يفرحون، ونظائره كثيرة في كتاب الله تعالى وغيره، فعرف أن لفظ «إذ» لم يذكر إلا تكثيراً للعوض عن الجملة المحذوفة أو عماداً له أعني التنوين لكونه حرفاً واحداً ساكناً تحسيناً لم يلاحظ معناها، ومثله كثير في أقوال أهل العربية في بعض الألفاظ لا يخفى على من له نظر فيها؛ كذا في فتح القدير.
Book of Emancipation, Chapter on Oaths by Emancipation. Emancipation is a recompense for the oath, by suspending emancipation on something; this is a start in explaining suspension after mentioning matters of immediate effect. He only mentioned the issue of suspension by birth in the Chapter on Emancipation of a Part, to clarify that part of him is emancipated when unaware. Al-half (oath) with fatha on ha, sukun on lam, and kasra on ha is the verbal noun of their saying 'halafa billahi yahlifu' meaning an oath; with kasra on ha and sukun on lam it means covenant. His saying: "And whoever says, 'If you enter, then every slave of mine on that day is free,' then what he owns after this statement, i.e., after this statement, [becomes free] upon entry, because the tanwin in 'yawma'idhin' substitutes for the clause to which the word 'idh' is added; its implied meaning is 'when you enter.' The word 'yawm' is a time adverb for the slave, so the implied meaning is: everyone who is in my ownership at the time of entry is free. This is in reality annexing the emancipation of the slave on the day of entry to the entry, and a slave only exists through ownership, so it is as if he said: if I own a slave at the time of the day of entry, then he is free. This is true for ownership before entry whose continuation coincides with entry, so it is as if he annexed emancipation to the ownership existing at the time of entry, unlike his saying regarding another's slave, 'If you enter the house, then my slave is free,' then he bought him and entered—he is not emancipated, because he did not annex emancipation to his ownership explicitly or implicitly. What is meant by 'yawm' here is absolute time, so even if he entered at night, what he owns is emancipated, because he annexed it to an action that does not extend, i.e., entry. Although in wording he annexed it to the word 'idh' which is added to entry, the meaning of 'idh' is not considered; otherwise, it would mean the day of the time of entry. And although it is possible to mean the day of the time in which entry occurs, restricting the day to it, but if absolute time is intended, the meaning becomes 'the time of the time of entry'. We know many such instances in eloquent usage, like 'And on that day the believers will rejoice in the help of Allah'—nothing of that is considered; for in this verse, it is not considered that at the time they are vanquished the believers rejoice, nor the day of the time they are vanquished they rejoice. Its parallels are many in the Book of Allah and elsewhere. So it is known that the word 'idh' was mentioned only to increase the substitution for the deleted clause or as a support for it, meaning the tanwin, because it is a single silent letter to beautify, and its meaning is not considered. Similarly, many such [usages] exist in the statements of Arabic scholars regarding some words, not hidden from one who examines them. Thus in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe explaining the ruling in Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the phrase 'كل مملوك لي يومئذ حر' in oaths of emancipation. The author clarifies that 'يومئذ' refers to the time when the condition (e.g., entry) occurs, not the time of the oath. The tanwin in 'يومئذ' compensates for the deleted clause 'إذ' meaning 'when'. Thus, the slave must be owned at the moment of the condition's fulfillment. The author supports this with linguistic analysis, showing that 'يوم' here means absolute time, so even nighttime entry triggers the emancipation. The analogy to the Quranic verse 'ويومئذ يفرح المؤمنون' demonstrates that 'إذ' is not semantically considered; it merely substitutes for the clause. Therefore, the ruling is that slaves acquired after the oath but before the condition are included, while slaves owned before the condition but not at its occurrence are not.

Key Terms
يومئذ (yawma'idhin): A compound word meaning 'on that day', where 'yawm' is day and 'idh' is a particle for past time, but here the tanwin substitutes for a clause, referring to the time of the condition's occurrence.
عتق (itq): Emancipation of a slave; in this context, it is the legal consequence (jaza') of an oath, made conditional on a future event.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending a legal effect (here emancipation) on the occurrence of a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'يومئذ' in the phrase 'كل مملوك لي يومئذ حر' refer to?
A) The day the oath is spoken.
B) The time of the condition's occurrence (e.g., entry).
C) The day the slave is purchased.
D) The day after the oath.

Key Takeaway
In suspended emancipation, 'that day' refers to the time of the condition, so only slaves owned at that moment are emancipated.

8 min
Scope of 'كل مملوك أملكه اليوم' in Emancipation Oaths
Ruling on 'كل مملوك أملكه اليوم' from al-Badai'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that the phrase 'كل مملوك أملكه اليوم' in an emancipation oath refers only to slaves owned at the time of the oath, not those acquired later in the day.

Core Idea
A time specification must be beneficial; 'today' only covers slaves owned at the oath.

When a person swears an emancipation oath using the phrase 'كل مملوك أملكه اليوم' (every slave I own today), the word 'today' is a time restriction. For the restriction to be meaningful, it must exclude something. If it applied to all slaves owned at any time, the word would be superfluous. The Hanafi school therefore interprets it as covering only the slaves owned at the moment of the oath.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath phrase
The phrase is 'كل مملوك أملكه اليوم' – note the present tense verb 'أملكه' and the time word 'اليوم'.
The verb form is ambiguous; the time word resolves it.
2
Apply the beneficial specification rule
The time restriction must be beneficial (مفيد). If it applied to all current and future slaves, it would not add anything. So it must restrict something.
This is a principle of interpretation in oaths.
3
Determine the restricted scope
Since the restriction is beneficial, 'today' limits the ownership to that existing at the time of the oath. Slaves acquired later in the day are not included.
The same applies to 'this month' or 'this year'.
4
Consider private intention
If the person later says he meant only one category (e.g., only current slaves), he is not believed in court because it contradicts the apparent meaning, but he is believed between himself and Allah.
This is a standard Hanafi rule for general words with a specific intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال المصنف عتق ما هو مملوك له وقت الدخول لكان أظهر لأن ما كان في ملكه وقت الحلف واستمر إلى وقت الدخول لم يملكه بعد اليمين ملكاً متجدداً. وفي ذلك البدائع : لو قال كل مملوك أملكه اليوم فهو حر ولا نية له وله مملوك فاستفاد في يومه مملوكاً آخر عتق ما في ملكه وما استفاد ملكه في اليوم، وكذا لو قال هذا الشهر أو هذه السنة لأنه لما وقت باليوم أو الشهر أو السنة فلا بد وأن يكون التوقيت مفيداً، ولو لم يتناول إلا ما في ملکه الحلف لم يكن مفيداً، فإن قال عنيت أحد الصنفين دون الآخر لم يدين يوم في القضاء لأنه نوى تخصيص العموم وأنه خلاف الظاهر فلا يصدق في القضاء ويصدق فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى لأن الله تعالى مطلع على نيته وفي البدائع أيضاً: لو قال كل مملوك اشتريه هو حر إن كلمت فلاناً أو إذا كلمت فلاناً أو إذا جاء الغد ولا نية له فهذا يقع على ما يشتريه قبل الكلام، فكل مملوك اشتراه قبل الكلام ثم كلم عتق وما اشتراه بعد الكلام لا يعتق، ولو قدم الشرط فقال إن كلمت فلاناً أو إذا كلمت فلاناً أو إذا جاء غد فكل مملوك اشتريه فهو حر فهذا على ما يشتريه بعد الكلام لا قبله حتى لو كان اشترى مماليك قبل الكلام ثم كلم لا يعتق واحد منهم وما اشتراه بعده يعتق ولو قال كل مملوك اشتريه إذا دخلت الدار فهو حر، أو قال إن قدم فلان فهذا على ما يشتري بعد الفعل الذي حلف عليه ولا يعتق ما اشترى قبل ذلك إلا أن يعينهم .
And if the author had said 'what is owned by him at the time of entry' it would be more apparent, because what was in his ownership at the time of the oath and continued until the time of entry—he did not own it after the oath as a renewed ownership. And in that regard, in al-Badai': if he said 'every slave I own today is free' and he has no intention, and he has a slave, and he acquires another slave during his day, then what is in his ownership [at the time of the oath] is emancipated, and what he acquired ownership of during the day is not. Similarly, if he said 'this month' or 'this year', because when he specified with 'day', 'month', or 'year', the specification must be beneficial. If it did not include except what was in his ownership at the time of the oath, it would not be beneficial. Then if he said 'I meant one of the two categories, not the other', he is not believed in court because he intended to specify the general, which contradicts the apparent, so he is not believed in court, but he is believed between himself and Allah, because Allah is aware of his intention. Also in al-Badai': if he said 'every slave I buy is free if I speak to so-and-so' or 'when I speak to so-and-so' or 'when tomorrow comes', and he has no intention, then this applies to what he buys before the speech. So every slave he bought before the speech then he spoke is emancipated, and what he bought after the speech is not emancipated. And if he placed the condition first and said 'if I speak to so-and-so' or 'when I speak to so-and-so' or 'when tomorrow comes, then every slave I buy is free', then this applies to what he buys after the speech, not before. So if he had bought slaves before the speech then spoke, none of them are emancipated, and what he buys after is emancipated. And if he said 'every slave I buy if I enter the house is free', or said 'if so-and-so arrives', then this applies to what he buys after the action he swore by, and what he bought before that is not emancipated unless he specifies them.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from al-Badai' that illustrate how time-related wording affects the scope of emancipation oaths. The first ruling concerns 'كل مملوك أملكه اليوم': the word 'today' restricts the application to slaves owned at the time of the oath; those acquired later that day are not included. This makes the time specification beneficial—if it only applied to current slaves, it would be redundant. The second ruling concerns 'كل مملوك اشتريه' with a condition like 'if I speak to so-and-so'. If the condition is stated after the purchase phrase (e.g., 'every slave I buy is free if I speak'), it applies to slaves bought before the speech; if the condition is stated first (e.g., 'if I speak, then every slave I buy is free'), it applies to slaves bought after the speech. The key distinction is the order: when the purchase phrase precedes the condition, the purchase action is suspended on the condition, so the reference is to purchases made before the condition occurs; when the condition precedes, the condition triggers the emancipation for future purchases.

Key Terms
أملكه (amlikuhu): Present tense verb meaning 'I own' or 'I acquire ownership of'; in the oath it is interpreted as referring to the present moment unless specified otherwise.
اليوم (al-yawm): Time word meaning 'today' – restricts the scope of the oath to the day of the oath.
توقيت (tawqit): Specification of time; must be beneficial for the ruling to have meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says 'كل مملوك أملكه اليوم' and currently owns no slaves, then later in the day acquires a slave, what happens to that slave?
A) The slave is emancipated because the oath covers the whole day.
B) The slave is not emancipated because the oath only covers ownership at the time of the oath.
C) The slave is emancipated only if the owner had a slave at the time of the oath.
D) The slave is not emancipated but the owner must pay a penalty.

Key Takeaway
In a Hanafi oath of emancipation, a time word like 'today' restricts the scope to slaves owned at the moment of the oath, not those acquired later.

Order of Condition and Purchase in Emancipation Oaths
Ruling on condition order in emancipation oaths from al-Badai'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine which purchases are covered in an oath linking purchase and a condition, based on the order of the clauses.

Core Idea
The order of condition and purchase phrase determines whether the oath covers past or future purchases.

When a person makes an emancipation oath that links the act of buying a slave with a condition (like speaking to someone), the order in which the purchase phrase and the condition appear is crucial. The passage from al-Badai' explains that if the purchase phrase comes first, the oath applies to purchases made before the condition is fulfilled; if the condition comes first, it applies to purchases made after the condition is fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possible orders
First order: 'كل مملوك اشتريه هو حر إن كلمت فلاناً' (purchase phrase first). Second order: 'إن كلمت فلاناً فكل مملوك اشتريه هو حر' (condition first).
The word 'إن' or 'إذا' marks the condition.
2
Analyze the first order (purchase phrase first)
When the purchase phrase precedes the condition, the oath is interpreted as applying to purchases made before the condition is fulfilled. So if he buys a slave before speaking, then speaks, that slave is emancipated.
The condition determines the trigger moment for the emancipation, but the purchase must precede it.
3
Analyze the second order (condition first)
When the condition precedes the purchase phrase, the oath applies to purchases made after the condition is fulfilled. So if he buys a slave before speaking, that slave is not covered; only purchases after speaking are covered.
The condition is like a trigger that activates the oath for future purchases.
4
Apply to other formulations
The same principle applies to other conditions like 'if I enter the house' or 'if so-and-so arrives'. The ruling depends on whether the purchase phrase or the condition comes first.
The passage explicitly says: 'هذا على ما يشتري بعد الفعل الذي حلف عليه'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if the author had said 'what is owned by him at the time of entry' it would be more apparent, because what was in his ownership at the time of the oath and continued until the time of entry—he did not own it after the oath as a renewed ownership. And in that regard, in al-Badai': if he said 'every slave I own today is free' and he has no intention, and he has a slave, and he acquires another slave during his day, then what is in his ownership [at the time of the oath] is emancipated, and what he acquired ownership of during the day is not. Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from al-Badai' that illustrate how time-related wording affects the scope of emancipation oaths. The first ruling concerns 'كل مملوك أملكه اليوم': the word 'today' restricts the application to slaves owned at the time of the oath; those acquired later that day are not included. The key distinction is the order: when the purchase phrase precedes the condition, the purchase action is suspended on the condition, so the reference is to purchases made before the condition occurs; when the condition precedes, the condition triggers the emancipation for future purchases.

Key Terms
اشتريه (ashtarihi): Present tense verb meaning 'I buy'; in the oath, it may refer to future purchases depending on the position of the condition.
إن (in): Conditional particle meaning 'if'; in oaths, it can indicate a future condition.
إذا (idha): Conditional particle meaning 'when'; often implies a condition expected to be fulfilled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man swears 'إن قدم فلان فكل مملوك اشتريه هو حر'. He buys a slave before the arrival, then the man arrives. What happens?
A) The slave is freed because the condition was fulfilled.
B) The slave is not freed because the condition comes first, so the oath covers purchases after the arrival.
C) The slave is freed only if the arrival was unexpected.
D) The slave is not freed because the oath is invalid.

Key Takeaway
In conditional emancipation oaths, the order of the purchase phrase and the condition determines whether the oath covers purchases before or after the condition is fulfilled.
