قبل لعدم الشرط. الخامسة لو أبرأ المولى العبد عن الألف لم يعتق ولو أبرأ المكاتب عتق ؛ كذا ذكروها والظاهر أنه لا موقع لها إذا الفرق بعد تحقق الإبراء في الموضعين يكون والإبراء لا يتصور في هذه المسألة لأنه لا دين على العبد بخلاف الكتابة السادسة لو باع المولى العبد ثم اشتراه أو رد عليه بخيار عيب ففي وجوب قبول ما يأتي به خلاف عند أبي يوسف نعم، وعند محمد لا ولكن لو قبضه عتق بخلاف الكتابة في أنه لا خلاف في أنه يجب أن يقبله ويعد قابضاً. السابعة أنه يقتصر على المجلس فلا يعتق ما لم يؤد في ذلك المجلس فلو اختلف بأن أعرض أو أخذ في عمل آخر فأدى لا يعتق بخلاف الكتابة وهذا إذا كان المذكور من أدوات الشرط لفظة «إن» فإن كان لفظ «إذا» أو «متى» فلا يقتصر على المجلس الثامنة أنه يجوز للمولى بيع العبد بعد قوله ذلك قبل أن يؤدي بخلاف الكاتبة التاسعة أن للسيد أن يأخذ ما يظفر به مما اكتسبه قبل أن يأتيه بما يؤديه بخلاف المكاتب العاشرة أنه إذا أدى وعتق وفضل عنده مال مما اكتسبه كان للسيد فيأخذه بخلاف المكاتب الحادية عشرة لو اكتسب العبد مالاً قبل تعليق السيد فأداه بعده إليه عتق وإن كان السيد يرجع بمثله على ما سيذكر بخلاف الكتابة لا يعتق بأدائه لأنه ملك المولى إلا أن يكون كاتبه على نفسه وماله فإنه حينئذ يصير أحق به. وفي البدائع ذكر محمد في الزيادات إذا قال إن أديت ألفاً في كيس أبيض فأنت فأداها حر في كيس أسود لا يعتق وفي الكتابة يعتق ا هـ . وهي الثانية عشر. ولو قال إذا أديت ألفاً في هذا الشهر فأنت حر فلم يؤدها في ذلك الشهر وأداها في غيره لم يعتق وفي الكتابة لا يبطل إلا بحكم الحاكم أو بتراضيهما كما في البدائع. وهي الثالثة عشر وفي المحيط : لو أمر غيره بالأداء فأدى لا يعتق لأن الشرط أداؤه ولم يوجد فلا حاجة إلى أداء غيره لأنه قادر على أدائه بخلاف الكتابة لأنها معاوضة حقيقة فيها معنى التعليق فكان الأصل فيها المعاوضة فكان المقصود حصول البدل ا هـ . وهي الرابعة عشر . وفي الذخيرة إذا قال إن أديت إلي ألفاً فأنت حر فاستقرض العبد من رجل ألفاً فدفعها إلى مولاه عتق العبد ورجع غريم العبد على المولى فيأخذ منه الألف لأنه أحق بها من المولى من قبل أنه عبد مأذون له في التجارة وغرماء العبد المأذون أحق بماله حتى يستوفوا ديونهم. ولو كان العبد استقرض من رجل ألفي درهم وقيمته ألفاً درهم فدفع أحد الألفين إلى مولاه وعتق بها وأكل الألف الأخرى فإن للمقرض أن يأخذ من المولى الألف التي دفعها العبد إليه ويضمن المولى أيضاً للغريم الألف لأن المولى منع العبد بعتقه من يباع بما عليه من الدين، وإن شاء المقرض اتبع العبد بجميع دينه أيضاً ا هـ. قيد بالتعليق لأنه لو لم يأت في الجواب بالفاء لا يتعلق بل يتنجز، سواء كان الجواب بالواو كقوله إن أديت إلي ألفاً وأنت حر ولا كقوله إن أديت إلي ألفاً أنت حر لكونه ابتداء لا جواباً لعدم الرابط. وفي الذخيرة قال لعبده أنت حر وأد إلي ألف درهم فهو حر ولا شيء عليه، ولو قال أدا إلي ألفاً وأنت حر لم يعتق حتى يؤدي، ولو قال فأنت حر عتق للحال لأن جواب الأمر بالواو لا بالفاء فهي للتعليل أي أدا لي ألفاً لأنك حر كقوله أبشر فقد أتاك الغوث وتمامه في الأصول من بحث الواو . وقد قدمنا في بحث عتق الحمل من الظهيرية أنه لو علق عتق الحمل بأدائه ألفاً فإنه يتوقف العتق على أدائه، فإذا أدى بعد الولادة عتق إذا ولدته لأقل من ستة أشهر. وقيد بأداء العبد لأنه لو علق عتقه بأداء أجنبي لا مأذوناً له كما إذا قال إذا أديت إلي ألفاً فعبدي هذا حر فجاء الأجنبي بألف ووضعها بين يديه يصير حراً؟ تأمل.
His statement: (And if he suspends his manumission on his payment, he becomes authorized) meaning by payment of money, such as saying: 'If you pay me a thousand, you are free.' So it is valid and he is freed at the time of payment without becoming a mukatab, because it is explicit in suspending manumission on payment, although it contains the meaning of exchange at the end. He only becomes authorized because it is a desire for earning by demanding payment from him, and his intent is trade not begging, so it is an implicit permission. It is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir that it differs from the mukatab in eleven matters: First, if the slave dies before payment and leaves property, it belongs to the master and nothing is paid from it on his behalf and he does not become free, contrary to kitabah. Second, if the master dies and the slave has earnings in hand, they belong to the master's heirs and the slave is sold, contrary to kitabah. Third, if the slave is a female and she gives birth then pays and becomes free, her child does not become free because she did not have the ruling of kitabah at the time of birth, contrary to kitabah. Fourth, if the slave says to the master: 'Deduct one hundred from me,' and the master deducts and he pays nine hundred, he does not become free, contrary to kitabah. In al-Bada'i': if he pays dinars instead of dirhams, he does not become free, even if accepted, due to absence of condition. Fifth, if the master releases the slave from the thousand, he does not become free; if he releases the mukatab, he becomes free. They mentioned it, but apparently it has no place because the difference after the occurrence of release in both places would be that release is inconceivable in this issue because there is no debt on the slave, contrary to kitabah. Sixth, if the master sells the slave then buys him back or he is returned to him due to an option of defect, then regarding the obligation to accept what he brings, there is disagreement: according to Abu Yusuf, yes; according to Muhammad, no. But if he takes it, he becomes free, contrary to kitabah where there is no disagreement that he must accept it and is considered a receiver. Seventh, it is confined to the session, so he does not become free unless he pays in that session; if he delays by turning away or engaging in another work and then pays, he does not become free, contrary to kitabah. This is if the conditional particle is 'in'; if it is 'idha' or 'mata', it is not confined to the session. Eighth, the master may sell the slave after saying that before he pays, contrary to kitabah. Ninth, the master may take whatever he finds of what the slave earned before he brings the payment, contrary to the mukatab. Tenth, when he pays and becomes free and there remains surplus earnings in his hand, it belongs to the master and he takes it, contrary to the mukatab. Eleventh, if the slave earned money before the master's suspension and then pays it afterwards to him, he becomes free, although the master has recourse for the like of it as will be mentioned, contrary to kitabah: he does not become free by paying it because it is the master's property, unless he contracted kitabah on himself and his property, then he becomes more entitled to it. In al-Bada'i', Muhammad mentioned in al-Ziyadat: if he says 'If you pay a thousand in a white bag, you are free' and he pays it in a black bag, he does not become free; in kitabah he becomes free. That is the twelfth. And if he says 'If you pay a thousand in this month, you are free' and he does not pay it in that month but pays in another, he does not become free; in kitabah it is not void except by a judge's ruling or mutual agreement, as in al-Bada'i'. That is the thirteenth. In al-Muhit: if he orders another to pay and he pays, he does not become free because the condition is his payment and it did not occur, so there is no need for another's payment since he is able to pay, contrary to kitabah because it is a true exchange with a sense of suspension, so the basis is exchange, so the goal is obtaining the substitute. That is the fourteenth. In al-Dhakhirah: if he says 'If you pay me a thousand, you are free' and the slave borrows a thousand from a man and hands it to his master, the slave becomes free and the creditor has recourse against the master, taking the thousand from him because he is more entitled to it than the master, since he is a slave authorized to trade, and creditors of an authorized slave are more entitled to his property until they collect their debts. And if the slave borrowed two thousand dirhams and his value is a thousand dirhams, and he pays one of the two thousand to his master and is freed by it, and consumes the other thousand, then the lender may take from the master the thousand that the slave paid to him, and also the master guarantees the creditor the thousand because the master prevented, by his manumission, the slave from being sold for the debt. And if the lender wishes, he may pursue the slave for all his debt. It is restricted to suspension because if he does not come with 'fa' in the response, it is not suspended but becomes immediate. Whether the response is with 'waw' as in 'If you pay me a thousand, and you are free,' or without as in 'If you pay me a thousand, you are free' being an independent sentence, not a response, for lack of connection. In al-Dhakhirah: he said to his slave: 'You are free and pay me a thousand dirhams,' he is free and owes nothing. And if he said: 'Pay me a thousand and you are free,' he does not become free until he pays. And if he said: 'You are then free,' he becomes free immediately because the command with 'waw' is not a response with 'fa', so it is for explanation: 'Pay me a thousand because you are free', like 'Rejoice, for help has come to you.' The full discussion is in usul on the topic of 'waw'. And we have previously presented in the section on manumission of a fetus from al-Zahiriyyah that if he suspends the manumission of a fetus on his payment of a thousand, the manumission depends on his payment; if he pays after birth, he becomes free if she gave birth at less than six months. And it is restricted to the slave's payment because if he suspends his manumission on the payment of a stranger who is not authorized, as if he says 'If you pay me a thousand, this slave of mine is free' and the stranger comes with a thousand and places it before him, he becomes free? Consider.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the ruling of ta'liq al-'itq bi al-ada' (suspended manumission for payment). The author explains that when a master says to his slave 'If you pay me X, you are free,' the slave becomes a ma'dhun (authorized slave) to trade, but he is not a mukatab. The commentator then lists numerous differences between this suspended manumission and kitabah (contractual manumission) as derived from Fath al-Qadir, al-Bada'i', al-Muhit, and al-Dhakhirah. The key point is that the suspended manumission is a ta'liq (suspension) not a contract of exchange, so it follows rules of suspension rather than contract. For example, if the slave dies before paying, no payment is taken from his estate because there was no debt; in kitabah it is a debt. If the master dies, the slave can still be sold because he is still a slave; in kitabah he is retained with the estate. Eleven differences are enumerated, then additional ones from other sources bringing the total to fifteen or more. The passage also discusses cases of borrowing and payment, emphasizing that when the slave is authorized, creditors have priority over his assets. Finally, it clarifies the importance of the response particle 'fa' for the suspension to be valid. If the master uses 'waw' instead, it becomes an immediate command. The commentary follows the order of the source text, explaining each difference and the underlying rationale.

Key Terms
تعليق العتق على أداء (ta'liq al-'itq 'ala al-ada'): Suspending the manumission of a slave on the condition that he pays a specified sum of money.
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who has entered into a formal contract of manumission (kitabah) with the master, agreeing to pay installments.
المأذون (al-ma'dhun): A slave given permission by the master to engage in trade; his earnings are his own but the master has prior claim in certain cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a master says 'If you pay me 1000 dirhams, you are free' and then sells the slave to a third party, and then the third party sells him back to the master? The slave later offers the 1000 dirhams to the master. According to the mufta bihi position:
A) The master is not obliged to accept the payment, and the slave remains a slave.
B) The master must accept the payment, and the slave becomes free.
C) The sale voids the original condition entirely, so the slave cannot become free by paying.
D) The slave is freed automatically because the sale and repurchase complete the condition.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school clearly separates ta'liq al-'itq bi al-ada' from kitabah, with the former being a conditional suspension that gives the slave ma'dhun status, leading to numerous practical differences based on the absence of a contractual debt.

intermediate

Three Contrasts between Ta'liq al-Itq and Kitabah
Three contrasting rulings between ta'liq al-'itq and kitabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate the Hanafi rulings for ta'liq al-itq and kitabah when conditions involve container, time, or agent, and apply the underlying principle of strictness versus exchange.

Core Idea
In ta'liq, conditions must be fulfilled exactly; in kitabah, the substitute is what matters.

The Hanafi school sharply distinguishes between conditional manumission (ta'liq al-itq) and the kitabah contract. This passage from al-Bada'i' and al-Muhit presents three specific contrasts: specification of container, time of payment, and the agent who pays. Understanding these contrasts reveals the legal nature of each institution: ta'liq is a suspended effect requiring precise fulfillment, while kitabah is an exchange contract where the master's primary interest is receiving the substitute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
The passage discusses three specifications: (1) payment in a white bag, (2) payment within a specific month, (3) payment by the slave himself (not by an agent).
These are conditions that the master stipulated explicitly.
2
State the ruling for ta'liq al-itq
In each case, if the condition is not fulfilled exactly (e.g., black bag, different month, payment by another), the slave is not freed. The condition is strict.
3
State the ruling for kitabah
In kitabah, these same variations do not invalidate the contract: payment in a different container, after the month, or by an agent still leads to freedom. The condition is interpreted flexibly.
For the time condition, kitabah is not invalidated except by judge's ruling or mutual consent.
4
Analyze the rationale
The passage explains: in ta'liq, the condition is personal and specific; the slave's own payment is required. In kitabah, the purpose is obtaining the substitute (the money), so any valid payment suffices.
This reflects the principle that ta'liq is a suspended effect, while kitabah is a commutative contract (mu'awadah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي البدائع ذكر محمد في الزيادات إذا قال إن أديت ألفاً في كيس أبيض فأنت فأداها حر في كيس أسود لا يعتق وفي الكتابة يعتق ا هـ . وهي الثانية عشر. ولو قال إذا أديت ألفاً في هذا الشهر فأنت حر فلم يؤدها في ذلك الشهر وأداها في غيره لم يعتق وفي الكتابة لا يبطل إلا بحكم الحاكم أو بتراضيهما كما في البدائع. وهي الثالثة عشر. وفي المحيط : لو أمر غيره بالأداء فأدى لا يعتق لأن الشرط أداؤه ولم يوجد فلا حاجة إلى أداء غيره لأنه قادر على أدائه بخلاف الكتابة لأنها معاوضة حقيقة فيها معنى التعليق فكان الأصل فيها المعاوضة فكان المقصود حصول البدل ا هـ . وهي الرابعة عشر.
And in al-Bada'i': Muhammad mentioned in al-Ziyadat: If he said, 'If you pay one thousand in a white bag, you are free,' and he paid it in a black bag, he is not freed; and in kitabah he is freed. That is the twelfth. And if he said, 'If you pay one thousand in this month, you are free,' and he did not pay it in that month but paid it in another, he is not freed; and in kitabah it is not invalidated except by a judge's ruling or by mutual consent as in al-Bada'i'. That is the thirteenth. And in al-Muhit: If he ordered someone else to pay and he paid, he is not freed because the condition is his own payment and it did not occur; there is no need for another's payment because he is able to pay, unlike kitabah because it is a true exchange with a meaning of suspension, so the basis in it is exchange, and the purpose is obtaining the substitute. That is the fourteenth.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage presents three distinct rulings from the Hanafi school, contrasting conditional manumission (ta'liq al-'itq) with the contract of kitabah. In ta'liq, the condition must be fulfilled exactly as stated: if the master specifies a white bag, payment in a black bag does not effect freedom; if a specific month is mentioned, payment after that month does not free the slave; and if the master requires personal payment, the slave cannot delegate it. In kitabah, however, the focus is on the exchange of property for freedom, so the condition is interpreted more flexibly: payment in a different container or time is acceptable, and payment by proxy is valid. The reasoning for the third case is explicitly stated: in ta'liq, the slave's personal payment is a strict condition, while in kitabah, the underlying purpose is obtaining the substitute, so any valid payment suffices.

Key Terms
كيس أبيض (kays abyad): A specific container (white bag) mentioned as a condition for payment.
كتابة (kitabah): A contract between master and slave for the slave to earn and pay for his freedom in installments.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending an effect (here, manumission) upon the occurrence of a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a master says to his slave, 'If you pay me one thousand dirhams in this month, you are free,' and the slave pays after the month, what is the ruling?
A) The slave is freed because the payment was made.
B) The slave is not freed because the condition was not fulfilled exactly.
C) The slave is freed only if the master accepts the late payment.
D) The slave is freed but must pay a penalty.

Key Takeaway
In ta'liq al-'itq, the condition must be fulfilled exactly; in kitabah, the focus is on receiving the substitute, so specifications are flexible.

Slave Borrowing for Manumission: Creditor's Rights
Ruling on slave borrowing and creditor recovery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an authorized slave borrows to pay for manumission and identify the creditor's right to recover from the master.

Core Idea
An authorized slave's creditors have priority over the master to the slave's assets.

This lesson examines a scenario from al-Dhakhira where a slave, authorized to trade, borrows money to fulfill the condition of his manumission. The master receives payment and frees the slave, but the creditor claims the money. The Hanafi ruling establishes the creditor's superior right, with additional consequences when the borrowed amount exceeds the slave's value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The master says: 'If you pay me 1000, you are free.' The slave, being authorized to trade (ma'dhun), borrows 1000 from a creditor and pays the master.
2
Determine the Status of the Slave
Recognize that an authorized slave's property is primarily for settling debts of creditors. The slave's trade activities generate assets that creditors can claim.
The slave is 'ma'dhun' — permitted to trade.
3
Apply the Rule of Creditor Priority
Because the slave's assets are pledged to creditors, the creditor has a greater right to the sum paid than the master. The master must return the money to the creditor.
The manumission is valid, but the creditor recovers from the master.
4
Analyze the Second Case
If the slave borrows 2000 while his value is 1000, pays 1000 to the master and consumes the other 1000, the master must pay both the 1000 received and an additional 1000 because manumission prevents selling the slave to cover the debt.
The master is liable for the full debt due to preventing sale.
5
Consider the Creditor's Options
The creditor may either: (1) recover from the master (who pays both portions) or (2) pursue the slave directly for the entire debt.
The choice is the creditor's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الذخيرة إذا قال إن أديت إلي ألفاً فأنت حر فاستقرض العبد من رجل ألفاً فدفعها إلى مولاه عتق العبد ورجع غريم العبد على المولى فيأخذ منه الألف لأنه أحق بها من المولى من قبل أنه عبد مأذون له في التجارة وغرماء العبد المأذون أحق بماله حتى يستوفوا ديونهم. ولو كان العبد استقرض من رجل ألفي درهم وقيمته ألفاً درهم فدفع أحد الألفين إلى مولاه وعتق بها وأكل الألف الأخرى فإن للمقرض أن يأخذ من المولى الألف التي دفعها العبد إليه ويضمن المولى أيضاً للغريم الألف لأن المولى منع العبد بعتقه من يباع بما عليه من الدين، وإن شاء المقرض اتبع العبد بجميع دينه أيضاً ا هـ.
And in al-Dhakhira: If he said, 'If you pay me one thousand, you are free,' and the slave borrowed one thousand from a man and paid it to his master, the slave becomes free, and the slave's creditor has recourse against the master, taking the thousand from him because he has a greater right to it than the master, due to the slave being authorized to trade, and creditors of an authorized slave have priority over his property until their debts are paid. And if the slave borrowed two thousand dirhams from a man while his value is one thousand dirhams, and paid one of the two thousand to his master and was freed by it, and consumed the other thousand, then the lender may take from the master the thousand that the slave paid to him, and the master also guarantees the other thousand to the creditor because the master prevented, by his manumission, the slave from being sold to cover his debt. If the lender wishes, he may also pursue the slave for all his debt.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage from al-Dhakhira discusses a scenario where a slave, who is authorized to trade (ma'dhun), borrows money to fulfill the condition of his manumission. Upon paying the master, the slave becomes free. However, the creditor has a right to recover from the master because the slave's assets are primarily for paying creditors. In the first case, the creditor can take the exact amount paid. In the second, if the slave borrowed more than his value, the master is liable for the portion paid to him plus an additional guarantee because manumission prevents the slave from being sold for debts. The creditor can also choose to pursue the slave directly.

Key Terms
مأذون (ma'dhun): A slave whom the master has permitted to engage in trade, making his debts payable from his earnings.
غريم (gharim): Creditor of the slave.
استقرض (istaqrada): To borrow money.
عتق (itq): Manumission; freeing a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, if an authorized slave borrows 2000 dirhams (value 1000) and pays 1000 to the master, what is the master's liability?
A) The master must return only the 1000 he received.
B) The master must pay the creditor 2000 total.
C) The master has no liability because the slave consumed the other 1000.
D) The master must pay 1000 to the creditor and the slave must pay the rest.

Key Takeaway
When an authorized slave borrows to pay for conditional manumission, the creditor can recover from the master, and if the borrowed amount exceeds the slave's value, the master guarantees the full debt.

The Dual Nature of Ta'liq al-'Itq: Suspension, Exchange, Takhliyah, and Exceptions
Legal analysis of conditional manumission: its nature, conditions, and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why ta'liq al-'itq is both a suspension and an exchange, apply the ruling that takhliyah constitutes possession, and identify the exceptions where the master is not compelled to accept payment.

Core Idea
Conditional manumission is a suspension in wording and an exchange in purpose: takhliyah effects possession without handover, but ambiguity and prohibition block compulsion.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores the subtle legal nature of conditional manumission (ta'liq al-'itq). The author explains that the particle 'fa' is essential for a valid suspension; without it, the declaration is immediate. More importantly, he reveals that such a conditional statement functions both as a suspension (to protect the master) and as an exchange (to protect the slave). The key practical ruling is that if the slave places the payment within the master's reach (takhliyah), the judge rules that possession has occurred and the slave becomes free. However, there are important exceptions when the payment is ambiguous, prohibited, or unspecified.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the linguistic requirement: the particle 'fa'
Identify why the response clause must begin with 'fa' (فاء) for a valid suspension. Without 'fa', the statement is an immediate declaration, not a suspended condition. Note the contrast with 'waw' (واو) which indicates a separate command.
The particle 'fa' establishes the cause-and-effect link between the condition and the result.
2
Grasp the dual legal nature: suspension and exchange
Understand that ta'liq al-'itq is treated as a suspension initially (to protect the master's rights) and as an exchange at the time of payment (to protect the slave's rights). This is analogous to kitabah (contract of manumission).
The dual nature resolves the apparent contradiction between the wording (suspension) and the purpose (exchange).
3
Apply the ruling on takhliyah
Learn that if the slave places the payment before the master such that the master can take it without obstruction (takhliyah), the judge rules that possession has occurred. The slave becomes free a fortiori from actual possession.
Takhliyah is sufficient for possession in sales, rentals, and debts; here it triggers manumission.
4
Identify the exceptions to compulsion
List the three cases where the master is not compelled to accept payment: (1) the property is ambiguous (e.g., 'dirhams' without specification), (2) the payment is wine (prohibited), (3) the payment is an unspecified garment or animal. In these cases, the condition is treated as a mere oath.
The exceptions protect the master from being forced into an exchange that is invalid (jahalah) or sinful (wine).

المحيط : لو قال إن أديت إلي كر حنطة فأنت حر فجاء بكر جيد يجبر على القبول لأن الكر المطلق إنما ينصرف إلى الوسط لدفع الضرر من الجانبين، فإذا أتاه بالجيد فقد أحسن في القضاء ورضي بهذا الضرر فبطل التعيين وتعلق العتق بحنطة مطلقة. ولو قال كر حنطة وسط فأتاه بكر جيد لا يجبر لأنه نص على التعليق بكر موصوفة وفي الشروط يعتبر التنصيص ما أمكن كما في مسألة الكيس الأبيض. ولو قال أعتق عبداً فأعتق عبداً مرتفعاً لا لأن كسبه مملوك للمولى ا هـ. الثانية لو كان العتق معلقاً على أداء الخمر لا يجبر على القبول وإن كان يعتق بقبولها لأن المسلم ممنوع عنها لحق الله تعالى. والثالثة لو كان معلقاً على أداء ثوب أو دابة لا يجبر على القبول. ولو أتى بثوب وسط أو جيد لأنه مجهول الجنس فلم يصلح عوضاً، ولذا لو وصفه أجبر على القبول. باب التعليق من كتاب الطلاق لو قال لعبده أد إلي ألفاً وأنت حر كان تعليقاً اهـ.
It is restricted to suspension because if the response does not come with 'fa', it is not suspended but is immediate, whether the response is with 'waw', like his saying, 'If you pay me one thousand, and you are free'—it does not suspend, and like his saying, 'If you pay me one thousand, you are free' because it is an independent clause, not a response, due to the lack of a connector. And in al-Dhakhira: He said to his slave, 'You are free, and pay me one thousand dirhams'—he is free and owes nothing. And if he said, 'Pay me one thousand, and you are free,' he is not freed until he pays. And if he said, 'Then you are free,' he is freed immediately because the response to a command with 'waw' is not with 'fa'; rather it is for explanation, i.e., 'Pay me one thousand because you are free,' like his saying, 'Rejoice, for help has come to you.' And its completion is in the principles of the discussion of 'waw'. And we have previously presented, in the discussion of manumission of a fetus from al-Zuhayriyya, that if he suspends the manumission of a fetus on its payment of one thousand, then the manumission is dependent on its payment; if it pays after birth, it becomes free if she gives birth to it before six months. And it is restricted to the slave's own payment because if he suspends his manumission on payment by a stranger who is not authorized, as if he says, 'If you pay me one thousand, this slave of mine is free,' and the stranger came with one thousand and placed it before him, the master is not compelled to accept and the slave is not freed. And if the master swears that he did not receive one thousand from so-and-so, he does not incur perjury; thus in al-Khaniyya. His statement: 'And he becomes free by takhliyah because it is suspension in terms of wording and exchange in terms of purpose'—because he only suspended his manumission on payment to urge him to pay money, so the slave attains the honor of freedom and the master obtains money in exchange, similar to kitabah. For this reason, it was a consideration in divorce in such wording, even if it was irrevocable. So we made it a suspension initially, acting upon the wording and to prevent harm to the master, so that it does not prevent his sale, nor does the slave become entitled to his earnings, nor does it extend to a child born before payment. And we made it an exchange at the end upon payment to prevent harm to the slave, so that the master is compelled to accept. Upon this the fiqh revolves and issues are derived. It is analogous to a gift with a condition of consideration. And takhliyah is the removal of impediments by his placing it before him such that if he extended his hand he would take it. Then the judge rules that he has taken possession of it—in this, in the price of a sold item, in the rental payment, and in all debts. And this is the meaning of their statement, 'The judge compels him to take possession' i.e., he rules so, not that he forces him to take possession by imprisonment or the like. And if the master swears that he did not pay him the thousand, he incurs perjury as in al-Khaniyya. And the mention of takhliyah is to indicate that he becomes free by actual possession a fortiori. And there are exceptions to the general ruling of what is in al-Mukhtasar: cases where he does not become free by the first takhliyah. First: if the property is unknown, such as when he says, 'If you pay me dirhams, you are free'—he is not compelled to accept because such ambiguity is not in exchange, nor can it be treated as kitabah; thus it is a pure oath and there is no compulsion in it, as in al-Tabyin. And in al-Muhit: If he said, 'If you pay me a kurr of wheat, you are free,' and he brought a good kurr, he is compelled to accept because the absolute kurr is understood as the average to prevent harm on both sides. If he brought good, he has improved in payment and consented to this harm, so the specification is annulled and the manumission is attached to absolute wheat. And if he said, 'A kurr of medium wheat,' and he brought a good kurr, he is not compelled because he specified the condition with a described kurr, and in conditions, specification is considered as much as possible, as in the case of the white bag. And if he said, 'Free a slave,' and he freed a valuable slave, he is not freed; but if he said, 'Pay me a slave and you are free,' and he paid him a valuable slave, he becomes free, as in the kurr case. The difference is that in payment, the master is pleased with the increase because it is bringing something into his ownership, so it is pure benefit and no harm; whereas manumission is removal from his ownership because the slave's earning is owned by the master. Second: if the manumission is suspended on payment of wine, he is not compelled to accept, although if he accepts, the slave becomes free, because a Muslim is prohibited from it for the right of Allah. Third: if it is suspended on payment of a garment or an animal, he is not compelled to accept. And if he brought a medium or good garment, because it is of unknown type, it is not suitable as a substitute; therefore if he described it, he is compelled. The chapter on suspension from the book of divorce: If he said to his slave, 'Pay me one thousand and you are free,' it is a suspension.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This lengthy passage explores the legal nature of conditional manumission (ta'liq al-'itq). The author first discusses the importance of the particle 'fa' in the response clause: without 'fa', the statement is not a valid suspension but an immediate declaration. Using 'waw' or no connector results in different rulings. The author then clarifies that ta'liq al-'itq is both a suspension (linguistically) and an exchange (in purpose), analogous to kitabah. At the initial stage, it protects the master's rights; at the time of payment, it protects the slave's rights by compelling the master to accept. The concept of takhliyah (placing the money before the master) is introduced: if the slave places the money within the master's reach, the judge rules that possession has occurred, and the slave becomes free even without physical handover. However, there are exceptions: (1) if the property is unspecified (e.g., 'dirhams'), the master is not compelled because it is a mere oath; (2) if wine is specified, the master is not compelled due to religious prohibition; (3) if a garment or animal of unspecified type is offered, compulsion does not apply because of ambiguity. The passage also distinguishes between cases where the condition involves bringing a specified item versus a general one, using the example of a kurr of wheat: if the condition is absolute, a higher quality is acceptable; if specified, it must be exactly as stated.

Key Terms
تخلية (takhliyah): The act of the slave placing the payment before the master such that the master can take it without obstruction, constituting legal possession.
كر (kurr): A measure of wheat (approximately 150-200 kg).
جهالة (jahalah): Ambiguity or lack of specification in the property offered as payment.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension of a legal effect (here, manumission) upon the occurrence of a future condition.
معاوضة (mu'awadah): An exchange transaction where one party gives something in return for another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is an exception where the master is NOT compelled to accept payment from the slave in a conditional manumission?
A) The payment is in gold coins.
B) The payment is a specified quantity of wheat (kurr).
C) The payment is an unspecified garment.
D) The payment is made by a third party authorized by the slave.

Key Takeaway
Ta'liq al-'itq is a dual-nature legal construct: it protects the master as a suspension initially and the slave as an exchange upon payment, with takhliyah serving as valid possession, subject to exceptions for ambiguity and prohibition.

The Dual Nature of Manumission by Vacating (Takhlīyah)
Commentary on manumission for a payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the dual nature of manumission by takhliyah (ta'liq initially, mu'awadah upon performance) and apply the ruling to cases involving unknown consideration or prohibited items.

Core Idea
Manumission by vacating is a suspension initially to protect the master, but becomes a binding exchange upon payment.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpackages a key fiqh principle: when a master says 'give me a thousand and you are free,' the law treats it as a suspension (ta'liq) at the outset to safeguard the master's rights, but upon actual performance it transforms into an exchange (mu'awadah), compelling the master to accept. Understanding this dual nature is essential for distinguishing similar cases, such as those involving unknown amounts or prohibited goods.

Guided Path
1
Determine the initial and final ruling
Note that initially the master is not compelled to accept, and the slave is not freed. Upon actual payment, the master is compelled and the slave is freed.
This dual ruling is the core of the passage.
2
Understand the legal rationale
The author explains the ruling by analyzing the wording (ta'liq) versus the intended purpose (mu'awadah), drawing analogy to kitabah and gift conditional on return.
This is istihsan-based reasoning.
3
Apply the exceptions
Identify when the master is NOT compelled: unknown money (e.g., 'dirhams'), wine (prohibited), unspecified goods (garment/animal). The consideration must be valid and specified.
Each exception has a specific justification.
4
Connect to oath scenarios
If the master swore he did not receive payment, mere takhliyah (placement) without a judge's ruling does not break the oath.
This clarifies the practical effect of takhliyah.
5
Summarize the fiqh principle
The fiqh revolves around preventing harm to both parties: initially protecting the master, then upon performance protecting the slave.
This is the guiding principle for analogous cases.

Source Text

كتاب العتق باب العتق على جعل
يديه لا يجبر المولى على القبول ولا يعتق العبد، ولو حلف المولى أنه لم يقبض من فلان ألفاً لا يحنث ؛ كذا في الخانية.
قوله : ( وعتق بالتخلية لأنه تعليق نظراً إلى اللفظ ومعاوضة نظراً إلى المقصود لأنه ما علق عتقه بالأداء، إلا ليحثه على دفع المال فينال العبد شرف الحرية والمولى المال بمقابلته بمنزلة الكتابة ولهذا كان عوضاً في الطلاق في مثل هذا اللفظ حتى كان بائناً فجعلناه تعليقاً في الابتداء عملاً باللفظ ودفعاً للضرر عن المولى حتى لا يمتنع عليه بيعه، ولا يكون العبد أحق بمكاسبه ولا يسري إلى الولد المولود قبل الأداء. وجعلناه معاوضة في الانتهاء عند الأداء دفعاً للضرر عن العبد حتى يجبر المولى على القبول، فعلى هذا يدور الفقه وتخرج المسائل نظيره الهبة، بشرط العوض والتخلية رفع الموانع بأن يضعه بين يديه بحيث لو مد يده أخذه فحينئذ يحكم القاضي بأنه قد قبضه فيه وفي ثمن المبيع وبدل الإجارة وسائر الديون، وهذا معنى قولهم أجبره الحاكم على قبضه أي حكم به لا أنه يجبره على قبضه بحبس ونحوه. ولو حلف المولى أنه لم يؤد فأنت لا يجبر على القبول لأن مثل حر هذه الجهالة لا تكون في المعاوضة ولا يمكن حملها على الكتابة فتكون يميناً محضاً ولا جبر فيها كما في التبيين. وفي المحيط : لو قال إن أديت إلي كر حنطة فأنت حر فجاء بكر جيد يجبر على القبول لأن الكر المطلق إنما ينصرف إلى الوسط لدفع الضرر من الجانبين، فإذا أتاه بالجيد فقد أحسن في القضاء ورضي بهذا الضرر فبطل التعيين وتعلق العتق بحنطة مطلقة. ولو قال کر حنطة وسط فأتاه بكر جيد لا يجبر لأنه نص على التعليق بكر موصوفة وفي الشروط يعتبر التنصيص ما أمكن كما في مسألة الكيس الأبيض. ولو قال أعتق . عبداً فأعتق عبداً مرتفعاً لا يعتق، ولو قال أدا لي عبداً وأنت حر فأدى إليه عبداً مرتفعاً حر يعتق كما في الكر والفرق أن في الأداء يكون المولى راضياً بالزيادة لأنه ادخال شيء في ملكه فيكون نفعاً محضاً فلا ضرر وأما العتق إخراج عن ملكه لأن كسبه مملوك للمولى ا هـ . الثانية لو كان العتق معلقاً على أداء الخمر لا يجبر على القبول وإن كان يعتق بقبوله لأن المسلم ممنوع عنها لحق الله تعالى والثالثة لو كان معلقاً على أداء ثوب أو دابة لا يجبر على القبول . ولو أتى بثوب وسط أو جيد لأنه مجهول الجنس فلم يصلح عوضاً، ولذا لو وصفه أجبر على باب التعليق من كتاب الطلاق لو قال لعبده أد إلي ألفاً وأنت حر كان تعليقاً اهـ. وهذا الكلام منشؤه الغفلة عما يذكره المؤلف بعد أربعة أسطر قوله : (ولو) حلف المولى أنه لم يقبض من فلان ألفاً لا يحنث) لأن القاضي لم يحكم بقبضه فلا تعد هذه التخلية قبضاً بخلاف المسألة الآتية عقب هذا.

عني
Book of Manumission, Chapter of Manumission for a Payment. His two hands: the master is not compelled to accept, nor is the slave freed. And if the master swears that he did not receive a thousand from so-and-so, he does not break his oath; as in al-Khaniyah. His statement: (And manumission occurs by vacating [takhliyah] because it is a suspension [ta'liq] with regard to the wording and an exchange [mu'awadah] with regard to the intended purpose, because he only suspended the manumission upon payment to urge him to pay the money, so the slave attains the honor of freedom and the master gets the money in return, akin to kitabah. For this reason, it was a consideration in divorce in such wording until it became irrevocable. So we made it a suspension initially, acting on the wording, and to prevent harm to the master so that he is not prevented from selling him, and the slave is not entitled to his earnings, and it does not extend to the child born before payment. And we made it an exchange at the end upon payment to prevent harm to the slave, so the master is compelled to accept. On this the fiqh revolves and the issues are derived, analogous to a gift conditional on a return. And takhliyah is the removal of obstacles: he places it before him such that if he extends his hand he can take it. Then the judge rules that he has received it concerning this and concerning the price of sold goods, the hire fee, and all other debts. This is the meaning of their statement: 'The judge compels him to take receipt,' i.e., he rules it, not that he forces him to take it by imprisonment or similar. And if the master swears that he did not pay the thousand, he breaks his oath; as in al-Khaniyah. He only mentioned takhliyah to indicate that he is freed by actual receipt a fortiori. Exceptions from the absolute statement in al-Mukhtasar: cases where he is not freed by the first takhliyah. First: if the money was unknown, e.g., he said 'when you give me dirhams, you are free' — he is not compelled to accept because such ignorance is not valid in an exchange and cannot be interpreted as kitabah, so it is a mere oath with no compulsion; as in al-Tabyin. In al-Muhit: if he said 'when you give me a kurr of wheat, you are free' and he brings a good kurr, he is compelled to accept because the absolute kurr refers to the average to prevent harm from both sides. So if he brings good, he has done well and is content with this harm, so the specification is nullified and the manumission is tied to absolute wheat. But if he said 'a medium kurr of wheat' and he brought a good kurr, he is not compelled because he explicitly tied it to a described kurr, and in conditions, specification is observed as much as possible, as in the case of the white bag. And if he said 'free a slave' and he freed a valuable slave, he is not freed. But if he said 'give me a slave and you are free' and he gave him a valuable slave, he is freed; as with the kurr. The difference is that in payment, the master is pleased with the increase because it brings something into his ownership, so it is pure benefit with no harm. As for manumission, it is taking out of his ownership because his earnings belong to the master. End. Second: if the manumission was suspended on delivering wine, he is not compelled to accept, although he is freed if he accepts, because the Muslim is prohibited from it due to Allah's right. Third: if it was suspended on delivering a garment or an animal, he is not compelled to accept, even if he brings a medium or good garment, because it is of unknown type and thus not valid as a consideration. Hence if he described it, he would be compelled. On the topic of suspension from the Book of Divorce: if he said to his slave 'give me a thousand and you are free,' it is a suspension. This statement arises from heedlessness of what the author mentions four lines later: his statement: (And if the master swears that he did not receive a thousand from so-and-so, he does not break his oath) because the judge has not ruled that he received it, so this takhliyah is not considered receipt, unlike the following case. And you. Concerning me.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explaining the ruling on manumission by takhliyah (vacating/placing). The author clarifies that when a master says to his slave, 'Give me a thousand and you are free,' this is initially treated as a ta'liq (suspension) to protect the master: he can still sell the slave, the slave's earnings belong to the master, and manumission does not extend to children born before payment. But upon actual payment, it becomes an exchange (mu'awadah), so the master is compelled to accept the payment and the slave is freed. The text then lists exceptions: ignorance of the amount (e.g., dirhams unspecified) does not compel acceptance; if the condition is on wine, acceptance is not compelled due to prohibition; goods of unknown type (e.g., unspecified garment or animal) also do not compel acceptance. The commentary also discusses oaths: if the master swears he did not receive a thousand, he does not break his oath by mere takhliyah unless the judge rules receipt. The overall rationale is balancing harm between master and slave.

Key Terms
تخلية (takhliyah): In this context, placing the payment within reach of the master such that if he extends his hand he can take it, used as a substitute for actual receipt in rulings.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension of a legal effect (here manumission) on a future condition (payment).
معاوضة (mu'awadah): An exchange where each party gives something (here payment for freedom).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of manumission for a payment, when is the master compelled to accept?
A) Immediately upon the slave's offer
B) When the slave actually performs the payment
C) Only if the payment is in cash
D) Never, it is the slave's option

Key Takeaway
Manumission by takhliyah is a ta'liq initially but becomes a binding mu'awadah upon payment, compelling the master to accept, with specific exceptions for unknown, prohibited, or unspecified consideration.

Manumission After Death: The Heir's Necessary Act
Ruling on deferred manumission with payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a deferred manumission after death with a payment, and explain why acceptance alone is insufficient.

Core Idea
Acceptance after death does not free the slave; the heir must actually perform the manumission.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a subtle point: when a master says to his slave 'You are free after my death for a thousand dirhams,' the slave's acceptance after the master's death does not alone effect freedom. Instead, the heir, executor, or judge must actively free the slave, treating it like a bequest. Understanding why the deceased's incapacity triggers this rule is key to mastering Hanafi manumission law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the initial ruling on acceptance
The passage begins with a master's statement linking manumission to after death with a payment. The author notes that acceptance must occur after death because the offer is future-oriented. However, the slave is not freed by acceptance alone.
2
Understand the analogy to 'free tomorrow'
The text draws an analogy: just as a manumission conditioned on 'tomorrow' requires acceptance after that time, similarly here, since death is the condition, acceptance must be after death. But the key difference is that the deceased cannot personally execute the manumission.
The analogy establishes the timing of acceptance, not the sufficiency of acceptance.
3
Recognize the deceased's incapacity and the need for a substitute
Because the deceased is not capable of manumission, the act falls to the heir, executor, or judge. The manumission is treated as a bequest (wasiyyah), and like any bequest, it must be executed by the legal representative.
The heir can free immediately or conditionally; the executor only immediately.
4
Note the authoritative position and its implications
Al-Sadr al-Shahid and al-Hidayah affirm that acceptance does not free the slave. The heir must actually perform the manumission. This is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.
The passage also mentions that if the heir frees the slave as his own expiation, it is valid for the deceased but not for the expiation, and the wala' remains with the deceased.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن قال أنت حر بعد موتي بألف فالقبول بعد موته لإضافة الإيجاب إلى ما بعد الموت فصار كما إذا قال أنت حر غداً على ألف درهم . وأشار المصنف بتأخير العتق عن الموت إلى أنه لا يعتق بقبوله فلا يعتق إلا بإعتاق الوارث أو الوصي أو القاضي إذا امتنع الوارث لأن العتق تأخر عن الموت إلى أن يقبل والعتق متى تأخر عن الموت لا يثبت إلا بإعتاق واحد من هؤلاء لأنه صار بمنزلة الوصية بالإعتاق ؛ ذكره الإمام العتابي وجزم به الأسبيجابي وقال : إن الوارث يملك عتقه تنجيزاً ،وتعليقاً، والوصي يملكه تنجيزاً فقط، ولو أعتقه الوارث عن كفارة يمينه جاز عن الميت لا عن الكفارة والولاء للميت لا للوارث . وصرح الصدر الشهيد بأن الأصح أنه لا يعتق بالقبول بل لا بد من إعتاق الوارث. وفي الهداية قالوا: لا يعتق وإن قبل بعد الموت ما لم يعتقه الوارث لأن الميت ليس بأهل للإعتاق
His statement: (And if he says, 'you are free after my death for a thousand,' then acceptance is after his death because he added the offer to after death, so it is as if he said 'you are free tomorrow for a thousand dirhams.' And the author indicated by delaying the manumission after death that he is not freed by acceptance, so he is only freed by the manumission of the heir, or the executor, or the judge if the heir refuses, because the manumission was delayed after death until acceptance, and whenever manumission is delayed after death it is only established by the manumission of one of these because it becomes like a bequest of manumission. Mentioned by Imam al-‘Attabi and confirmed by al-Asbijabi, and he said: The heir can free him immediately or conditionally, and the executor can only free him immediately. And if the heir frees him as expiation for his own oath, it is valid for the deceased, not for the expiation, and the wala' belongs to the deceased, not the heir. And al-Sadr al-Shahid stated that the correct view is that he is not freed by acceptance, rather the heir must free him. And in al-Hidayah they said: He is not freed even if he accepts after death as long as the heir does not free him, because the deceased is not capable of manumission.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq comments on a matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding a statement like 'You are free after my death for a thousand dirhams.' The ruling is that acceptance must occur after the master's death because the offer is linked to a future time. The slave is not freed by mere acceptance; instead, the heir (or executor or judge) must actually perform the manumission. This is because the deceased cannot free, so it is treated like a bequest (wasiyyah) of manumission. The heir may free him immediately or conditionally, but the executor only immediately. If the heir frees the slave as expiation for his own oath, the manumission is valid for the deceased but not as expiation, and the wala' (clientage) belongs to the deceased. The authoritative position is that acceptance alone does not effect freedom; the heir's act is necessary.

Key Terms
إعتاق الوارث (i'tāq al-wārith): The act of the heir freeing the slave, which is required for the manumission to take effect after the master's death.
وصية بالإعتاق (wasiyyah bil-i'tāq): A bequest of manumission; the delayed manumission is treated like a bequest.
العتق بعد الموت (al-‘itq ba‘d al-mawt): Manumission deferred to after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a manumission deferred to after death does not take effect by the slave's acceptance; the heir must physically free him, treating it as a bequest.

Manumission After Death: Acceptance or Heir's Action?
Expansion of an intra-Hanafi dispute on conditional manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the relied-upon Hanafi position on conditional manumission after death and evaluate the opposing intra-madhhab argument.

Core Idea
After death, ownership has transferred; acceptance alone does not free the slave.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about a master who says to his slave, 'You are free after my death for 1000 dirhams.' The critical question: does the slave become free by accepting after the master's death, or must the heir manumit him? We will analyse the proofs and the resolution by later Hanafi authorities.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the relied-upon view: the slave does not become free by acceptance after death; the heir (or executor/judge) must manumit.
This is the mufta bihi according to later scholars.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Some early Hanafi scholars (reflected in 'al-asahh' and Ghayat al-Bayan) held that the slave becomes free constructively (hukman) upon acceptance.
Opponent's basis: the offer was from a qualified person, and acceptance should suffice.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent argues that the master's words constitute a valid offer, and since the slave accepts, manumission should occur by constructive freedom (itq hukmi), analogous to immediate talaq or i'taq.
They claim that ownership at the time of acceptance is not required if the offer was valid.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The response is twofold: (a) the deceased is not legally qualified to effect manumission (laysa bi-ahl li al-i'taq), and (b) ownership has passed to the heir, so the condition cannot operate on property no longer owned by the deceased.
Constructive freedom requires ownership at the time it takes effect, which is absent.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If acceptance alone sufficed, the slave would be free immediately after death; if not, the heir must actively manumit, or the executor/judge steps in if the heir refuses.
Practical consequence affects the timing and method of freedom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قال أنت حر بعد موتي بألف فالقبول بعد موته لإضافة الإيجاب إلى ما بعد الموت فصار كما إذا قال أنت حر غداً على ألف درهم . وأشار المصنف بتأخير العتق عن الموت إلى أنه لا يعتق بقبوله فلا يعتق إلا بإعتاق الوارث أو الوصي أو القاضي إذا امتنع الوارث لأن العتق تأخر عن الموت إلى أن يقبل والعتق متى تأخر عن الموت لا يثبت إلا بإعتاق واحد من هؤلاء لأنه صار بمنزلة الوصية بالإعتاق ؛ ذكره الإمام العتابي وجزم به الأسبيجابي وقال : إن الوارث يملك عتقه تنجيزاً ،وتعليقاً، والوصي يملكه تنجيزاً فقط، ولو أعتقه الوارث عن كفارة يمينه جاز عن الميت لا عن الكفارة والولاء للميت لا للوارث . وصرح الصدر الشهيد بأن الأصح أنه لا يعتق بالقبول بل لا بد من إعتاق الوارث. وفي الهداية قالوا: لا يعتق وإن قبل بعد الموت ما لم يعتقه الوارث لأن الميت ليس بأهل للإعتاق ... وهذا صحيح وتعقبه في غاية البيان بأنه ينبغي أن يعتق حكماً لكلام صدر من الأهل مضافاً إلى المحل وإن كان الميت ليس بأهل للإعتاق ولأن القبول لم يعتبر في حال الحياة فإذا لم يعتق بالقبول بعد الوفاة إلا باعتاق واحد منهم لا يكون معتبراً بعد الوفاة أيضاً فلا يبقى فائدة لقبوله بعد الموت ا.هـ. وجوابه أن العتق الحكمي وإن كان لا يشترط فيه الأهلية يشترط قيام الملك وقته، وهنا قد خرج ملك المعلق وبقي للوارث ومتى خرج عن ملكه لا يقع بوجود الشرط مع وجود الأهلية فما ظنك عند عدمها؟ وقوله إنه لا فائدة للقبول بعد الموت ممنوع لأنه لولا القبول لم يصح إعتاق الوصي والقاضي لعدم الملك لهما ولم يلزم الوارث الإعتاق والحاصل أن المسألة مختلف فيها فظاهر إطلاق المتون أنه يعتق بالقبول بعد الموت من غير توقف على إعتاق أحد وهو قول البعض كما يشير إليه لفظ الأصح وله أصله في الرواية كما في غاية البيان، وصحح المتأخرون أنه لا يعتق بالقبول كما قدمنا، ولا فرق في أن بين يؤخر ذكر المال أو يقدمه كأن يقول أنت حر على ألف درهم بعد موتي كما في غاية البيان، لكنه نقل الإجماع. وقد علمت أن الخلاف ثابت وظهر بهذا أن قول الزيلعي وقاضيخان في الفتاوى أنه لو قال له أنت حر على ألف درهم بعد موتي أن القبول فيه للحال ليس بصحيح إذ لا فرق بينه وبين مسألة الكتاب. وقيد بأنت حر لأنه لو قال أنت مدبر على درهم فالقبول فيه للحال فإذا قبل صار مدبراً ولا يلزمه المال لأن الرق قائم والمولى لا يستوجب على عبده ديناً إلا أن يكون مكاتباً. وقد بحث فيه المحقق ابن الهمام بحثاً حسناً فراجعه. وفي الخانية أن القبول فيه بعد الموت كمسألة الكتاب.
And if he said, 'You are free after my death for a thousand,' then acceptance is after his death, because the offer is appended to after death, so it becomes as if he said, 'You are free tomorrow for a thousand dirhams.' And the author indicated by delaying the manumission until after death that he does not become free by his acceptance, so he does not become free except by the manumission of the heir, the executor, or the judge if the heir refuses, because the manumission was delayed until after death until acceptance, and whenever manumission is delayed until after death, it is not established except by the manumission of one of these, because it becomes like a bequest of manumission. Imam al-Atabi mentioned this and al-Asbijabi affirmed it, saying: The heir has the power to manumit him immediately and conditionally, and the executor has the power only immediately. And if the heir manumitted him for his expiatory oath, it is valid for the deceased, not for the expiation, and the patronage belongs to the deceased, not to the heir. And al-Sadr al-Shahid explicitly stated that the correct view is that he does not become free by acceptance; rather, manumission by the heir is necessary. In al-Hidayah they said: He does not become free even if he accepts after death, unless the heir manumits him, because the deceased is not qualified for manumission... This is correct, and it was objected in Ghayat al-Bayan that it is proper that he becomes free constructively, due to speech issued from a qualified person and attributed to the subject matter, even if the deceased is not qualified for manumission, and because acceptance was not considered during life, so if he does not become free by acceptance after death except by the manumission of one of them, it is not considered after death either, so there is no benefit to his acceptance after death. End quote. The answer is that constructive manumission, although it does not require qualification, requires the existence of ownership at the time, and here the ownership of the person who made the conditional statement has left and remains for the heir, and whenever it leaves his ownership, it does not occur upon the existence of the condition with qualification, so what do you think when it is absent? And his statement that there is no benefit to acceptance after death is rejected, because without acceptance, the manumission by the executor or judge would not be valid due to their lack of ownership, and the heir would not be required to manumit. In summary, the issue is disputed. The apparent import of the texts is that he becomes free by acceptance after death without waiting for anyone's manumission, and this is the view of some, as indicated by the word 'al-asahh' (the soundest), and it has its origin in narration as in Ghayat al-Bayan. The later scholars corrected that he does not become free by acceptance, as we have presented. There is no difference between delaying the mention of the money or advancing it, such as if he says, 'You are free for a thousand dirhams after my death,' as in Ghayat al-Bayan, but he [the author of Ghayat al-Bayan] claimed consensus. And you have known that disagreement is confirmed, and it appears from this that the statement of al-Zayla'i and Qadikhan in the Fatawa that if he says to him, 'You are free for a thousand dirhams after my death,' then acceptance is immediate, is not correct, because there is no difference between it and the issue of the book. And it is restricted to 'You are free,' because if he said, 'You are mudabbar for a dirham,' then acceptance is immediate, and when he accepts, he becomes mudabbar, and the money is not due because slavery is present and the master does not owe a debt from his slave unless he is a mukatib. And the verifier Ibn al-Humam researched it well, so refer to it. In al-Khaniyyah, acceptance after death is like the issue of the book.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of a master saying, 'You are free after my death for a thousand dirhams.' The core issue is whether the slave becomes free upon acceptance after the master's death, or whether the heir must manumit him. The author explains that the matn implies acceptance is after death but does not by itself effect manumission. Citing al-Atabi and al-Asbijabi, the view is that the heir, executor, or judge must manumit. This is because the master is no longer the owner and is not qualified to manumit after death. The passage then presents an objection from Ghayat al-Bayan that manumission should occur 'constructively' (hukman) since the offer was valid, but the author refutes this by arguing that ownership has left the deceased, so the condition cannot operate. The later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) affirm that acceptance alone is insufficient. The author also rejects the view of al-Zayla'i and Qadikhan that acceptance is immediate, stating that delaying the payment does not change the ruling. Finally, the case of tadbir is distinguished: if the master says 'You are mudabbar for a dirham,' acceptance is immediate because the slave remains a slave and the debt is not due. This passage shows the Hanafi method of resolving apparent contradictions between texts and the reliance on usul principles such as ownership and qualification (ahliyyah).

Key Terms
إعتاق (i'tāq): The act of manumitting a slave by the owner or his representative.
قبول (qabūl): The acceptance of the slave to the conditional offer of manumission with payment.
عتق حكمي (itq ḥukmī): Constructive manumission; the legal recognition of freedom without an explicit act of manumission by the owner.
معلق (mu'allaq): The person who made a conditional statement (here, the master).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a master saying 'You are free after my death for 1000 dirhams,' what is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling regarding acceptance after death?
A) The slave becomes free immediately upon acceptance.
B) The slave does not become free unless the heir manumits him.
C) The slave becomes free only if he pays the 1000 dirhams.
D) The slave becomes free and must pay the 1000 dirhams to the heir.

Key Takeaway
Manumission after death requires the heir's action; acceptance alone does not free the slave because ownership has passed.

Timing of Acceptance in Conditional Emancipation After Death
Dispute over whether acceptance is immediate or after death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the timing of acceptance in conditional emancipation after death and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Acceptance after death frees no one without an actual emancipator.

This lesson unpacks an intra-Hanafi dispute about a master's conditional promise: 'You are free for 1000 dirhams after my death.' Does the slave's acceptance free him after death, or must someone else emancipate him? The passage contrasts early and later Hanafi authorities, revealing how ownership and eligibility shape the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the master's statement and condition
The master says: 'You are free for 1000 dirhams after my death.' This creates a conditional emancipation for a consideration.
The condition is death; the consideration is 1000 dirhams.
2
State the two conflicting views
View 1 (apparent from matn): acceptance after death frees the slave automatically. View 2 (later scholars): acceptance after death does not free; someone must actually emancipate.
3
Follow the reasoning behind each view
View 1 argues that legal emancipation requires ownership at the time of fulfillment, not eligibility. View 2 argues that ownership passes to heirs, so the master's authority ends at death.
The objection from Ghayat al-Bayan is countered by the need for acceptance to empower the executor.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If acceptance is immediate, freedom occurs during life. If after death, it does not, so the heir or executor must act.
This affects when the money is owed and who receives it.
5
Determine which view is mufta bihi and why
Later scholars' view is mufta bihi because it respects the transfer of ownership to heirs.
The text states 'wa sahhaḥa al-muta’akhkhirūna annahu lā yu‘taqu bi al-qubūl'.

Source Text

اه. وهذا صحيح وتعقبه في غاية البيان بأنه ينبغي أن يعتق حكماً لكلام صدر من الأهل مضافاً إلى المحل وإن كان الميت ليس بأهل للإعتاق ولأن القبول لم يعتبر في حال الحياة فإذا لم يعتق بالقبول بعد الوفاة إلا باعتاق واحد منهم لا يكون معتبراً بعد الوفاة أيضاً فلا يبقى فائدة لقبوله بعد الموت ا.هـ. وجوابه أن العتق الحكمي وإن كان لا يشترط فيه الأهلية يشترط قيام الملك وقته، وهنا قد خرج ملك المعلق وبقي للوارث ومتى خرج عن ملكه لا يقع بوجود الشرط مع وجود الأهلية فما ظنك عند عدمها؟ وقوله إنه لا فائدة للقبول بعد الموت ممنوع لأنه لولا القبول لم يصح إعتاق الوصي والقاضي لعدم الملك لهما ولم يلزم الوارث الإعتاق والحاصل أن المسألة مختلف فيها فظاهر إطلاق المتون أنه يعتق بالقبول بعد الموت من غير توقف على إعتاق أحد وهو قول البعض كما يشير إليه لفظ الأصح وله أصله في الرواية كما في غاية البيان، وصحح المتأخرون أنه لا يعتق بالقبول كما قدمنا، ولا فرق في أن بين يؤخر ذكر المال أو يقدمه كأن يقول أنت حر على ألف درهم بعد موتي كما في غاية البيان، لكنه نقل الإجماع. وقد علمت أن الخلاف ثابت وظهر بهذا أن قول الزيلعي وقاضيخان في الفتاوى أنه لو قال له أنت حر على ألف درهم بعد موتي أن القبول فيه للحال ليس بصحيح إذ لا فرق بينه وبين مسألة الكتاب. وقيد بأنت حر لأنه لو قال أنت مدبر على درهم فالقبول فيه للحال فإذا قبل صار مدبراً ولا يلزمه المال لأن الرق قائم والمولى لا يستوجب على عبده ديناً إلا أن يكون مكاتباً. وقد بحث فيه المحقق ابن الهمام بحثاً حسناً فراجعه. وفي الخانية أن القبول فيه بعد الموت كمسألة الكتاب
Chapter of Emancipation, Section on Emancipation for a Consideration. This is correct. But it was objected to in Ghayat al-Bayan that he should be freed legally because of a statement emanating from someone eligible, attached to a person, even if the deceased is not eligible for emancipation, and because acceptance was not considered during his lifetime. So if he is not freed by acceptance after death except by the emancipation of one of them, it would not be considered after death either. Thus there remains no benefit for his acceptance after death. The answer is that legal emancipation, even if it does not require eligibility, requires the existence of ownership at that time. Here the ownership of the suspended person has left and remains with the heir. Once it leaves his ownership, it does not occur upon the occurrence of the condition even with eligibility, so what do you think when it is absent? His statement that there is no benefit for acceptance after death is denied, because without acceptance the emancipation of the executor and the judge would not be valid due to lack of ownership for them, and the heir would not be obligated to emancipate. The gist is that the issue is disputed. Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of acceptance when a master says to his slave, 'You are free for a thousand dirhams after my death.' The core question is: Does the slave's acceptance take effect immediately during the master's lifetime, or after his death? The text first reports an objection from Ghayat al-Bayan: since the deceased is not eligible to emancipate and acceptance during life was not required, acceptance after death serves no purpose. The response distinguishes between real and legal emancipation: legal emancipation only requires ownership at the time, but here ownership passes to the heirs. The objection also argues that without acceptance after death, the executor or judge could not emancipate, but the defender says acceptance is needed for their authority. The author notes that the apparent position of the texts is that acceptance after death frees the slave without any action from heirs, but later scholars corrected this, holding that acceptance after death does not free the slave. The dispute extends to whether it makes a difference if the money is mentioned before or after. The author sides with those who hold acceptance after death is valid, citing that consensus was claimed but disagreement is real. This passage guards against the misunderstanding that all conditional emancipations require immediate acceptance.

Key Terms
العتق على جعل (al-‘itq ‘alā ja‘l): Emancipation of a slave in exchange for a consideration (e.g., money or service).
القبول (al-qubūl): The slave's acceptance of the offer of emancipation for a consideration.
عتق حكمي (‘itq hukmī): Legal emancipation that occurs by judicial decree or operation of law, as opposed to direct action of the master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Basic Case: Emancipation with Hajj Will – Work Obligation
First scenario: emancipation for Hajj with no other property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a master wills his only slave to perform Hajj and be freed, and calculate the slave's work obligation for the heirs.

Core Idea
A slave freed by will without payment is only free for one-third; he must work for the remaining two-thirds.

This lesson examines the primary scenario from the passage: a master's will that his only slave perform Hajj after death and then be freed. The slave is the entire estate. The Hanafi rule treats emancipation without payment as a bequest from the one-third. We will see that the slave is not immediately free; he must first perform Hajj, then the heirs free him, and he works to compensate for the two-thirds that exceed the bequest limit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the will and the estate
The master says to his slave: 'Perform Hajj on my behalf after my death, and you are free.' The only asset is the slave himself. Recognize that the slave's value constitutes the entire estate.
This is a single asset case.
2
Classify the emancipation
The emancipation is 'itq bi-ghayri mal (without money), so it is treated as a bequest from the one-third. The heirs cannot refuse the bequest of emancipation, but they are not obligated to give more than one-third of the slave's value.
Bequests are limited to one-third of the estate.
3
Determine the slave's obligation
Since the slave's full value is the estate, the one-third covers only part of his freedom. The heirs free him entirely, but he must work to pay for the remaining two-thirds of his value. The text says 'yu'taquhu al-warathatu wa yas'ā fī thuluthay qīmatihi'.
The slave works for the heirs to compensate for the two-thirds.
4
Check for additional bequests
In this basic case, there is no other bequest. The entire one-third goes to the slave's freedom. The work obligation is exactly two-thirds.
If there were other bequests, the calculation would change (see lesson 2).
5
Apply the ruling
Given a slave valued at $9,000, the heirs free him after Hajj, and he must work to earn $6,000 for them. He is free for $3,000 worth.
The work can be in any form of service or payment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : لو قال لعبده حج عني حجة بعد موتي وأنت حر ولا مال له سواه يحج عنه حجاً وسطاً ثم تعتقه الورثة ويسعى في ثلثي قيمته لأنه عتق بغير مال فيعتبر من الثلث، فإن أوصى الميت مع هذا بثلث ماله لرجل قسم الثلث بين العبد والموصى له على أربعة ثلاثة أرباعه منها للعبد ويسعى للموصى له في ربع ثلث رقبته وللورثة في ثلثي قيمته لأن العبد له بعتق جميع رقبته فيضرب بجميع الرقبة والموصى له يضرب بالثلث فصار الثلث موصى بينهما على أربعة أسهم وجميع الرقبة على اثني عشر، فسلم للعبد ثلاثة ويسعى للموصى له في سهم وللورثة ثمانية. ولو قال ادفع إلى الوصي قيمة حج يحج بها عني فدفع فعلى الورثة أن يعتقوه ولا ينتظر الحج لأنه عتق بمال والحج مشورة وليس بشرط، فإن كانت قيمة الحج أقل من قيمته نظر؛ إن كانت مقدار ثلثي قيمته جاز لأن الوصية بالعتق نافذة في الثلث، وإن كانت أقل من ثلثي قيمته فعليه أن يسعى إلى تمام الثلثين ثم يدفع إلى الورثة أو إلى الوصي مقدار حجة، فإن أجازت الورثة الحج فحج بذلك كله فثلثاه للورثة والثلث يحج به عنه من حيث يبلغ ولو قال لعبده ادفع إلى الوصي قيمة حجة فإذا دفعتها إليه فحج بها عني فأنت لا يعتق العبد ما لم يحج عن الميت، ولو قال حج عني بعد الموت وأنت حر فمات وأبى الورثة خروجه للحج ولا مال للميت غيره فلهم ذلك حتى يخدمهم مقدار ثلثي ما يحتاج إليه للخروج إلى الحج، لأن مقدار ثلث صار حقاً للورثة رقبة ومنفعة، وإذا خرج اشتغل عن خدمتهم، وإذا حج وجب إعتاقه فيبطل حق الورثة عن منفعته وخدمته فيحبسونه ويستخدمونه إلى العام القابل استيفاء لحقهم، فإن قال الورثة أخرج في هذا العام فقال أخدمكم العام وأخرج السنة الثانية فليس للعبد ذلك، فإن أمكنه الخروج في العام وإلا أبطل القاضي وصيته، فإن لم يطلب منه الورثة حتى مضت السنة فله أن يحج في السنة الثانية، إن لم يكن الميت قال حج عني في هذه السنة، ولو قال حج عني بعد موتي بخمس سنين وأنت فأبى الورثة أن يتركوه إلى خمس سنين فليس لهم ذلك اهـ
In al-Muhit: If a man says to his slave, 'Perform Hajj on my behalf after my death, and you are free,' and he has no other property, the slave performs a moderate Hajj, then the heirs emancipate him, and he works for two-thirds of his value because the emancipation is without money, so it is considered from the one-third. If the deceased also bequeathed one-third of his property to a man, the one-third is divided between the slave and the legatee into four shares: three-quarters of it for the slave, and he works for the legatee for one-quarter of one-third of his value, and for the heirs for two-thirds of his value, because the slave has in his emancipation the whole of his value, so he contributes with the whole of his value, and the legatee contributes with the one-third. So the one-third is bequeathed between them into four shares, and the whole of the slave's value is twelve; thus the slave gets three, works for the legatee for one share, and for the heirs for eight. If he said, 'Pay to the executor the value of a Hajj to perform Hajj for me,' and he paid, then the heirs must emancipate him and not wait for the Hajj, because the emancipation is for money and Hajj is a recommendation and not a condition. If the value of the Hajj is less than his value, he looks: if it is two-thirds of his value, it is valid because the bequest of emancipation is effective in the one-third. If it is less than two-thirds, he must work until completing two-thirds, then pay to the heirs or to the executor the amount of a Hajj. If the heirs approve the Hajj and he performs it with all that, two-thirds are for the heirs and one-third is used to perform Hajj on his behalf where it suffices. If he said to his slave, 'Pay to the executor the value of a Hajj, and when you have paid it, perform Hajj on my behalf,' then the slave is not freed until he performs Hajj on behalf of the deceased. If he said, 'Perform Hajj on my behalf after death, and you are free,' and he died, and the heirs refuse to let him go for Hajj, and the deceased has no other property, they have the right to do so until he serves them the amount of two-thirds of what is needed for going out for Hajj, because one-third became the right of the heirs in both value and service. If he goes out, he busies himself from serving them. When he performs Hajj, his emancipation becomes obligatory, so the heirs' right to his service and benefit is voided. So they detain him and employ him until the next year to recover their right. If the heirs say, 'Go out this year,' and he says, 'I will serve you this year and go out next year,' the slave does not have that right. If it is possible for him to go out this year, otherwise the judge voids his will. If the heirs do not demand from him until the year passes, he may perform Hajj in the second year, if the deceased did not say, 'Perform Hajj for me in this year.' If he said, 'Perform Hajj for me after my death in five years, and you are free,' and the heirs refuse to let him go for five years, they do not have that right.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rulings on a scenario where a master wills that his slave perform Hajj for him after his death and then be freed, with the slave being the only asset. The text explains how the slave's freedom is treated as a bequest from the one-third of the estate. If the master also bequeaths one-third to someone else, a complex distribution ensues: the one-third is divided into four shares (three for the slave's freedom, one for the legatee), but the slave must also work for the heirs and legatee to compensate for the value exceeding the one-third. Further cases include paying the executor for Hajj, and the heirs' right to detain the slave to recover their portion of service. The slave cannot postpone the Hajj against the heirs' wishes, and if the master specified a time, the heirs cannot prevent it. This lesson guards against the misunderstanding that the slave becomes free immediately upon the master's death; rather, conditions and compensation apply.

Key Terms
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum portion that can be bequeathed in Islamic law.
عتق بغير مال ('itq bi-ghayri mal): Emancipation without receiving any payment from the slave; it is treated as a bequest from the one-third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One-third
B) One-half
C) Two-thirds
D) All of it

Key Takeaway
A slave freed by will without money is only free for the one-third bequest; he must work for the remaining two-thirds to compensate the heirs.
