Bequest Conflict: Emancipation and Cash Bequest
Second scenario: two bequests – emancipation and cash.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the distribution of the one-third when a slave's emancipation competes with another bequest, applying the proportional allocation principle.

Core Idea
When two bequests compete, they share the one-third proportionally based on their claims.

This lesson extends the previous one by adding a second bequest: the master also bequeaths one-third of his property to a stranger. The slave is still the only asset. Now the emancipation (claiming the whole slave's value) and the cash bequest (claiming one-third of the estate) compete for the same one-third limit. The Hanafi solution is proportional reduction, resulting in a specific distribution where the slave is freed for 3/12 of his value and works for the remaining 9/12 (1/12 for the legatee and 8/12 for the heirs).

Guided Path
1
Identify the total claims
The slave's emancipation claims his entire value (12/12 of the estate). The legatee claims 1/3 of the estate (4/12). Total claims = 16/12, but only 4/12 (the one-third) is available for bequests.
Claims exceed the bequest pool.
2
Determine the bequest pool
The one-third of the estate is 4/12. This is the maximum that can be given in bequests. The remaining 8/12 is the heirs' inheritance.
The heirs automatically get the residue.
3
Apply proportional distribution
The available 4/12 is distributed proportionally to the claims: emancipation claim (12/12) and cash claim (4/12). Ratio of claims = 12:4 = 3:1. So emancipation gets 3/4 of the bequest pool (3/12) and cash gets 1/4 (1/12).
This is the principle of proportional reduction.
4
Calculate the slave's work obligations
The slave is freed for 3/12 of his value (no work for that part). He must work for the legatee for 1/12 (the legatee's bequest), and for the heirs for the remaining 8/12. Total work = 9/12 = 3/4 of his value.
The text says: 'yas'ā lil-mūṣā lah fī rub‘ thuluth raqabathī wa lil-warathati fī thuluthay qīmatihī' – he works for the legatee for one-quarter of one-third (1/12) and for the heirs for two-thirds (8/12).
5
Verify using the 12-base calculation
The text explicitly uses 12 as base: slave gets 3, works for legatee for 1, and for heirs for 8. Total value 12, work 9, freedom 3. This matches.
The calculation is self-consistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : لو قال لعبده حج عني حجة بعد موتي وأنت حر ولا مال له سواه يحج عنه حجاً وسطاً ثم تعتقه الورثة ويسعى في ثلثي قيمته لأنه عتق بغير مال فيعتبر من الثلث، فإن أوصى الميت مع هذا بثلث ماله لرجل قسم الثلث بين العبد والموصى له على أربعة ثلاثة أرباعه منها للعبد ويسعى للموصى له في ربع ثلث رقبته وللورثة في ثلثي قيمته لأن العبد له بعتق جميع رقبته فيضرب بجميع الرقبة والموصى له يضرب بالثلث فصار الثلث موصى بينهما على أربعة أسهم وجميع الرقبة على اثني عشر، فسلم للعبد ثلاثة ويسعى للموصى له في سهم وللورثة ثمانية. ولو قال ادفع إلى الوصي قيمة حج يحج بها عني فدفع فعلى الورثة أن يعتقوه ولا ينتظر الحج لأنه عتق بمال والحج مشورة وليس بشرط، فإن كانت قيمة الحج أقل من قيمته نظر؛ إن كانت مقدار ثلثي قيمته جاز لأن الوصية بالعتق نافذة في الثلث، وإن كانت أقل من ثلثي قيمته فعليه أن يسعى إلى تمام الثلثين ثم يدفع إلى الورثة أو إلى الوصي مقدار حجة، فإن أجازت الورثة الحج فحج بذلك كله فثلثاه للورثة والثلث يحج به عنه من حيث يبلغ ولو قال لعبده ادفع إلى الوصي قيمة حجة فإذا دفعتها إليه فحج بها عني فأنت لا يعتق العبد ما لم يحج عن الميت، ولو قال حج عني بعد الموت وأنت حر فمات وأبى الورثة خروجه للحج ولا مال للميت غيره فلهم ذلك حتى يخدمهم مقدار ثلثي ما يحتاج إليه للخروج إلى الحج، لأن مقدار ثلث صار حقاً للورثة رقبة ومنفعة، وإذا خرج اشتغل عن خدمتهم، وإذا حج وجب إعتاقه فيبطل حق الورثة عن منفعته وخدمته فيحبسونه ويستخدمونه إلى العام القابل استيفاء لحقهم، فإن قال الورثة أخرج في هذا العام فقال أخدمكم العام وأخرج السنة الثانية فليس للعبد ذلك، فإن أمكنه الخروج في العام وإلا أبطل القاضي وصيته، فإن لم يطلب منه الورثة حتى مضت السنة فله أن يحج في السنة الثانية، إن لم يكن الميت قال حج عني في هذه السنة، ولو قال حج عني بعد موتي بخمس سنين وأنت فأبى الورثة أن يتركوه إلى خمس سنين فليس لهم ذلك اهـ
In al-Muhit: If a man says to his slave, 'Perform Hajj on my behalf after my death, and you are free,' and he has no other property, the slave performs a moderate Hajj, then the heirs emancipate him, and he works for two-thirds of his value because the emancipation is without money, so it is considered from the one-third. If the deceased also bequeathed one-third of his property to a man, the one-third is divided between the slave and the legatee into four shares: three-quarters of it for the slave, and he works for the legatee for one-quarter of one-third of his value, and for the heirs for two-thirds of his value, because the slave has in his emancipation the whole of his value, so he contributes with the whole of his value, and the legatee contributes with the one-third. So the one-third is bequeathed between them into four shares, and the whole of the slave's value is twelve; thus the slave gets three, works for the legatee for one share, and for the heirs for eight. If he said, 'Pay to the executor the value of a Hajj to perform Hajj for me,' and he paid, then the heirs must emancipate him and not wait for the Hajj, because the emancipation is for money and Hajj is a recommendation and not a condition. If the value of the Hajj is less than his value, he looks: if it is two-thirds of his value, it is valid because the bequest of emancipation is effective in the one-third. If it is less than two-thirds, he must work until completing two-thirds, then pay to the heirs or to the executor the amount of a Hajj. If the heirs approve the Hajj and he performs it with all that, two-thirds are for the heirs and one-third is used to perform Hajj on his behalf where it suffices. If he said to his slave, 'Pay to the executor the value of a Hajj, and when you have paid it, perform Hajj on my behalf,' then the slave is not freed until he performs Hajj on behalf of the deceased. If he said, 'Perform Hajj on my behalf after death, and you are free,' and he died, and the heirs refuse to let him go for Hajj, and the deceased has no other property, they have the right to do so until he serves them the amount of two-thirds of what is needed for going out for Hajj, because one-third became the right of the heirs in both value and service. If he goes out, he busies himself from serving them. When he performs Hajj, his emancipation becomes obligatory, so the heirs' right to his service and benefit is voided. So they detain him and employ him until the next year to recover their right. If the heirs say, 'Go out this year,' and he says, 'I will serve you this year and go out next year,' the slave does not have that right. If it is possible for him to go out this year, otherwise the judge voids his will. If the heirs do not demand from him until the year passes, he may perform Hajj in the second year, if the deceased did not say, 'Perform Hajj for me in this year.' If he said, 'Perform Hajj for me after my death in five years, and you are free,' and the heirs refuse to let him go for five years, they do not have that right.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rulings on a scenario where a master wills that his slave perform Hajj for him after his death and then be freed, with the slave being the only asset. The text explains how the slave's freedom is treated as a bequest from the one-third of the estate. If the master also bequeaths one-third to someone else, a complex distribution ensues: the one-third is divided into four shares (three for the slave's freedom, one for the legatee), but the slave must also work for the heirs and legatee to compensate for the value exceeding the one-third. Further cases include paying the executor for Hajj, and the heirs' right to detain the slave to recover their portion of service. The slave cannot postpone the Hajj against the heirs' wishes, and if the master specified a time, the heirs cannot prevent it. This lesson guards against the misunderstanding that the slave becomes free immediately upon the master's death; rather, conditions and compensation apply.

Key Terms
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum portion that can be bequeathed in Islamic law.
عتق بغير مال ('itq bi-ghayri mal): Emancipation without receiving any payment from the slave; it is treated as a bequest from the one-third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the two-bequest case, what is the total fraction of the slave's value that he must work for (including work for the legatee and heirs)?
A) 2/3 (8/12)
B) 3/4 (9/12)
C) 1/2 (6/12)
D) 5/6 (10/12)

Key Takeaway
When two bequests compete for the one-third, they share proportionally; the slave's work obligation increases from 2/3 to 3/4 of his value.

Variations: Heirs' Rights and Timing Conditions
Heirs' rights and timing conditions in the will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the heirs' right to detain a slave to recover their share through service, and identify when a specified time for Hajj binds the heirs.

Core Idea
Heirs may detain a slave to recover their two-thirds share through service, but they cannot prevent Hajj beyond a specified time set by the testator.

This lesson covers the latter part of the passage, which discusses scenarios where the heirs refuse to let the slave go for Hajj immediately, and the master's specification of a time for Hajj. The Hanafi ruling balances the heirs' right to recover their inheritance (through the slave's service) with the obligation to fulfill the master's will. The text gives detailed conditions: the heirs can detain the slave until he serves them for the value of two-thirds of the travel expenses for Hajj, but if the master set a specific year, the heirs cannot prevent the slave from going then.

Guided Path
1
Understand the heirs' right to service
Since two-thirds of the slave's value belongs to the heirs, they have a right to his service until that value is compensated. The slave's going for Hajj would interrupt that service.
The heirs can detain him to recover their share.
2
Limit of detention
The heirs can only detain him until he serves them the amount equivalent to two-thirds of the cost needed for Hajj travel. This is because the one-third portion of his value is already freed by the bequest, and the Hajj expense is considered a necessary expenditure from the bequest.
The text: 'until he serves them the amount of two-thirds of what is needed for going out for Hajj'.
3
Slave cannot postpone against heirs' wishes
If the heirs want him to go this year, the slave cannot defer to the next year. The heirs have the right to enforce the timing of the work recovery.
The slave's choice is subordinate to the heirs' right to recover.
4
Judge's intervention
If the slave cannot go this year (e.g., due to inability), the judge may invalidate the will (i.e., the condition of Hajj) so that the emancipation is still effective but without the Hajj condition, allowing the heirs to recover their share.
The judge balances the interests.
5
Master's specific time binds heirs
If the testator specified a particular year or five years later for Hajj, the heirs cannot prevent the slave from going at that time, because the master's will must be respected.
The text: if he said 'after five years,' the heirs cannot refuse to let him go.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Conditions and Options in Conditional Emancipation After Death
Rulings on conditions in post-death emancipation and the timing of the slave's option.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on conditional emancipation after death, distinguishing between suspensive and restrictive conditions, and identifying the timing of the slave's option based on the placement of the phrase 'if you wish'.

Core Idea
The wording of a condition determines whether emancipation is suspended or immediate, and whether the slave's option is now or later.

This lesson examines several rulings from al-Dhakhira and other Hanafi texts on conditional emancipation after death. You will learn how the phrasing of a condition—whether it is suspensive (if you do not drink) or restrictive (on condition that)—affects the validity of the emancipation. Additionally, you will understand how the position of the option clause ('if you wish') relative to the time phrase determines when the slave may exercise his option.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of condition
Determine whether the condition is suspensive (ta'liq) or restrictive (shart). The ruling differs: suspensive conditions that are violated void the emancipation; restrictive conditions do not affect freedom.
Look for phrases like 'in lam' (if not) vs 'ala an' (on condition that).
2
Analyze the effect of a prior judicial decree
If the emancipation was already decreed by a judge before the condition was broken, the emancipation remains valid even if the condition is later violated.
This is an exception to the general rule.
3
Locate the option clause
For option (mashi'a) clauses, note the placement of 'if you wish' relative to 'free' and the time phrase: if 'if you wish' precedes 'free', the option is immediate; if it follows, the option is at the future time.
The timing of the option is determined solely by this word order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الذخيرة: رجل قال لعبده أنت حر بعد موتي إن لم تشرب الخمر فأقام أشهراً ثم شرب الخمر قبل أن يعتق بطل عتقه، وإن رفع الأمر إلى القاضي بعد موت المولى قبل أن يشرب فأمضى فيه العتق ثم شرب ذلك الخمر بعد لم يرد إلى الرق، ولو قال لعبده أنت حر على أن لا تشرب الخمر فهو حر شرب الخمر أو لم يشرب ا اهـ. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو قال لعبده إن شئت فأنت حر بعد موتي فإن المشيئة له بعد موته، وكذا إذا قال إذا جاء غد فأنت حر إن شئت كانت المشيئة إليه بعد طلوع الفجر من الغد وكذا إذا قال أنت غداً إن شئت كانت المشيئة في الغد، ولو قال إن شئت فأنت حر غداً كانت المشيئة للحال في قول أبي يوسف ومحمد وظاهر الرواية عن أبي حنيفة؛ كذا في الخانية. وفي البدائع: لو قال أنت حر غداً إن شئت فالمشيئة في
In al-Dhakhira: A man said to his slave, 'You are free after my death if you do not drink wine.' He stayed for months, then drank wine before being freed; his emancipation is void. If the matter was raised to the judge after the death of the master before the slave drank, and the judge passed the emancipation, then the slave drank that wine afterwards, he does not return to slavery. If he said to his slave, 'You are free on condition that you do not drink wine,' he is free whether he drank or not. The author indicated that if he said to his slave, 'If you wish, you are free after my death,' then the option is after his death. Similarly, if he said, 'When tomorrow comes, you are free if you wish,' the option is after dawn of the next day. Also, if he said, 'You are free tomorrow if you wish,' the option is tomorrow. If he said, 'If you wish, you are free tomorrow,' the option is immediate according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and the apparent narration from Abu Hanifa. Thus in al-Khaniyya. In al-Bada'i: If he said, 'You are free tomorrow if you wish,' the option is in
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings on conditional emancipation after death. The first case: a master conditions freedom after death on the slave not drinking wine. If the slave drinks before the master's death, the condition is broken and emancipation is void. However, if a judge had already decreed the emancipation after death (before the slave drinks), then the slave is free and later drinking does not affect it. The second case: if the condition is phrased as 'on condition that you do not drink,' this is a restrictive condition (not suspensive), so the slave is free whether he drinks or not. The third set of rulings deals with option clauses (mashi'a). The key principle is that the timing of the option depends on the wording: if 'if you wish' comes before the freedom statement, the option is immediate; if after, the option is at the future time. This passage guards against confusing suspensive conditions with restrictive conditions, and against misplacing the option clause in the wording.

Key Terms
المشيئة (al-mashī'a): The option or will of the slave to accept or reject the emancipation.
العتق المعلق (al-‘itq al-mu‘allaq): Suspended emancipation that takes effect upon the occurrence of a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master says to his slave, 'If you wish, you are free tomorrow,' when does the slave have the option?
A) Immediately
B) Tomorrow
C) After the master's death
D) At any time

Key Takeaway
The wording of a condition or option clause in emancipation determines its legal effect: suspensive conditions void emancipation if broken, while restrictive conditions do not, and the placement of 'if you wish' decides when the slave may choose.

Conditional Emancipation: Ta'liq vs Qayd
Ruling on conditional emancipation with wine prohibition: two cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a suspensive condition (ta'liq) and a restrictive condition (qayd) in Hanafi emancipation law and state the ruling for each case.

Core Idea
A suspensive condition voids emancipation if violated; a restrictive condition does not affect freedom.

This passage from al-Dhakhira clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi emancipation law. It presents two scenarios where a master ties emancipation to the slave's wine drinking. The ruling hinges on whether the condition is suspensive (ta'liq: 'if you do not drink') or restrictive (qayd: 'on condition that you do not drink'). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the law of conditional emancipation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and note the two wordings: (1) 'You are free after my death if you do not drink wine' and (2) 'You are free on condition that you do not drink wine'. Recognize that in the first, freedom is postponed and contingent on a future condition; in the second, freedom is immediate with a restrictive condition.
The wording 'if' indicates ta'liq; 'on condition that' indicates qayd.
2
Analyze the effect of drinking before the event
In the first scenario, if the slave drinks before the master dies, the emancipation is void. In the second, drinking does not affect freedom at all.
The timing of the condition's violation matters only in ta'liq.
3
Understand the role of the judge's ruling
If the judge already executed the emancipation after the master's death, a later violation does not revert the slave to slavery. The judge's ruling finalizes freedom.
This prevents instability in legal status.
4
Distinguish ta'liq from qayd in principle
Ta'liq suspends the entire effect of the contract on a future uncertain event. Qayd restricts the scope of the contract but does not suspend its immediate effect. In the second wording, the condition is interpreted as a prohibition, not a suspension.
This distinction is a hallmark of Hanafi jurisprudence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الذخيرة: رجل قال لعبده أنت حر بعد موتي إن لم تشرب الخمر فأقام أشهراً ثم شرب الخمر قبل أن يعتق بطل عتقه، وإن رفع الأمر إلى القاضي بعد موت المولى قبل أن يشرب فأمضى فيه العتق ثم شرب ذلك الخمر بعد لم يرد إلى الرق، ولو قال لعبده أنت حر على أن لا تشرب الخمر فهو حر شرب الخمر أو لم يشرب ا اهـ.
And in al-Dhakhira: A man said to his slave: 'You are free after my death if you do not drink wine.' He stayed for months, then drank wine before he became free – his emancipation is void. And if the matter was raised to the judge after the death of the master before he drank, and the judge executed the emancipation, then he drank that wine afterwards – he does not return to slavery. And if he said to his slave: 'You are free on condition that you do not drink wine,' then he is free whether he drank wine or did not drink. End.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage from al-Dhakhira presents two distinct scenarios regarding conditional emancipation and wine. In the first, the master conditions freedom after death on the slave not drinking wine. If the slave drinks before the master dies, the conditional emancipation is void. However, if the judge already ruled the slave free before the drinking occurred (after the master's death), the subsequent drinking does not return him to slavery. In the second scenario, the master says 'You are free on condition that you do not drink wine.' Here, the condition is not a suspensive condition (ta'liq) but a restrictive condition (qayd). The slave is free immediately regardless of whether he drinks, because the condition is interpreted as a prohibition, not a suspending factor.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition attached to emancipation; here it is either suspensive (ta'liq) or restrictive (qayd).
عتق (itq): Emancipation, freeing of a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master says to his slave 'You are free on condition that you do not drink wine' and the slave drinks wine, what is the ruling?
A) The emancipation is void because the condition is violated.
B) The emancipation is valid and the slave remains free.
C) The emancipation is suspended until the slave repents.
D) The slave returns to slavery if he drinks habitually.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi emancipation, a suspensive condition (ta'liq) voids freedom if violated, while a restrictive condition (qayd) does not affect the immediate emancipation.

Timing of the Slave's Choice in Conditional Emancipation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on when the slave's choice is exercised in conditional emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a slave exercises his choice in different conditional emancipation phrasings and distinguish between cases where the choice is immediate versus future.

Core Idea
Wording order determines timing: if 'if you wish' comes first, choice is immediate; if last, choice is future.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about the timing of the slave's choice (mashi'ah) in conditional emancipation. The key question is whether the slave must consent now or can delay his choice until the future event. The Hanafi masters analyze different phrasings to derive the correct ruling, emphasizing the importance of word order.

Guided Path
1
Identify the different phrasings
List the three main patterns from the passage: (1) 'If you wish, then you are free after my death' (2) 'If you wish, then you are free tomorrow' (3) 'You are free tomorrow if you wish'.
The placement of 'if you wish' relative to 'you are free' is decisive.
2
Apply the general rule
When the condition (in shi'ta) precedes the result (anta hurr), the choice is immediate because the condition must be fulfilled now to bring about the future result. When the result is stated first and the condition follows, the choice is at the future time specified.
This is a principle of talil (verbal reasoning) in Hanafi fiqh.
3
State the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
For the phrase 'If you wish, then you are free tomorrow', Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule that the choice is in the present (immediately upon utterance). The apparent transmission from Abu Hanifa also supports this.
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi nuance
The passage does not explicitly name the opposing view, but indicates that some might consider the choice to be on tomorrow because the freedom is future. However, the preferred view is the immediate choice.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If the slave chooses immediately, he becomes free tomorrow; if he does not, the condition is void and he remains enslaved. If the choice were delayed, he could choose tomorrow, potentially freeing himself even if he remained silent now.
Practical consequence: the slave's silence now is fatal under the preferred view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو قال لعبده إن شئت فأنت حر بعد موتي فإن المشيئة له بعد موته، وكذا إذا قال إذا جاء غد فأنت حر إن شئت كانت المشيئة إليه بعد طلوع الفجر من الغد وكذا إذا قال أنت غداً إن شئت كانت المشيئة في الغد، ولو قال إن شئت فأنت حر غداً كانت المشيئة للحال في قول أبي يوسف ومحمد وظاهر الرواية عن أبي حنيفة؛ كذا في الخانية. وفي البدائع : لو قال أنت حر . غداً إن شئت فالمشيئة في
And the author pointed out that if he said to his slave: 'If you wish, then you are free after my death' – then the choice is his after his death. Likewise, if he said: 'When tomorrow comes, you are free if you wish' – the choice is his after the dawn of tomorrow. Likewise, if he said: 'You are free tomorrow if you wish' – the choice is on tomorrow. And if he said: 'If you wish, then you are free tomorrow' – the choice is for the present in the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and the apparent transmission from Abu Hanifa; thus in al-Khaniyyah. And in al-Bada'i': If he said: 'You are free. Tomorrow if you wish' – the choice is on...
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage discusses the timing of the slave's choice (mashi'ah) in conditional emancipation sentences. The author of al-Hidayah (the commentator) analyzes different wordings. If the master says 'If you wish, then you are free after my death,' the slave's choice is after the master's death, because the freedom is future. Similarly, if he says 'When tomorrow comes, you are free if you wish,' the choice is after dawn on that day. In the phrase 'You are free tomorrow if you wish,' the choice is also on the next day. However, if the master says 'If you wish, then you are free tomorrow,' the choice is in the present moment (before tomorrow arrives) according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and the apparent transmission from Abu Hanifa. The reasoning is that the phrase 'if you wish' precedes the freedom, so the slave must choose now to activate the future freedom. There is a disagreement: the text says 'the apparent transmission from Abu Hanifa' agrees with the two, but al-Khaniyyah mentions this. Al-Bada'i' gives a slightly different wording requiring further analysis.

Key Terms
المشيئة (al-mashi'ah): The slave's choice or will to accept the conditional freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, if a master says 'If you wish, then you are free tomorrow,' when does the slave exercise his choice?
A) Immediately upon hearing the statement.
B) At the dawn of tomorrow.
C) After the master's death.
D) Anytime during the day.

Key Takeaway
In conditional emancipation, the timing of the slave's choice depends on the order of words: if the condition precedes the result, the choice is immediate; if the condition follows, the choice is at the future time.

Tadbir: Definition and Linguistic Identity
Refinement of the definition of tadbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of tadbir and explain why al-Maqdisi considers it identical to the phrase 'you are free after my death.'

Core Idea
Tadbir is simply emancipation postponed to death; its wording does not change its legal reality.

The institution of tadbir (postponed emancipation) is a key feature of Hanafi slave law. In this passage, the commentator al-Maqdisi engages in a precise linguistic and legal analysis to show that the expression 'You are mudabbar' is identical in meaning to 'You are free after my death.' This clarification resolves a dispute among later Hanafi scholars about whether the two formulations require different rules of acceptance. Understanding this definition is crucial for correctly applying the rulings of tadbir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two formulations
Recognise that the master can declare tadbir using either the single word 'anta mudabbar' or the compound phrase 'anta hurr ba'da mawti'. Both are legally operative declarations.
The words differ but the intended legal consequence is the same.
2
Analyse al-Maqdisi's linguistic claim
Al-Maqdisi argues that the meaning (المعنى) is one: emancipation attached to after death. He uses the analogy of 'limit' (hadd) and 'the limited' (mahdud) to show that a single essence can be expressed by different linguistic forms.
Just as 'human' and 'rational animal' denote the same reality, tadbir and the explicit phrase denote the same legal reality.
3
Distinguish between essence and legal consequence
The essence of tadbir is the idafah (attachment) of emancipation to future death. The right to freedom (haqq al-hurriyyah) that arises before death is a legal ruling (hukm) derived from that valid attachment, not part of the definition.
This distinction is critical to refuting the opposing view that tadbir establishes a right distinct from direct emancipation.
4
Conclude the identity
Since both formulations share the same core meaning and any difference is only linguistic, rulings that depend on the meaning (such as the need for immediate acceptance) must be uniform across both expressions.
This sets the stage for the dispute on acceptance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الألف في التدبير بحق الحرية وهو متحقق قبل الموت وفي تلك قابلها بحقيقة الحرية وحقيقتها بعد الموت فالقبول بعده وحاصل بحث المحقق أن التدبير ليس معناه إلا إعتاق مضاف إلى ما بعد الموت وذلك هو الثابت في كل من قوله أنت مدبر أو أنت حر بعد موتي بلا فرق، بل المعنى واحد دل عليه بلفظ مفرد ومركب كلفظ الحد والمحدود في إنسان وحيوان ناطق ثم يثبت حق الحرية فرعاً على صحة الإضافة التي هي | التدبير لا أن حق الحرية هو معنى التدبير ابتداء فلم يتحقق الفرق. وأجاب المقدسي بأنه لما صار حق الحرية حكماً شرعياً له صح أن يطلق، ويراد به حكمه كما في كثير من المعاني الشرعية كما ذكر هو أن البيع يطلق ويراد به الملك فتأمل. وكذا في قوله أنت على ألف بعد موتي قابلها بحقيقة الحرية فاحتاج إلى القبول حالاً ثم أضافها إلى ما بعد الموت. فقول بعض المتأخرين هنا إن قول الزيلعي والخانية أن القبول فيه للحال غير صحيح إذ لا فرق بينه وبين الكتاب إن اعتمد في ذلك على غاية البيان فيقال : لم لم يعكس ويقول إن ما فيها غير صحب لما في الكافي وغيره لا سيما وقد نقل عنه الإجماع وخطأه فيه . اهـ كلام المقدسي .
The alif in tadbir is about the right to freedom, and it is realized before death, while in that [other phrase] he contrasted it with the reality of freedom, and its reality is after death, so acceptance is after death. The conclusion of the muhaqqiq's research is that tadbir means nothing more than emancipation attached to after death, and that is established in both his saying 'You are mudabbar' and 'You are free after my death' without difference. Rather, the meaning is one, indicated by a single word or composite word, like the word 'limit' and 'the limited' in 'human' and 'rational animal'. Then the right to freedom is established as a branch of the validity of the addition which is tadbir, not that the right to freedom is the meaning of tadbir initially, so the difference is not realized. And al-Maqdisi answered: Since the right to freedom became a legal ruling, it is correct to use it and intend its ruling, as in many legal meanings, as he mentioned that 'sale' is used and meant as ownership. So reflect. Similarly in his saying: 'You owe one thousand after my death,' he contrasted it with the reality of freedom, so it needed acceptance immediately, then he added it to after death. So the statement of some later scholars here that the saying of al-Zayla'i and al-Khaniyyah that acceptance is in the present is not correct, since there is no difference between it and the book. If he relied on Ghayat al-Bayan for that, then it is said: Why did he not reverse and say that what is in it is not correct, because of what is in al-Kafi and others, especially since consensus has been transmitted from him, and he was mistaken in it. End of al-Maqdisi's words.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by al-Maqdisi on the topic of tadbir. The commentator (al-Zayla'i or others) had argued that 'You are mudabbar' and 'You are free after my death' differ in that tadbir gives a right to freedom before death, while the latter gives actual freedom after death, requiring acceptance after death. Al-Maqdisi refutes this: tadbir simply means emancipation postponed to after death, identical in meaning to 'You are free after my death.' The right to freedom is a consequence of the valid attachment (idafah) to the future, not the essence of tadbir. Therefore, there is no difference requiring distinct rulings on acceptance. Al-Maqdisi further criticizes some later scholars who claimed that in the phrase 'You owe one thousand after my death,' acceptance must be immediate, but he argues that this is inconsistent; if acceptance is required in the book (the original text), then it should be required here too. He points out that the claim of consensus is erroneous.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): Emancipation attached to after the master's death, synonymous with 'you are free after my death'.
قبول (qabul): Acceptance by the slave of the conditional emancipation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Maqdisi, what is the meaning of tadbir?
A) A right to freedom established before death.
B) Emancipation attached to after the master's death, identical to saying 'you are free after my death'.
C) A conditional emancipation that requires immediate acceptance.
D) A type of sale.

Key Takeaway
Tadbir is defined as emancipation attached to death; its linguistic form does not alter its legal essence, settling the dispute on definition.

The Dispute on Immediate Acceptance in Tadbir
Critical refinement of acceptance requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on whether tadbir requires immediate acceptance, and evaluate al-Maqdisi's argument that acceptance is only after death.

Core Idea
Acceptance in tadbir is a consequence of the attachment to death, not a condition of the declaration.

The passage continues from the definitional discussion to address a practical legal consequence: does the slave need to accept the tadbir immediately upon declaration? Some later Hanafi scholars distinguished between the single-word expression 'You are mudabbar' and the compound 'You are free after my death,' claiming that the latter requires immediate acceptance while the former does not. Al-Maqdisi refutes this distinction, arguing that both are identical and acceptance is only required after death. This dispute has direct implications for the validity of the tadbir if the slave does not accept immediately.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Position A (al-Zayla'i, al-Khaniyyah): For 'anta mudabbar', no immediate acceptance needed; for 'anta hurr ba'da mawti', immediate acceptance required. Position B (al-Maqdisi): Both identical, so no immediate acceptance needed in either case.
The key is the practical difference in the timing of acceptance.
2
Understand the basis of Position A
They distinguish between a right (haqq) to freedom established before death (in tadbir) and actual freedom (haqiqah) granted at death (in the explicit phrase). The right is considered a present legal benefit, so the slave's acceptance is not necessary; but the direct declaration of freedom, even if postponed, requires acceptance at the time of declaration.
This subtle distinction relies on the nature of the right.
3
Analyse al-Maqdisi's response
Al-Maqdisi argues that the right to freedom is merely a legal ruling (hukm) derived from the valid idafah, not the meaning of tadbir. Therefore, there is no substantive difference between the two expressions that would warrant different acceptance rules.
He uses the analogy of debt: 'You owe me a thousand after my death' does not require immediate acceptance because the obligation is attached to the future; similarly, tadbir is an obligation attached to death.
4
Consider the debt analogy
The passage mentions 'anta 'alayya alf ba'da mawti' (you owe one thousand after my death). In that case, acceptance is not needed immediately because the obligation is attached to the future. Al-Maqdisi uses this to challenge the consistency of the opposing view: if acceptance is required in the explicit phrase for emancipation, why not in the debt case?
This analogy strengthens al-Maqdisi's argument.
5
Identify the tarjih
Al-Maqdisi claims his view is supported by earlier authoritative texts like al-Kafi and refutes the alleged consensus of the opposing side. In Hanafi fatwa practice, the position that no immediate acceptance is required is considered stronger.
The tarjih favours al-Maqdisi's view, but later Hanafi fatwa manuals may vary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Emancipation in Exchange for Service: Contract vs. Condition
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of freedom in emancipation-for-service contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on when a slave is freed when the master says 'Serve me for a year and you are free,' and explain the practical difference between the views of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
When a master says 'Serve me and you are free,' Abu Hanifa frees instantly; Abu Yusuf defers freedom until service ends.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: is the statement 'Serve me for a year and you are free' a contract of immediate emancipation or a conditional suspension? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf differ on the timing of freedom, with practical consequences for the slave's status and obligations. The passage also considers the effects on dependents and the distinction between contracts and conditions, illustrating how textual wording determines the legal outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the master's statement
Determine whether the wording is a direct offer (e.g., 'I free you on condition that you serve me') or a conditional statement (e.g., 'If you serve me, you are free'). This classification determines the legal structure.
The first is a contract (mu`awadah); the second is a suspended condition (ta`liq).
2
Apply Abu Hanifa's view
According to Abu Hanifa, the offer is a contract that requires immediate acceptance. Upon acceptance, the slave becomes free instantly and owes the service as a debt. If the service period is unspecified, the slave pays his value instead.
Acceptance must occur in the same session (majlis al-`aqd).
3
Apply Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf considers the statement a condition (ta`liq). The slave does not become free until the service is performed, regardless of acceptance. Freedom is suspended on the completion of service.
Under this view, the slave remains in bondage until service ends.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the slave is free immediately and can marry, inherit, etc., but must serve. Under Abu Yusuf, he remains a slave with limited rights until service is complete.
This affects obligations like nafaqah and the slave's ability to earn.
5
Consider additional implications
If the slave has dependents and no wealth, the commentator deduces that he may earn for his family first, then serve the master, analogizing to insolvency in monetary emancipation.
Service does not depend on earning money, so the slave is not automatically authorized (ma'dhun) to trade.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو حرره على خدمته سنة فقبل عتق وخدمه يعني من ساعته لأن الإعتاق على الشيء يشترط فيه وجود القبول في المجلس لا وجود المقبول كسائر العقود، وعليه أن يخدمه المدة المعينة وهو المراد بالسنة سنة أو أقل أو أكثر. ونص الحاكم الشهيد أن الخدمة المعروفة بين الناس قيد بالمدة لأنه لو حرره على خدمته من غير مدة عتق وعليه أن يرد قيمة نفسه لأن الخدمة مجهولة، وكذا لو قال الجاريته أنت حرة على أن تخدمني فلانة فقبلت عتقت وردت قيمتها. وقال محمد: ترد قيمة الخدمة شهراً؛ كذا في الذخيرة. ونقل في الظهيرية عن بعضهم أنها إن خدمته عمره أو عمرها لا شيء عليها، وإن أبت أن تخدمه عمره أو عمرها تسعى في قيمتها اهـ. وقد وقع الاستفتاء عما إذا حرره على خدمته مدة معينة وقبل العبد وعتق وكان له زوجة وأولاد فما حكم نفقته ونفقتهم إذا لم يكن له مال فإنه لا يتفرغ للاكتساب بسبب خدمة المولى هذه المدة، فلم أر فيه نقلاً، وينبغي أن يشتغل بالاكتساب لأجل الانفاق على نفسه وعياله إلى أن يستغني عن الاكتساب فيخدم المولى المدة المعينة لأنه معسر عن أداء البدل فصار كما إذا أعتقه على مال ولا قدرة له عليه فإنه يؤخر إلى الميسرة. قيد بكونه حرره على خدمته كأن قال له أعتقتك على أن تخدمني لأنه لو قال إن كذا مدة فأنت خدمتني لا يعتق حتى يخدمه لأنه معلق بشرط والأول معاوضة، ولم حر يصرحوا هنا بأنه يكون مأذوناً لأنه لا ضرورة إليه إذ الخدمة لا تتوقف على اكتساب المال بخلاف إن أديت الي ألفاً فأنت حر كما قدمناه وفي الذخيرة لو قال اخدمني سنة وأنت حر عتق الساعة ولا شيء عليه في قول أبي حنيفة. وقال أبو يوسف : لا يعتق إلا بالخدمة قبل أو لم يقبل. وفي الظهيرية : لو قال لأمته عند وصيته إذا خدمت ابني وابنتي حتى يستغنيا فأنت حرة، فإن كانا صغيرين تخدمهما حتى يدركا ، فإن أدرك أحدهما دون الآخر تخدمهما جميعاً، وإن كانا مدركين تخدم البنت حتى تتزوج والابن حتى يحصل له ثمن جارية، فإذا
His saying: (And if he emancipates him in exchange for his service for a year, and he accepts, he becomes free and serves him), meaning from that very hour, because emancipation in exchange for something requires the existence of acceptance in the session, not the existence of the thing accepted, like other contracts. And it is upon him to serve him for the specified period, and by 'year' is meant a year or less or more. Al-Hakim al-Shahid expressly stated that service known among people is restricted by a period because if he emancipates him in exchange for his service without a period, he becomes free and must return the value of himself because the service is unknown. Likewise, if he said to his slave-girl: 'You are free on condition that you serve so-and-so,' and she accepts, she becomes free and returns her value. Muhammad said: She returns the value of one month's service; thus in al-Dhakhira. And it is reported in al-Zahiriyyah from some that if she serves him for his lifetime or her lifetime, nothing is owed; but if she refuses to serve him for his lifetime or her lifetime, she works to pay her value. End. And a question arose: if he emancipates him in exchange for his service for a specified period, and the slave accepts and becomes free, and he has a wife and children, what is the ruling on his nafaqah and their nafaqah if he has no wealth? For he cannot engage in earning due to serving the master for this period. I have not seen a transmission on this. It is appropriate that he engage in earning for the sake of spending on himself and his family until he becomes independent of earning, then he serves the master for the specified period, because he is insolvent and cannot pay the substitute, so it is like the case where he emancipates him for money and he cannot pay it – he is deferred until ease. The restriction is that he emancipated him in exchange for his service, as if he said: 'I emancipated you on condition that you serve me,' because if he said: 'If you serve me for such a period, you are free,' he does not become free until he serves, because it is suspended on a condition, and the first is a contract. And they did not explicitly state here that he is authorized (ma'dhun) because there is no need, since service does not depend on earning money, unlike 'If you pay me one thousand, you are free' as we mentioned. And in al-Dhakhira: If he said: 'Serve me for a year and you are free,' he becomes free immediately and nothing is owed, according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: He does not become free except by serving, whether he accepted or not. And in al-Zahiriyyah: If he said to his slave-girl in his will: 'When you serve my son and daughter until they become independent, you are free,' then if they are young, she serves them until they reach maturity; if one reaches maturity before the other, she serves both; if they are already mature, she serves the daughter until she marries and the son until he obtains the price of a slave-girl, then when...
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This commentary discusses emancipation in exchange for service (al-`itq `ala al-khidmah). The original text states that if a master says 'I free you on condition you serve me for a year,' and the slave accepts, he becomes free immediately and must serve for the specified period. Acceptance must occur in the same session (majlis). The service must be specified; if no period is given, the slave becomes free but must pay his value because the service is unknown (jahalah). The same applies to a slave-girl. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that if the master says 'Serve me for a year and you are free,' the slave is free immediately without any payment. Abu Yusuf disagrees: the slave only becomes free after performing the service, whether he accepted or not. For cases where the slave has dependents, the commentator deduces that the slave should earn for his family first, then serve the master, treating him as insolvent (mu`sir). The passage also distinguishes between emancipation as a contract (mu`awadah) and a suspended condition (ta`liq). In a contract, the slave is free upon acceptance; in a conditional sentence, freedom occurs only after fulfilling the condition.

Key Terms
عتق على جعل (itq `ala ja`l): Emancipation in exchange for something (here: service).
خدمة (khidmah): Service; here, the consideration for emancipation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a master says 'Serve me for a year and you are free,' when does the slave become free?
A) Immediately after the statement, with no payment required.
B) After completing one year of service.
C) Only if he accepts in the session.
D) After the master's death.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between contract and condition determines whether a slave becomes free immediately or after service in emancipation-for-service arrangements.

Freeing a Slave Conditional on Serving Another: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on a slave-girl freed on condition she serves another, with dispute on compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a slave is freed to serve another and distinguish the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on compensation.

Core Idea
When a slave is freed to serve another, the consideration's unspecified nature triggers a compensation dispute.

This passage from al-Dhakhira presents a case where a master frees his slave-girl on condition she serves a third party. The service is unspecified, leading to her freedom and the obligation to pay her full value. However, when the service is specified for a month, a disagreement arises between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: does she pay full value or only the value of the service period? The passage also includes a variant for a male slave, where the third party's acceptance is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The master says to his slave-girl, 'You are free on condition that you serve so-and-so.' This is a suspended emancipation with a conditional service to a third party.
2
State the ruling for unspecified service
Since the service is unknown (majhul), the condition is void; the slave-girl becomes free but must pay the full value (qimah) of herself as compensation.
There is no dispute on this point.
3
Distinguish the two positions when service is specified
If the service is specified for a month, Abu Yusuf says she pays full value, while Muhammad says she pays only the value of one month's service.
The text does not specify a tarjih; both views are valid within the Hanafi school.
4
Consider the parallel case for a male slave
The passage reports from Bishr from Abu Yusuf: if a male slave is freed to serve someone for a year, the third party's acceptance is required. If he accepts but the slave does not serve, the slave repays his full value.
This case emphasizes the role of the third party's consent.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Yusuf, the financial liability is higher; under Muhammad, it is lower. In practice, a mufti may choose either view depending on circumstances.
Later Hanafi works often prefer Muhammad's view for specified service periods.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وكذا لو قال الجاريته (الخ) عبارة الذخيرة. هكذا رجل قال لأمته أنت حرة على أن تخدمني فلانة فقبلت فهي حرة وعليها أن ترد قيمتها لأن الخدمة مجهولة، ولو قال على أن تخدمني فلانة شهراً فإن أبا يوسف قال : ترد قيمتها. وقال محمد ترد قيمتها شهراً. وفيه أيضاً بشر عن أبي يوسف: رجل قال لعبده أنت حر على أن تخدم فلاناً سنة فالقبول إلى فلان، فإن قبل عتق وإن لم يخدمه رد العبد قيمته اهـ
His saying: (And likewise if he said to his slave-girl ...) is the wording of al-Dhakhira. Thus: A man said to his slave-girl: 'You are free on condition that you serve so-and-so,' and she accepted – she is free and upon her is to return her value because the service is unknown. And if he said: 'On condition that you serve so-and-so for a month,' then Abu Yusuf said: She returns her value. And Muhammad said: She returns the value of her service for a month. And in it also from Bishr from Abu Yusuf: A man said to his slave: 'You are free on condition that you serve so-and-so for a year' – the acceptance is to so-and-so; if he accepts, he becomes free, and if he does not serve him, the slave returns his value. End.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage from al-Dhakhira clarifies the ruling when a master says to his female slave 'You are free on condition that you serve so-and-so.' Since the service is unspecified (majhulah), she becomes free immediately upon acceptance but must pay the full value of herself (qimatiha). If the service is specified for a month, Abu Yusuf says she pays full value, while Muhammad says she pays only the value of one month's service. There is also a case where the master says to his male slave 'You are free on condition that you serve so-and-so for a year.' Here, the acceptance belongs to the third party (so-and-so). If that person accepts, the slave becomes free; if the slave does not serve, he must pay his value.

Key Terms
قيمة (qimah): Market value of the slave (full value or value of service).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must the slave-girl pay if the master says 'You are free on condition you serve so-and-so' without specifying a time?
A) Nothing
B) Full market value
C) Value of service for one month
D) The value of so-and-so's service

Key Takeaway
When a slave-girl is conditionally freed to serve another, the compensation depends on whether the service is specified; unspecified service requires full value; specified service triggers a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Slave's Obligation to Earn for Family During Service Period
Ruling on whether a freed slave must earn for his family during the service period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling concerning a freed slave's responsibility to earn for his family during the service period and identify the alternative view analogizing to a legatee of service.

Core Idea
A freed slave serving the master must earn for his family; the master is not obligated.

This passage from Ibn Nujaym's al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a specific scenario: a slave freed on condition of serving the master for a fixed period. The question arises: who bears the responsibility for maintaining the slave's family during that time? The preferred view is that the slave should earn for them, but an alternative analogy suggests the master might be obliged. In this lesson, we will examine the ruling and the analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the slave's earning for his family during the service period. The ruling is that it is appropriate (yambaghi) for the slave to do so, not obligatory.
2
Locate the alternative view
The commentator mentions an opinion from al-Manh that the master might be obliged to provide nafaqah, analogizing the slave to a legatee of service (musa la bi al-khidmah).
The passage is cut off, but the analogy is key.
3
Analyze the analogy
In the case of a legatee of service, the master is not obliged to provide nafaqah for the slave's family; the slave is expected to earn. Thus the analogy actually supports the slave's duty.
The alternative view is not adopted in the text.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage affirms the view that the slave should earn. This is the relied-upon position.
Al-Nahr confirms the original ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وينبغي أن يشتغل بالاكتساب الخ أقره عليه في النهر. وقال في المنح: ويمكن أن يقال بوجوبها على المولى في المدة المذكورة ويجعل كالموصى له بالخدمة فإن النفقة
His saying: (And it is appropriate that he engage in earning ...) was affirmed by al-Nahr. And in al-Manh: It can be said that it is obligatory upon the master during the mentioned period, and it is treated like a legatee of service, for the nafaqah...
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This brief passage is a comment on the earlier ruling that a slave freed in exchange for service should earn for his family. The commentator notes that this view is affirmed by al-Nahr. Another scholar (al-Manh) suggests an alternative: the master might be obliged to provide nafaqah (maintenance) for the slave's family during the service period, analogizing the slave to a legatee of service (musa la bi al-khidmah). The text is incomplete, but it indicates a difference of opinion on whether the slave or the master bears the responsibility for the slave's dependents during the service term.

Key Terms
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance, financial support for dependents.
موصى له بالخدمة (musa la bi al-khidmah): A person who has been bequeathed the service of a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the preferred view regarding the freed slave's family maintenance during his service period?
A) The master must provide full nafaqah.
B) The slave should earn for his family.
C) The slave's family must fend for themselves.
D) The state provides support.

Key Takeaway
A freed slave serving the master is expected to earn for his family; the master is not obligated to provide maintenance.

Immediate Freedom Upon Acceptance: Emancipation on Service
Commentary on the basic ruling of emancipation on service.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that emancipation on condition of service is an exchange contract requiring acceptance in the session, explain the qiyas to emancipation for money, and identify the position of Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Emancipation on service is an exchange: acceptance frees immediately, service is a debt.

In this lesson, we examine the core ruling from the passage: when a master offers freedom in exchange for service, what constitutes a valid contract? The commentator clarifies that acceptance must occur in the same session, and the slave becomes free instantly—like a sale. We will also explore how this ruling is derived by analogy (qiyas) to the well-established case of emancipation for a monetary payment, and note a significant difference of opinion within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the exact scenario: master says to slave 'you are free on condition you serve me for a year' and the slave accepts. What is the hukm according to Abu Hanifa? The slave becomes free immediately upon acceptance.
The commentary explicitly states 'عتق وخدمه يعني من ساعته' (he becomes free and must serve him, meaning from his hour).
2
Understand the condition of acceptance in session
Why must acceptance be in the same session? Because this is an exchange contract (معاوضة), similar to other contracts like sale. The existence of the countervalue (service) can be deferred, but the mutual consent must be expressed in the session.
Compare to conditional emancipation (تعليق) where no acceptance is needed; that is a different legal category.
3
Trace the qiyas to emancipation for money
The commentator draws an analogy: freeing a slave for money (عتق على مال) results in immediate freedom with a debt of money. Here, the countervalue is service. The illa (effective cause) is that both are exchanges with a deferred countervalue.
The qiyas is khafi (implicit) because service is not exactly like money, but the principle is the same: the slave gains freedom and owes the countervalue.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf disagrees: the slave is not freed until he actually performs the service, even if he accepted. This is mentioned in the passage. The mufta bihi (operative position) is that of Abu Hanifa (immediate freedom).
This ikhtilaf has practical implications: under Abu Yusuf's view, the slave remains in bondage until service is done, affecting his ability to marry, earn, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

أقل أو أكثر. ونص الحاكم الشهيد أن الخدمة المعروفة بين الناس قيد بالمدة لأنه لو حرره على خدمته من غير مدة عتق وعليه أن يرد قيمة نفسه لأن الخدمة مجهولة، وكذا لو قال الجاريته أنت حرة على أن تخدمني فلانة فقبلت عتقت وردت قيمتها. وقال محمد: ترد قيمة الخدمة شهراً؛ كذا في الذخيرة. ونقل في الظهيرية عن بعضهم أنها إن خدمته عمره أو عمرها لا شيء عليها، وإن أبت أن تخدمه عمره أو عمرها تسعى في قيمتها اهـ. وقد وقع الاستفتاء عما إذا حرره على خدمته مدة معينة وقبل العبد وعتق وكان له زوجة وأولاد فما حكم نفقته ونفقتهم إذا لم يكن له مال فإنه لا يتفرغ للاكتساب بسبب خدمة المولى هذه المدة، فلم أر فيه نقلاً، وينبغي أن يشتغل بالاكتساب لأجل الانفاق على نفسه وعياله إلى أن يستغني عن الاكتساب فيخدم المولى المدة المعينة لأنه معسر عن أداء البدل فصار كما إذا أعتقه على مال ولا قدرة له عليه فإنه يؤخر إلى الميسرة. قيد بكونه حرره على خدمته كأن قال له أعتقتك على أن تخدمني لأنه لو قال إن كذا مدة فأنت خدمتني لا يعتق حتى يخدمه لأنه معلق بشرط والأول معاوضة، ولم يصرحوا هنا بأنه يكون مأذوناً لأنه لا ضرورة إليه إذ الخدمة لا تتوقف الظهيرية : لو قال لأمته عند وصيته إذا خدمت ابني وابنتي حتى يستغنيا فأنت حرة، فإن كانا صغيرين تخدمهما حتى يدركا ، فإن أدرك أحدهما دون الآخر تخدمهما جميعاً، وإن كانا مدركين تخدم البنت حتى تتزوج والابن حتى يحصل له ثمن جارية، فإذا زوجت البنت وبقي الابن تخدمهما جميعاً، وإن مات أحدهما وهما كبيران أو صغيران بطلت الوصية ا هـ. وفي شرح النقاية في مسألة إن خدمتني كذا لو خدمه أقل منها أو أعطاه مالاً عن خدمته لا يعتق وكذا لو قال إن خدمتني وأولادي سنة فمات بعض الأولاد لا يعتق ا هـ قوله : (وكذا لو قال الجاريته (الخ) عبارة الذخيرة. هكذا رجل قال لأمته أنت حرة على أن تخدمني فلانة فقبلت فهي حرة وعليها أن ترد قيمتها لأن الخدمة مجهولة، ولو قال على أن تخدمني فلانة شهراً فإن أبا يوسف قال : ترد قيمتها. وقال محمد ترد قيمتها شهراً. وفيه أيضاً بشر عن أبي يوسف: رجل قال لعبده أنت حر على أن تخدم فلاناً سنة فالقبول إلى فلان، فإن قبل عتق وإن لم يخدمه رد العبد قيمته اهـ قوله : ( وينبغي أن يشتغل بالاكتساب الخ أقره عليه في النهر. وقال في المنح: ويمكن أن يقال بوجوبها على المولى في المدة المذكورة ويجعل كالموصى له بالخدمة فإن النفقة واجبة عليه وإن لم يكن له ملك الرقبة لكونه محبوساً بخدمته والحبس هو الأصل في هذا الباب أصله القاضي والمفتي، فإن مرض فينبغي أن تفرض نفقته في بيت المال بخلاف الموصى بخدمته إذا مرض فإن نفقته على مولاه .اهـ. قال بعض الفضلاء والذي يظهر ما في البحر وقياسه في المنح على الموصى له. قياس مع الفارق فإن الموصى به يخدم الموصى له لا في مقابلة شيء فلذلك كانت نفقته عليه، أما هذا فإنه يخدم في مقابلة رقبته فكان كالمستأجر تأمل.
His saying: (And if he frees him on condition of his service for a year, and he accepts, he becomes free and must serve him), meaning from his very hour, because emancipation upon something requires acceptance to exist in the session, not the existence of the accepted thing, like other contracts. And he must serve him for the specified period, and what is meant by a year is a year or less or more. Al-Hakim al-Shahid stated that service known among people is restricted by time, because if he freed him on condition of his service without a time period, he becomes free and must return the value of himself, because service is unknown. Similarly, if he said to his slave girl: 'You are free on condition that you serve so-and-so for me,' and she accepted, she becomes free and must return her value. Muhammad said: she returns the value of one month's service; as in al-Dhakhira. And it is reported in al-Zahiriyya from some that if she serves him for his lifetime or her lifetime, nothing is due from her, and if she refuses to serve him for his lifetime or her lifetime, she must work to pay her value. A fatwa was sought regarding a case where he freed him on condition of his service for a specified period, and the slave accepted and became free, and he had a wife and children—what is the ruling on his maintenance and theirs if he has no wealth? For he cannot engage in earning due to serving the master this period. I have seen no transmission on it. It is appropriate that he should engage in earning for the sake of spending on himself and his family until he becomes free from the need to earn, then he serves the master for the specified period, because he is unable to pay the substitute, so it becomes like the case where he freed him for money and he has no ability to pay it—then it is postponed until ease. It is restricted to his freeing him on condition of his service, such as saying to him: 'I have freed you on condition that you serve me,' because if he said: 'If you serve me for such-and-such a period, you are free,' he does not become free until he serves him, because it is suspended on a condition, and the first is an exchange. And they did not explicitly state here that he becomes a permitted slave, because there is no need for it, since service does not require acquisition of wealth, unlike the case of 'If you pay me a thousand, you are free' as we have mentioned. In al-Dhakhira: if he said: 'Serve me for a year and you are free,' he becomes free immediately and nothing is due from him according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: he does not become free except by service, whether he accepts or not. In al-Zahiriyya: if he said to his slave girl in his will: 'If you serve my son and daughter until they become independent, you are free,' then if they are young, she serves them until they mature; if one matures before the other, she serves them both; if they are mature, she serves the daughter until she marries and the son until he obtains the price of a slave girl; when the daughter is married and the son remains, she serves them both; if one of them dies while they are both old or young, the will is void. In Sharh al-Niqaya on the issue: 'If you serve me such-and-such,' if he serves him less than that or gives him money for his service, he does not become free; similarly if he said: 'If you serve me and my children for a year,' then some of the children die, he does not become free. His saying: (And similarly if he said to his slave girl) end—expression of al-Dhakhira: thus a man said to his slave girl: 'You are free on condition that you serve so-and-so for me,' and she accepted, she is free and must return her value because the service is unknown. If he said: 'On condition that you serve so-and-so for a month,' Abu Yusuf said: she returns her value. Muhammad said: she returns the value of one month's service. In it also, from [؟] from Abu Yusuf: a man said to his slave: 'You are free on condition that you serve so-and-so for a year,' then acceptance belongs to so-and-so; if he accepts, he becomes free, and if he does not serve him, the slave returns his value. His saying: (And it is appropriate that he should engage in earning) etc., he approved it in al-Nahr. And he said in al-Minh: it can be said that it is obligatory upon the master during the mentioned period, and he is made like the legatee of service, for maintenance is obligatory upon him even though he does not own the slave, because he is detained due to his service, and detention is the basis in this chapter—its basis is the judge and mufti. If he falls ill, his maintenance should be prescribed from the public treasury, unlike the legatee of service when he falls ill, his maintenance is upon his master. Some virtuous said: what appears is what is in al-Bahr, and his analogy in al-Minh to the legatee is an analogy with a difference, for the legatee serves the legatee not in exchange for anything, therefore his maintenance is upon him. As for this, he serves in exchange for his person, so he is like a hired person—ponder.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of emancipation on condition of service. The author begins by explaining the matn: if a master says to his slave 'you are free on condition that you serve me for a year' and the slave accepts, the slave becomes free immediately from that moment. Acceptance must occur in the same session, similar to other contracts. The slave must serve the entire agreed period, whether it is a year, less, or more. If no period is specified, the service is unknown, so the slave must repay his value. The same applies to a female slave: if freed on condition of serving another, she must pay her value. Imam Muhammad holds she pays only one month's service value. There is a view that if she serves for the lifetime of either party, nothing is due. A fatwa was sought about a freed slave who must serve his master but has a family to support; the commentator suggests he should first earn enough to support them, then serve the master, analogous to a slave freed for money who cannot pay. The text distinguishes between emancipation as an exchange (where acceptance in the session is required) and a conditional freeing (where the condition must be fulfilled). Abu Yusuf differs, requiring actual service for freedom. The passage also covers a case where a master in his will frees a slave girl on condition of serving his children, with details on her service until they are independent. Finally, a discussion on maintenance: some argue the master must provide maintenance during the service period, similar to a legatee of service, but a critic notes the difference—the slave serves in exchange for his freedom, not gratuitously.

Key Terms
عتق على جعل (itq ‘ala ju‘l): Emancipation in exchange for a consideration, such as service or payment.
خدمة (khidmah): Service performed by the slave for the master or a third party as the consideration for emancipation.
قبول في المجلس (qabul fi al-majlis): Acceptance must take place in the same session as the offer, like other exchange contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Immediately upon acceptance
B) After serving one year
C) After serving any part of the year
D) When the master dies

Key Takeaway
Emancipation on service is an exchange contract: acceptance in the session frees the slave immediately, and the service is a binding obligation, analogous to emancipation for money.

Unspecified Service, Third-Party Beneficiaries, and Maintenance Post-Emancipation
Commentary on variant cases of emancipation on service.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when service is unspecified or for a third party, and identify the positions of Abu Hanifa and his students on the timing of freedom and the slave's obligations.

Core Idea
Unspecified service leads to payment of value; service for a third party requires the third party's acceptance.

This lesson delves into the variants of emancipation on service. We examine what happens when the period is not specified, when the service is to be performed for a third party, and the practical question of the freed slave's maintenance obligations toward his family during the service period. The passage provides detailed rulings and a notable intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the timing of freedom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for unspecified service
If the master does not specify a time period, the service is unknown (gharar). In that case, what does the slave owe? The passage states the slave must pay his value.
This is based on al-Hakim al-Shahid's statement.
2
Analyze service to a third party
If the master frees the slave on condition of serving someone else, who must accept? The passage indicates that acceptance belongs to that third party. If the third party accepts, the slave is free and must serve; if not, the slave pays value.
Consider the scenario where the third party is a beneficiary of the service.
3
Examine the fatwa on maintenance
The passage discusses a fatwa: a freed slave must serve his master for a period but has a family to support. The commentator suggests he should earn for his family first, then serve, akin to the slave freed for money who cannot pay.
This is a practical application of the principle of 'postponement until ease'.
4
Understand the will case
The passage includes a scenario from a will: a female slave serves the testator's children until they are independent. Details on her obligations and termination are given.
This shows how the ruling extends to testamentary dispositions.

His saying: (And if he frees him on condition of his service for a year, and he accepts, he becomes free and must serve him), meaning from his very hour, because emancipation upon something requires acceptance to exist in the session, not the existence of the accepted thing, like other contracts. Death of Master or Slave Before Service Completion: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on the consequences when either the master or the slave dies before the service period ends

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, Muhammad b. al-Hasan, and 'Isa b. Aban regarding compensation when service is interrupted by death, and state the mufta bihi according to al-Hawi al-Qudsi.

Core Idea
Service is a personal utility, not an inheritable property — thus death of the master releases the slave from personal service but demands compensation from his estate.

When a slave is obligated to serve for a period (e.g., as part of a kitaba or emancipation contract), the death of either party before completion raises a key question: does the obligation transfer to heirs or convert to monetary compensation? The Hanafi masters disagree on this point, and their reasoning reveals a deeper usul distinction between debts of property and debts of utility. In this lesson, we explore the intra-madhab dispute and the authority that settles it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Read the passage and identify the core scenario: the master or slave dies before the service period agreed upon (e.g., four years of service after emancipation) is completed.
The service is a contractual obligation, often part of a mu‘amalah like al-kitabah or al-‘itq ‘ala mal.
2
State the Majority Position (Two Companions)
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two companions), the full market value of the slave is due upon death of either party. This is the zahir al-riwaya position.
They equate master's death and slave's death.
3
Present Muhammad's Alternative
Imam Muhammad holds that only the value of the remaining service period is due, not the full slave value.
This is stated in the text as 'value of the service for the period'.
4
Introduce 'Isa's Objection
'Isa b. Aban criticizes the equality of master's and slave's death when the master dies. He argues that service is a debt (dayn) that should be inherited by the heirs, so the slave should serve them.
He draws an analogy to a monetary debt where partial payment was made.
5
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The majority (zahir al-riwaya) rejects 'Isa's analogy because service is a utility (manfa‘a), not a stable property. Utility varies with the persons involved (e.g., poor vs. rich, old vs. young, one vs. many), so it cannot be precisely inherited. Hence monetary compensation is the appropriate remedy.
The text gives specific examples of variation.
6
Determine the Mufta Bihi
According to al-Hawi al-Qudsi, the relied-upon position is that of Imam Muhammad: the value of the remaining service is due. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
Even though the majority (two companions) is in the zahir al-riwaya, later preference leans towards Muhammad's more proportional view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فلو مات تجب قيمته أي لو مات المولى أو العبد قبل الخدمة وجبت قيمة العبد عليه عندهما. وقال محمد عليه قيمة الخدمة في المدة وقد قدمناه فيما إذا أعتقه على مال فاستحق وسووا بين موت المولى وموت العبد وقد طعن عيسى وقال : هذا غلط فيما إذا مات المولى بل يخدم الورثة ما بقي منها لأن الخدمة دين فيخلفه وارثه فيه بعد موته كما لو أعتقه على ألف درهم فاستوفى بعضها ومات ولكن في ظاهر الرواية لا فرق بينهما لأن الخدمة عبارة عن المنفعة وهي لا تورث فلا يمكن إبقاء عين المنفعة بعد موت المولى أو لأن الناس يتفاوتون فيها فإن خدمة الفقراء أسهل من غيرهم وخدمة الشيخ ليست كخدمة الشاب، وقد تكون الورثة كثيرين وخدمة الواحد أسهل من خدمة الجماعة. وقيدنا بموته قبل الخدمة لأنه لو خدمه بعض المدة كسنة من أربع سنين ثم مات فعلى قولهما عليه ثلاثة أرباع قيمته، وعلى قول محمد عليه قيمة خدمته ثلاث سنين ؛ كذا في شرح الطحاوي. وفي الحاوي القدسي: وبقول محمد نأخذ ولو أو حكم ما إذا مرض العبد مرضاً لا يمكن معه الخدمة وينبغي أن يكون كالموت .
His saying: (If he dies, his value is obligatory), meaning if the master or the slave dies before the service, the value of the slave becomes obligatory upon him according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Muhammad said: upon him is the value of the service for the period. And we have presented it earlier regarding the case where he freed him for money and it was invalidated. And they equated the death of the master and the death of the slave. 'Isa objected and said: This is a mistake in the case of the master's death; rather, the slave should serve the heirs for the remainder, because service is a debt, so the heir inherits it after his death, just as if he freed him for a thousand dirhams and some were collected and then he died. But in the apparent transmission, there is no difference between them, because service is an expression of utility, and it is not inherited, so it is not possible to preserve the very utility after the master's death; or because people differ in it, for service of the poor is easier than that of others, and service of an old person is not like service of a young one, and the heirs may be many, and service of one is easier than service of a group. And we restrict it to his death before service, because if he served part of the period, such as one year out of four, then died, according to them (the two) he owes three-quarters of his value, and according to Muhammad he owes the value of the service for three years; as in Sharh al-Tahawi. And in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: we take by the saying of Muhammad; and if it is judged that the slave is ill with an illness that prevents service, it should be like death.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where either the master or the slave dies before the service period is completed. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the full value of the slave is due from the estate or the slave (depending on who died). Muhammad holds that only the value of the remaining service is due. The author notes that 'Isa criticized the view that treats master's and slave's death equally; he argued that if the master dies, the slave should serve the heirs for the remaining period, because service is a debt that can be inherited. However, the majority (zahir al-riwaya) rejects this because service is a personal utility that varies among people and cannot be precisely inherited. If the slave dies after serving part of the period, compensation is proportional. In al-Hawi al-Qudsi, Muhammad's view is taken. Illness that prevents service is analogized to death.

Key Terms
خدمة دين (khidmah dayn): Service considered as a debt owed by the slave, which upon death must be compensated monetarily.
قيمة الخدمة (qimat al-khidmah): Monetary value of the remaining service period, as held by Imam Muhammad.
منفعة (manfa‘ah): Utility; the benefit derived from service, which is personal and not inheritable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a slave is freed on condition of serving the master for four years, and the master dies after one year of service, what do Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions) say the slave owes?
A) Three-quarters of the slave's value
B) Value of three years' service
C) Nothing
D) Service to the heirs for three years

Key Takeaway
When service is interrupted by death, the Hanafi school prefers proportional monetary compensation over inheriting the service itself, because utility (manfa‘a) is personal and not inheritable.
