Third Party Offer to Free Slave Girl on Condition of Marriage: Emancipation Free of Charge
Ruling on void condition in third-party emancipation offer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a third party offers to pay for a slave girl's emancipation on condition of marriage, and explain why the condition is void.

Core Idea
The condition to pay a substitute for emancipation cannot be imposed on a third party; the slave becomes free for free.

This passage examines a scenario where a third party intervenes in a slave's emancipation, offering payment conditional on marriage. The Hanafi school rules that the emancipation stands alone; the condition is invalid because only the one who benefits from freedom (the slave) can be obligated to pay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Note the scenario: a third party commands the master to free a slave girl for a specified sum on condition that the master marries her to him. The master obeys, but the girl refuses marriage. The ruling: she becomes free without any payment.
2
Understand why the condition is void
The condition requiring the third party to pay the substitute for emancipation is invalid because the third party does not receive the benefit of freedom. The substitute for emancipation is only obligatory on the one who gains the legal capacity (quwwa hukmiyya) from it, i.e., the slave.
Analogous to khul‘ but with a key difference: in khul‘ the third party can be a proxy for the wife, but here the slave herself gains capacity.
3
Analyze the dalil: qiyas and distinction
The reasoning relies on qiyas to khul‘ (divorce for compensation) and its distinction. In khul‘, the third party can pay because the wife does not own the right to divorce; here, the slave immediately acquires legal capacity upon emancipation, so the substitute must be from her.
4
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the emancipation is valid and the condition is void. She is free without any payment due from anyone.
This is consistent with the principle that substitutes for emancipation are due only from the one who receives the countervalue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو قال أعتقها بألف على أن تزوجنيها ففعل وأبت أن تتزوجه عتقت مجاناً) أي لو قال أجنبي لمالك جارية إلى آخره، وحاصله أمره المخاطب بإعتاق أمته وتزويجها منه على عوض معين مشروط على الأجنبي عن الأمة وعن مهرها فلما لم تتزوجه بطلت عنه حصة المهر عنها وأما حصة العتق فباطلة أيضاً إذ لا يصح اشتراط بدل العتق على الأجنبي بخلاف الخلع لأن الأجنبي فيه كالمرأة لم يحصل لها ملك ما لم تكن تملكه بخلاف العتق فإنه يثبت للعبد فيه قوة حكمية هي ملك البيع والشراء والإجارة والتزويج وغيره ذلك، ولا يجب العوض إلا على من حصل له المعوض فمعنى قوله مجاناً أنها تعتق بغير شيء يلزمها أو يلزم الأمر أي لا يلزم أحداً شيء وأطلق فشمل ما إذا قال بألف علي أو لم يقل علي وكان الأولى ذكرها كما في بعض نسخ الهداية ليفيد عدم الوجوب عند عدم ذكرها بالأولى. وأفاد بقوله . واجبة عليه وإن لم يكن له ملك الرقبة لكونه محبوساً بخدمته والحبس هو الأصل في هذا الباب أصله القاضي والمفتي، فإن مرض فينبغي أن تفرض نفقته في بيت المال بخلاف الموصى بخدمته إذا مرض فإن نفقته على مولاه .اهـ. قال بعض الفضلاء والذي يظهر ما في البحر وقياسه في المنح على الموصى له. قياس مع الفارق فإن الموصى به يخدم الموصى له لا في مقابلة شيء فلذلك كانت نفقته عليه، أما هذا فإنه يخدم في مقابلة رقبته فكان كالمستأجر تأمل.
His saying: (And if he said: 'Free her for a thousand on condition that you marry her to me,' and he did so, and she refused to marry him, she becomes free for free) meaning if a third party said to the owner of a slave girl, etc. Its summary: he commanded the addressee to free his slave girl and marry her to him for a specified consideration conditioned upon the third party on behalf of the slave girl and her dower. When she did not marry him, the share of the dower fell away from him, and the share of emancipation is also invalid, because it is not valid to stipulate the substitute for emancipation upon a third party, unlike khul‘, because the third party therein is like the woman—she does not acquire ownership unless she owns it. Unlike emancipation, for the slave acquires a legal capacity (quwwa hukmiyya) which is the right to sell, buy, hire, marry, etc. And the substitute is only obligatory upon the one who receives the compensation. So the meaning of 'for free' is that she becomes free without anything being owed by her or by the commander—i.e., nothing is owed by anyone. And it is general, including whether he said 'for a thousand upon me' or did not say 'upon me,' though it was better to mention it as in some copies of al-Hidayah to indicate that when not mentioned, it is all the more not obligatory. And he added by his saying: 'Obligatory upon him even though he does not own the slave, because he is detained due to his service, and detention is the basis in this chapter—its basis is the judge and mufti. If he falls ill, his maintenance should be prescribed from the public treasury, unlike the legatee of service when he falls ill, his maintenance is upon his master.' Some virtuous said: what appears is what is in al-Bahr, and his analogy in al-Minh to the legatee is an analogy with a difference, for the legatee serves the legatee not in exchange for anything, therefore his maintenance is upon him. As for this, he serves in exchange for his person, so he is like a hired person—ponder.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where a third party (ajnabi) tells the master of a slave girl: 'Free her for a thousand dirhams on condition that you marry her to me.' If the master frees her but she refuses to marry the third party, the ruling is that she becomes free without any payment—neither she nor the third party owes anything. The reason is that the condition to pay a substitute for emancipation cannot be imposed on a third party (the third party is not the one receiving the benefit of freedom). Unlike khul‘ (divorce for compensation) where the third party can be a proxy, here the slave herself gains freedom and legal capacity, so the substitute should be from her, not from an outsider. The condition is void; the emancipation is valid unconditionally. The passage also includes a separate discussion on maintenance during service, likely a continuation from earlier, but here it is appended. Some argue that the master must provide maintenance if the slave is detained for service, analogous to a hired worker, not a gratuitous legatee.

Key Terms
عتق مجاناً (itq majanan): Emancipation without any consideration being paid by anyone.
قوة حكمية (quwwa hukmiyya): Legal capacity acquired by the slave upon emancipation, including the ability to own property, marry, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A third party says to a slave owner: 'Free your slave girl for a thousand dirhams and marry her to me.' The owner frees her, but she refuses to marry the third party. What is the ruling?
A) She remains a slave until the thousand is paid
B) She is free, and the third party must pay the thousand
C) She is free for free, with no payment required
D) She must pay the thousand herself

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, an emancipation conditioned on a third party's payment is unconditionally valid; the third party is not liable for the substitute.

Conditional Emancipation with Marriage: Woman Refuses
Ruling with proof: conditional emancipation and marriage refusal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a slave refuses marriage after conditional emancipation and explain the reasoning (talil) behind the gratuitous emancipation.

Core Idea
In conditional emancipation with a marriage stipulation, the condition is void upon the slave's refusal; she is freed gratis because consideration can only come from the one who obtains the benefit.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a scenario where a third party offers to pay for a slave girl's emancipation on condition that the owner marries her to him. The key legal question is: what happens if the slave girl refuses? The Hanafi ruling is clear: she goes free without any payment, and no one owes anything. This lesson unpacks the reasoning (talil) behind this ruling, highlighting the distinction from khul' and the concept of quwwa hukmiyya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and parties
A third party (ajnabi) says to the slave owner: 'Emancipate your slave girl for a thousand dirhams on condition that you marry her to me.' The owner complies, but the slave girl refuses to marry the third party.
The third party is not the owner and has no direct claim on the slave.
2
Separate the two components
The transaction has two parts: (1) emancipation for a price, and (2) a condition of marriage. The Hanafi analysis treats the condition as separate from the emancipation contract.
The stipulation of marriage is not inherent to emancipation.
3
Determine validity of the condition
It is not valid to stipulate the consideration for emancipation upon a stranger (the third party) because the third party is not the one who receives the compensated thing (the slave's freedom). In emancipation, the slave acquires a legal capacity (quwwa hukmiyya) – the slave becomes the direct beneficiary.
Contrast with khul': in khul', a stranger can be treated like the wife.
4
Apply the ruling
Since the condition is void ab initio, the emancipation itself stands, but no payment is owed by anyone. The phrase 'gratuitously' (majjānan) means the slave is freed without any liability on the third party, the owner, or the slave.
This applies whether or not the third party said 'upon me'.
5
Contrast with similar cases
The passage also cites examples from al-Muhit involving a female owner and male slave. If the slave refuses marriage after accepting the condition, he may owe value; if the owner refuses, the slave is free without payment. This reinforces that the party who breaches the condition bears the loss.
The principles are consistent: the stipulation is void if the marriage condition fails due to the slave's refusal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو قال أعتقها بألف على أن تزوجنيها ففعل وأبت أن تتزوجه عتقت مجاناً) أي لو قال أجنبي لمالك جارية إلى آخره، وحاصله أمره المخاطب بإعتاق أمته وتزويجها منه على عوض معين مشروط على الأجنبي عن الأمة وعن مهرها فلما لم تتزوجه بطلت عنه حصة المهر عنها وأما حصة العتق فباطلة أيضاً إذ لا يصح اشتراط بدل العتق على الأجنبي بخلاف الخلع لأن الأجنبي فيه كالمرأة لم يحصل لها ملك ما لم تكن تملكه بخلاف العتق فإنه يثبت للعبد فيه قوة حكمية هي ملك البيع والشراء والإجارة والتزويج وغيره ذلك، ولا يجب العوض إلا على من حصل له المعوض فمعنى قوله مجاناً أنها تعتق بغير شيء يلزمها أو يلزم الأمر أي لا يلزم أحداً شيء وأطلق فشمل ما إذا قال بألف علي أو لم يقل علي وكان الأولى ذكرها كما في بعض نسخ الهداية ليفيد عدم الوجوب عند عدم ذكرها بالأولى. وأفاد بقوله . وفي المحيط : لو قالت العبدها أعتقتك على ألف على أن تتزوجني على عشرة فقبل ذلك ثم أبى أن يتزوجها فعليه الألف، فإن كانت قيمته أكثر من الألف في تمام القيمة لأنه لم يف، وإن قالت أعتقتك سعی علي أن تتزوجني وتمهرني ألفاً، فقيل ثم أبى ذلك عتق وعليه أن يسعى في قيمته، وإن تزوجها على مائة ورضيت بذلك فلا سعاية عليه لأنه وفى لها بالتزوج وهي رضيت بدون ما شرطت عليه من المهر، ولو دعاها العبد على أن يتزوجها على ألف فأبت المرأة فلا سعاية عليه لأنه قد وفى لها بما شرطت عليه فجاء الامتناع من قبلها ا هـ .
His statement: (And if he said: 'Emancipate her for a thousand on condition that you marry her to me,' and he did that, and she refused to marry him, she is emancipated gratuitously.) That is, if a stranger said to the owner of a slave girl, etc. The summary: he commanded the addressee to emancipate his slave girl and marry her to him for a specified consideration conditioned upon the stranger on behalf of the slave girl and her dower. So when she did not marry him, the share of the dower from him is void; and as for the share of emancipation, it is also void because it is not valid to stipulate the consideration for emancipation upon a stranger, unlike khul' because the stranger in it is like the woman, not having acquired ownership of what he does not own. Unlike emancipation, for the slave acquires a legal capacity (quwwa hukmiyya) being ownership of selling, buying, leasing, marrying, etc. And the consideration is only due to the one who obtains the compensated thing. So the meaning of 'gratuitously' is that she is emancipated without anything being incumbent upon her or upon the commander, i.e., nothing is incumbent upon anyone. And it is general, including whether he said 'for a thousand upon me' or did not say 'upon me,' and it would have been better to mention it as in some copies of al-Hidayah to indicate the absence of obligation when not mentioned a fortiori. And he added with his statement... And in al-Muhit: If the owner said to her slave: 'I emancipated you for a thousand on condition that you marry me for ten,' and he accepted, then he refused to marry her, then the thousand is due from him. If his value is more than the thousand, the full value is due because he did not fulfill. And if she said: 'I emancipated you on condition that you marry me and give me a thousand as dower,' and he agreed, then he refused, he is emancipated and must work to earn his value. And if he married her for a hundred and she was pleased with that, then no earning is required because he fulfilled the marriage and she was satisfied with less than the stipulated dower. And if the slave invited her to marry him for a thousand and she refused, then no earning is required because he fulfilled what she stipulated, and the refusal came from her.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with reasoning. It addresses a scenario where a third party (ajnabi) says to the owner of a slave girl: 'Emancipate her for a thousand dirhams on condition that you marry her to me.' The owner does so, but the slave girl refuses to marry the third party. The ruling: she is emancipated gratuitously (free of any payment). The reason given is that the condition to marry is void ab initio because it is not permissible to stipulate the consideration for emancipation upon a stranger (the third party). The third party is not the one receiving the 'iwad (compensated thing) – that is the slave girl. In emancipation, the slave acquires a legal capacity (quwwa hukmiyya) such as the ability to own and transact. The consideration is due only from the one who obtains the compensated thing. Since the third party does not obtain the slave (she is already emancipated), no payment is due from him. The term 'gratuitously' means nothing is payable by anyone. This applies whether the third party said 'upon me' or not, though mentioning it reinforces the ruling. The passage also includes examples from al-Muhit involving a female owner and male slave, where similar logic applies: if the stipulated marriage is not fulfilled, the slave may owe value or may be free depending on who breached the condition.

Key Terms
مجاناً (majjānan): Free of charge; no payment is owed by anyone
قوة حكمية (quwwa hukmiyya): Legal capacity acquired by the slave upon emancipation, i.e., the ability to own and transact

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The third party must pay the thousand dirhams.
B) The slave girl must pay the thousand dirhams.
C) The slave girl is emancipated free and no one pays anything.
D) The owner must refund the third party.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, if a third party stipulates marriage as a condition for emancipation and the slave refuses, the emancipation stands but no payment is due from anyone.

Division of Consideration When 'Ani Is Added
A ruling on dividing consideration in a conditional emancipation transaction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of proportional apportionment when a conditional emancipation transaction includes a marriage condition and the third party says 'for me.'

Core Idea
The thousand is split by value and mahr; only the value portion is due when marriage fails.

This passage extends our understanding of conditional emancipation transactions. When the third party adds 'for me,' the transaction implicitly includes a purchase. The total consideration is apportioned between the slave's market value and the standard dower. If the marriage condition fails, only the value portion is paid. Learn how the Hanafi school harmonizes sale and marriage stipulations in the context of emancipation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Transaction Type
Recognize the scenario: a conditional emancipation where the third party says 'for me' and attaches a marriage condition.
The word 'عني' transforms the transaction from a simple gift of emancipation to an implied purchase.
2
Understand the Apportionment Rule
The total consideration (1,000 dirhams) is divided proportionally between the slave's value (qīmah) and the standard dower (mahr al-mithl).
3
Determine What Is Due
Only the portion corresponding to the value is paid by the third party; the dower portion is dropped because the marriage did not occur.
The marriage benefits are compensable but not realized; hence the dower share is forgiven.
4
Analyze the Legal Rationale
Why is the sale valid despite the marriage condition? Because the condition supports emancipation, so the less strict conditions of emancipation apply, not those of sale.
The commander must have capacity for emancipation (ahliyyat al-i'tāq).
5
Contrast with the 'For Nothing' Case
Note the intra-Hanafi difference: when the third party says 'for nothing,' delivery (qabd) is required according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf.
This highlights how the presence of consideration changes the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو زاد عني قسم الألف على قيمتها ومهر مثلها ويجب ما أصاب القيمة فقط) أي لو قال أعتقها عني بألف درهم على أن تزوجنيها فأبت أن تتزوجه قسمت الألف على قيمتها وعلى مهر مثلها، فما أصاب القيمة أداه الآمر للمأمور، وما أصاب المهر سقط عنه لأنه لما قال «عني» تضمن الشراء اقتضاء على ما عرف في الأصول والفروع لكن ضم إلى رقبتها تزويجها وقابل المجموع بعوض هو ألف فانقسمت عليها بالحصة ومنافع البضع وإن لم تكن مالاً لكن أخذت حكم المال لأنها متقومة حالة الدخول وإيراد العقد عليها ولم يبطل البيع باشتراط النكاح لأنه مقتضى لصحة العتق فلا يراعى فيه شرائط البيع بل شرائط العتق وهو المقتضي - بالكسر - حتى يعتبر في الأمر أهلية الإعتاق بخلاف ما إذا قال اعتق عبدك عني بغير شيء فأعتقه حيث لا يسقط القبض عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف، وقد قدمناه قبيل نكاح الكافر. وفي الولوالجية: رجل قال جاريتي هذه لك على أن تعتق عني عبدك فلاناً فرضي بذلك ودفع الجارية إليه لا تكون له حتى يعتبر عبده لأنه طلب منه تمليك العبد يقتضي قوله : (لأنه طلب منه تمليك العبد مقتضى الاعتاق الخ) مقتضى يدل من تمليك وهو بضم الميم الضاد اسم مفعول كما رأيته في الولوالجية والذي في النسخ يقتضي بصيغة المضارع وهو تحريف. وقوله بتمليك الجارية متعلق بطلب .
His statement: (And if he added 'for me,' the thousand is divided between her value and her like dower, and only what corresponds to the value is due.) That is, if he said: 'Emancipate her for me for a thousand dirhams on condition that you marry her to me,' and she refused to marry him, the thousand is divided between her value and her like dower. What corresponds to the value, the commander pays to the commandee, and what corresponds to the dower is dropped from him. Because when he said 'for me,' it implicitly includes purchase as is known in principles and branches. But he combined her emancipation with her marriage and set the total against a consideration of a thousand, so it is divided proportionally. And the benefits of intercourse, even though not property, take the ruling of property because they are compensable upon consummation and the contract is made upon them. And the sale is not invalidated by stipulating marriage because it is a requirement for the validity of emancipation; so the conditions of sale are not considered, but rather the conditions of emancipation, which require capacity for emancipation in the commander. Unlike if he said 'emancipate your slave for me for nothing' and he emancipated him, where the delivery is not dropped according to the two, contrary to Abu Yusuf. And we have already presented this before the chapter on marriage of a disbeliever. And in al-Walwaljiyya: A man said: 'This slave girl of mine is for you on condition that you emancipate your slave so-and-so for me,' and he agreed and gave the slave girl to him. It is not his until he emancipates his slave. Because he sought from him the ownership of the slave requiring... His statement: 'because he sought from him the ownership of the slave, the requirement of emancipation etc.' 'Requirement' indicates from 'tamlik' (making owner), and it is a passive participle as I saw in al-Walwaljiyya, and in the copies it is 'yaqtadi' in the present tense, which is a corruption. And his statement 'with the ownership of the slave girl' is related to 'sought'.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage elaborates on a variant of the previous scenario where the third party adds the word 'for me' (عني). This changes the nature of the transaction: it now implicitly includes an element of purchase (the master sells the slave girl to the third party for a price). However, because the condition of marriage is attached, the total consideration of one thousand dirhams is apportioned between the value of the slave girl and the mahr of her like (mahr al-mithl). The third party (the commander) must pay to the master the portion corresponding to the slave's value, but the portion corresponding to the dower is dropped because the marriage did not occur (she refused). The reasoning is that the benefits of marriage (manafi' al-bid') are treated as compensable even though not strictly property. The transaction is considered valid because the stipulation of marriage does not invalidate the sale; rather, it is a requirement for the validity of emancipation, so the conditions of emancipation (like capacity for emancipation) govern, not the strict conditions of sale. The passage also contrasts with a case where a third party says 'emancipate your slave for me for nothing' - according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the delivery (qabd) is not dropped (i.e., the slave must be delivered to the third party to complete the gift), unlike Abu Yusuf's view. Finally, a case from al-Walwaljiyya illustrates a similar principle: a man gives a slave girl in exchange for the emancipation of another's slave; ownership transfers only upon fulfillment of the condition.

Key Terms
مهر مثلها (mahr mithlihā): The standard dower of a woman of her status
البيع باشتراط النكاح (al-bay‘ bi-ishtirāṭ al-nikāḥ): A sale combined with a condition of marriage

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The full thousand dirhams.
B) Only the portion corresponding to the slave's value.
C) Only the portion corresponding to the mahr.
D) Nothing at all.

Key Takeaway
In a conditional emancipation with 'for me,' the consideration is apportioned between value and dower; only the value is payable if the marriage fails.

Manumission with Marriage Condition: Payment Division
Dividing payment between value and mahr when marriage is refused.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of dividing a conditional payment (ju'l) proportionally between the slave's value and the woman's mahr.

Core Idea
The payment is divided: the portion for value is dropped, the portion for mahr is owed.

This lesson unpacks a key ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: when a man frees a woman on condition that she marries him, and she refuses, the payment he offered is not forfeited entirely but is split. Understanding this division requires distinguishing the two components embedded in the payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the condition
The scenario: a man (the commander) says to another (the agent) 'Free her (the slave) for me for 1000 dirhams on condition that you marry her to me.' The agent frees her, but she refuses to marry.
The manumission is valid immediately; the condition of marriage is separate.
2
Understand the dual nature of the payment
The payment of 1000 is a single sum that implicitly covers two things: the slave's value (qimah) as a consideration for freeing, and her mahr (dower) for the marriage. Because the marriage does not occur, the portion intended as mahr is still owed (she lost the marriage benefit), but the portion for value is dropped (she is free without payment).
The text calls this a 'divided' payment proportionally.
3
Apply the proportion formula
Take the slave's value (e.g., 200) and her mahr mithl (e.g., 100). Total = 300. The 1000 is divided as 1000 * (value / total) for value, and 1000 * (mahr / total) for mahr. The value portion is dropped; the mahr portion is owed.
If value = mahr, half is dropped and half owed. If value is double mahr, two-thirds dropped and one-third owed.
4
Distinguish from the case where she marries
If she agrees to marry, the entire 1000 becomes her mahr. The division is only relevant when the marriage fails.
The author's phrase 'and she refuses' is crucial to trigger the division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤٠ كتاب العتق باب العتق على جعل أن تتزوجنه عتقت مجاناً ولو زاد عني قسم الألف على قيمتها ومهر مثلها ويجب ما أصاب القيمة فقط . «وأبت أن لها الامتناع من تزوجه لأنها ملكت نفسها بالعتق وقيد بإبائها لأنها لو تزوجته قسمت الألف على قيمتها ومهر مثلها فما أصاب قيمتها سقط عنه لما ذكرناه. وما أصاب مهرها وجب لها عليه فإن استويا بأن كان قيمتها مائة ومهرها مائة سقط عنه خمسمائة ووجب لها خمسمائة عليه وإن تفاوتاً كأن كان قيمتها مائتين والمهر مائة سقط عنه ستمائة وستة وستون وثلثان ووجب لها ثلثمائة وثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وبهذا علم أن المصنف لو حذف قوله «وأبت» لكان أولى لأنها تعتق مجاناً، سواء أبت أو تزوجته، وأما وجوب المهر فشيء آخر. وكذا قوله على أن تزوجنيها» ليس بقيد لأنها تعتق مجاناً لو قال أعتقها بالألف علي ففعل لكن إنما ذكره ليفرع عليه المسألة الثانية. وفي المحيط : لو قالت العبدها أعتقتك على ألف على أن تتزوجني على عشرة فقبل ذلك ثم أبى أن يتزوجها فعليه الألف، فإن كانت قيمته أكثر من الألف في تمام القيمة لأنه لم يف، وإن قالت أعتقتك سعي علي أن تتزوجني وتمهرني ألفاً، فقيل ثم أبى ذلك عتق وعليه أن يسعى في قيمته، وإن تزوجها على مائة ورضيت بذلك فلا سعاية عليه لأنه وفى لها بالتزوج وهي رضيت بدون ما شرطت عليه من المهر، ولو دعاها العبد على أن يتزوجها على ألف فأبت المرأة فلا سعاية عليه لأنه قد وفى لها بما شرطت عليه فجاء الامتناع من قبلها ا هـ .
قوله : (ولو زاد عني قسم الألف على قيمتها ومهر مثلها ويجب ما أصاب القيمة فقط) أي لو قال أعتقها عني بألف درهم على أن تزوجنيها فأبت أن تتزوجه قسمت الألف على قيمتها وعلى مهر مثلها، فما أصاب القيمة أداه الآمر للمأمور، وما أصاب المهر سقط عنه لأنه لما قال «عني تضمن الشراء اقتضاء على ما عرف في الأصول والفروع لكن ضم إلى رقبتها تزويجها وقابل المجموع بعوض هو ألف فانقسمت عليها بالحصة ومنافع البضع وإن لم تكن مالاً لكن أخذت حكم المال لأنها متقومة حالة الدخول وإيراد العقد عليها ولم يبطل البيع باشتراط النكاح لأنه مقتضى لصحة العتق فلا يراعى فيه شرائط البيع بل شرائط العتق وهو المقتضي - بالكسر - حتى يعتبر في الأمر أهلية الإعتاق بخلاف ما إذا قال اعتق عبدك عني بغير شيء فأعتقه حيث لا يسقط القبض عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف، وقد قدمناه قبيل نكاح الكافر. وفي الولوالجية: رجل قال جاريتي هذه لك على أن تعتق عني عبدك فلاناً فرضي بذلك ودفع الجارية إليه لا تكون له حتى يعتبر عبده لأنه طلب منه تمليك العبد يقتضي
قوله : (لأنه طلب منه تمليك العبد مقتضى الاعتاق الخ) مقتضى يدل من تمليك وهو بضم الميم الضاد اسم مفعول كما رأيته في الولوالجية والذي في النسخ يقتضي بصيغة المضارع وهو تحريف. وقوله بتمليك الجارية متعلق بطلب .
وفتح
الإعتاق بتمليك الجارية فما لم يعتق لم يوجد تمليك العبد فلا يتملك الجارية ا هـ . وقيد بإبائها في الثانية أيضاً لأنها لو تزوجته فما أصاب قيمتها فهو للمولى وما أصاب مهر مثلها كان مهراً لها. وقيد المصنف باشتراط التزوج من الأجنبي لأنه لو أعتق أمته على أن تزوجه نفسها فزوجته نفسها كان لها مهر مثلها عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن العتق ليس بمال فلا يصلح مهراً، وعند أبي يوسف يجوز جعل العتق صداقاً لأنه لا أعتق صفية ونكحها وجعل عتقها مهرها . قلنا : كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مخصوصاً بالنكاح بغير مهر فإن أبت أن تتزوجه فعليها قيمتها في قولهم جميعاً. وفي الخانية : أم الولد إذا أعتقها مولاها على أن تزوج نفسها منه فقبلت عتقت فإن أبت أن تزوج نفسها منه لا سعاية عليها والله أعلم.
40 Kitab al-Itq, Bab al-Itq 'ala Ju'l: If you marry him, she is freed gratuitously. And if he exceeds me, the thousand is divided between her value and her like mahr, and only what hits the value is owed. 'And she refuses': she has the right to refrain from marrying him because she owns herself by the manumission. It is qualified by her refusal because if she married him, the thousand would be divided between her value and her mahr; what hits her value is dropped from him for what we mentioned, and what hits her mahr is owed to her. If they are equal, e.g., her value is 100 and her mahr 100, 500 falls from him and 500 is owed to her. If they differ, e.g., her value is 200 and mahr 100, 666 and 2/3 falls from him and 333 and 1/3 is owed to her. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. By this it is known that if the author had omitted his saying 'and she refuses' it would be better because she is freed gratuitously whether she refuses or marries him; the obligation of mahr is something else. Similarly his saying 'on the condition that you marry me' is not a restriction because she would be freed gratuitously if he said 'I free her for 1000 on me' and he did so, but he mentioned it only to branch the second issue. In al-Muhit: If a woman says to her slave 'I free you for 1000 on condition that you marry me for 10' and he accepts, then refuses to marry her, he owes the 1000, and if his value is more than 1000, he owes the full value because he did not fulfill. If she said 'I free you on a payment that you marry me and give me 1000 mahr' and he then refuses, he is free and must earn his value; if he marries her for 100 and she is pleased, no earning on him because he fulfilled marriage and she was pleased with less than what she stipulated. If the slave calls her to marry him for 1000 and she refuses, no earning on him because he fulfilled what she stipulated and the refusal came from her. End. His saying: (And if he exceeds me, the thousand is divided between her value and her like mahr, and only what hits the value is owed) means: If he said 'Free her for me for 1000 dirhams on condition that you marry her to me' and she refuses to marry him, the thousand is divided between her value and her like mahr. What hits the value the commander pays to the commanded; what hits the mahr is dropped from him because when he said 'for me' it implies purchase by acquisition as known in usul and furu', but he attached to her neck her marriage and confronted the total with a consideration of 1000, so it is divided between them by share. The usufructs of the vulva, though not property, take the ruling of property because they are valued at the time of entry and the contract is entered upon them. The sale is not invalidated by stipulating marriage because it is a requirement for the validity of manumission, so conditions of sale are not considered but rather conditions of manumission. Thus the commander's eligibility for manumission is considered, unlike if he said 'Free your slave for me without anything' and he frees him, where the handover is not dropped according to the two, contrary to Abu Yusuf, and we have mentioned it before the marriage of the disbeliever. In al-Walwaljiah: A man said 'This slave-girl of mine is yours on condition that you free your slave so-and-so for me' and he agreed and gave the slave-girl, it is not owned by him until he frees his slave because he requested from him the transfer of ownership of the slave requires... His saying: (because he requested from him the transfer of ownership of the slave, requirement of manumission etc.) The requirement indicates from transfer, with dammah on the mim and consonant daad, passive participle as I saw in al-Walwaljiah, and in the copies 'requires' in the present tense, which is a corruption. His saying 'by transferring the slave-girl' is attached to 'request'. Fath. The manumission by transferring the slave-girl: as long as he does not free, the transfer of ownership of the slave does not occur, so he does not own the slave-girl. End. And it is qualified by her refusal in the second also because if she married him, what hits her value is for the master and what hits her like mahr is mahr for her. The author qualified it by stipulating marriage from a stranger because if he freed his own female slave on condition that she marry him and she married him, she has her like mahr according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because manumission is not property so it is not valid as mahr, and according to Abu Yusuf it is permissible to make manumission as dower because the Prophet freed Safiyyah and married her and made her manumission her mahr. We say: The Prophet was specified for marriage without mahr. If she refuses to marry him, she owes her value in the opinion of all of them. In al-Khaniyyah: If the master of an umm walad frees her on condition that she marry herself to him and she accepts, she is free; if she refuses to marry herself to him, no earning is on her. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the chapter on manumission upon a payment (ju'l), specifically when a condition of marriage is attached. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq comments on the matn (base text) of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The passage begins by stating a central ruling: If a woman frees her slave on condition that he marries her (for a specified amount), the act of manumission is valid and the slave is free immediately, regardless of whether the marriage occurs. The payment (e.g., 1000 dirhams) is not a price for freedom but is divided proportionally between the slave's market value (qimah) and the like mahr (mahr mithl) of the woman. This division occurs only if the woman refuses to marry; if she marries, the whole amount is treated as mahr. The commentary then provides numerical examples: if value and mahr are equal (100 each), half of the 1000 (500) is dropped and half owed; if value is 200 and mahr 100, the proportion is 2:1, so two-thirds of 1000 (666.67) is dropped and one-third (333.33) owed. The text then critically notes that the author's phrase 'and she refuses' is unnecessary because the woman is free regardless, but it serves to introduce the second case where a third party (an outsider) is involved. The third-party case: a man says to another, 'Free my slave for me for 1000 dirhams on condition that you marry her (the slave) to me.' If the woman refuses marriage, the 1000 is divided between her value and her mahr; the fraction hitting value is paid by the commander to the agent, and the fraction hitting mahr is dropped. The reasoning involves an analogy to a conditional sale where the object includes both the slave's value and the benefit of marriage. The text then discusses a dispute (intra-Hanafi) between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other regarding the permissibility of making manumission itself the mahr. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that manumission is not property (mal) and thus cannot serve as mahr, while Abu Yusuf cites the hadith that the Prophet freed Safiyyah and made her manumission her mahr. The Hanafi response is that this was a special prerogative of the Prophet. The passage concludes with a fatwa from al-Khaniyyah regarding umm walad (a slave who bore her master's child).

Key Terms
عتق على جعل (itq 'ala ju'l): Manumission of a slave in exchange for a payment (ju'l), often with an additional condition.
قيمة (qimah): The market value of the slave at the time of manumission.
مهر مثل (mahr mithl): The standard dower for a woman of similar status in her family and community.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a slave woman is freed on condition of marriage, and she refuses, what determines the portion of the payment that is dropped?
A) The slave's age
B) The slave's market value (qimah) relative to her mahr mithl
C) The amount of the payment alone
D) The decision of the agent

Key Takeaway
When a conditional manumission fails due to the woman's refusal, the payment is split into value (dropped) and mahr (owed).
